<p>Enemy might be a supernatural gunslinger who </p>
<p>wants your hero dead.</p>
<p>If the enemy is one day defeated, the GM should </p>
<p>gradually work in a replacement, or the hero may </p>
<p>buy off the Hindrance by sacrificing an Advance.</p>
<p>Greedy.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>Your  miserly  hero  measures  his  worth  in </p>
<p>treasure. If a Minor Hindrance, he argues bitterly </p>
<p>over  any  loot  acquired  during  play.  If  a  Major </p>
<p>Hindrance, he fights over anything he considers </p>
<p>unfair, and may even kill for his “fair share.”</p>
<p>Habit.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>Your warrior has an annoying and constant habit </p>
<p>of some sort. Maybe she picks her nose, says </p>
<p>“y’know” in every sentence, or chews gum like </p>
<p>it’s going out of style.</p>
<p>A Minor Habit irritates those around her but isn’t </p>
<p>dangerous. Your hero suffers a –1 Charisma.</p>
<p>A Major Habit is a physical or mental addiction </p>
<p>of some sort that is debilitating or possibly even </p>
<p>deadly. This includes drug use, chronic drinking, </p>
<p>or  perhaps  even  an  addiction  to  virtual  reality </p>
<p>in a high-tech setting. A character who doesn’t </p>
<p>get his fix must make a Fatigue check every 24 </p>
<p>hours thereafter (see Fatigue on page 99). The </p>
<p>first failed roll makes the character Fatigued, then </p>
<p>Exhausted. The  final  result  is  a  coma  for  hard </p>
<p>drug use, or a bad case of the shakes for things </p>
<p>like alcohol or VR. Medical care may ease the </p>
<p>symptoms. Otherwise the victim must live with the </p>
<p>penalties for 1d6 days. Afterward, the hero must </p>
<p>buy off the Hindrance by sacrificing an opportunity </p>
<p>to Advance  or  he  eventually  falls  back  into  his </p>
<p>dependency.</p>
<p>Hard.of.Hearing.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>Characters who have lost some or all of their </p>
<p>hearing  have  this  disadvantage. As  a  Minor </p>
<p>Hindrance, it subtracts 2 from all Notice rolls made </p>
<p>to hear, including awaking due to loud noises. A </p>
<p>Major Hindrance means the character is deaf. She </p>
<p>cannot hear and automatically fails all Notice rolls </p>
<p>that depend on hearing.</p>
<p>Heroic.(Major)</p>
<p>This noble soul never says no to a person in </p>
<p>need. She doesn’t have to be happy about it, but </p>
<p>she  always  comes  to  the  rescue  of  those  she </p>
<p>feels can’t help themselves. She’s the first one </p>
<p>to run into a burning building, usually agrees to </p>
<p>hunt monsters for little or no pay, and is generally </p>
<p>a pushover for a sob story.</p>
<p>Illiterate.(Minor)</p>
<p>Your hero cannot read. He can probably sign </p>
<p>his  name  and  knows  what  a  STOP  sign  says, </p>
<p>but can do little else. He also doesn’t know much </p>
<p>about math either. He can probably do 2+2=4, but </p>
<p>multiplication and the like are beyond him.</p>
<p>Illiterates can’t read or write in any language, by </p>
<p>the way, no matter how many they actually speak.</p>
<p>Lame.(Major)</p>
<p>A past wound has nearly crippled your hero. His </p>
<p>basic Pace is reduced by 2 and he rolls only a d4 </p>
<p>for running rolls. A character’s Pace may never </p>
<p>be reduced below 1.</p>
<p>Loyal.(Minor)</p>
<p>Your character may not be a hero, but he’d give </p>
<p>his life for his friends. This character can never </p>
<p>leave a man behind if there’s any chance at all </p>
<p>he could help.</p>
<p>Mean.(Minor)</p>
<p>This  fellow  is  ill-tempered  and  disagreeable. </p>
<p>No  one  really  likes  him,  and  he  has  trouble </p>
<p>doing  anything  kind  for  anyone  else.  He  must </p>
<p>be paid for his troubles and doesn’t even accept </p>
<p>awards graciously. Your character suffers –2 to </p>
<p>his Charisma.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--32</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Obese.(Minor)</p>
<p>Particularly  large  people  often  have  great </p>
<p>difficulty in dangerous physical situations. Those </p>
<p>who carry their weight well have the Brawny Edge. </p>
<p>Those who don’t handle it very well are Obese. </p>
<p>A character cannot be both Brawny and Obese.</p>
<p>An Obese hero adds 1 to his Toughness, but </p>
<p>his Pace is decreased by 1 and his running die is </p>
<p>a d4. Obese characters may also have difficulty </p>
<p>finding armor or clothing that fits, squeezing into </p>
<p>tight spaces, or even riding in confined spaces </p>
<p>such as coach airplane seats or compact cars.</p>
<p>One.Arm.(Major)</p>
<p>Whether by birth or battle, your hero has lost </p>
<p>an arm. Fortunately, his other arm is (now) his </p>
<p>“good” one. Tasks that require two hands, such </p>
<p>as Climbing, suffer a –4 modifier.</p>
<p>One.Eye.(Major)</p>
<p>Your  hero  lost  an  eye  for  some  unfortunate </p>
<p>reason. If he doesn’t wear a patch or buy a glass </p>
<p>replacement (typically $500), he suffers –1 to his </p>
<p>Charisma for the grotesque wound.</p>
<p>He  suffers  –2  to  any  Trait  rolls  that  require </p>
<p>depth perception, such as Shooting or Throwing, </p>
<p>jumping a ravine or rooftop, and so on.</p>
<p>One.Leg.(Major)</p>
<p>With  a  prosthetic,  One  Leg  acts  exactly  like </p>
<p>the  Lame  Hindrance,  reducing  Pace  by  2  and </p>
<p>running rolls are now a d4. Without a prosthetic, </p>
<p>the character’s Pace is 2 and he can never run. </p>
<p>He also suffers –2 to Traits that require mobility, </p>
<p>such as Climbing and Fighting. A character with </p>
<p>one leg also suffers a –2 penalty to his Swimming </p>
<p>skill (and Pace).</p>
<p>Outsider.(Minor)</p>
<p>In  a  society  made  up  of  only  a  few  types  of </p>
<p>people, your hero isn’t one of them. An Indian in a </p>
<p>Western town, an alien in a sci-fi game of human </p>
<p>marines, or a half-orc in a party of elves, dwarves, </p>
<p>and humans are all examples of outsiders. Locals </p>
<p>are likely to raise prices on the Outsider, ignore </p>
<p>pleas for help, and generally treat him as if he’s of </p>
<p>a lower class than the rest of their society.</p>
<p>In addition to the roleplaying effects above, your </p>
<p>hero’s Charisma suffers a –2 modifier among all </p>
<p>but his own people.</p>
<p>Overconfident.(Major)</p>
<p>There’s nothing out there your hero can’t defeat. </p>
<p>At least that’s what he thinks. He believes he can </p>
<p>do most anything and never wants to retreat from a </p>
<p>challenge. He’s not suicidal, but he certainly takes </p>
<p>on more than common sense dictates.</p>
<p>Pacifist.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>Your hero absolutely despises violence. Minor </p>
<p>pacifism means he only fights when given no other </p>
<p>choice, and never allows the killing of prisoners </p>
<p>or other defenseless victims.</p>
<p>Major Pacifists won’t fight living characters under </p>
<p><i>any</i> circumstances. They may defend themselves, </p>
<p>but  won’t  do  anything  to  permanently  harm </p>
<p>sentient,  living  creatures.  Note  that  undeniably </p>
<p>evil creatures, undead, demons, and the like are </p>
<p>fair game. A Major Pacifist might also fight with </p>
<p>nonlethal methods, such as with his fists. Such </p>
<p>characters only do so when obviously threatened, </p>
<p>however.</p>
<p>Phobia.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>Phobias  are  overwhelming  and  irrational </p>
<p>fears that stay with a hero for the rest of his life. </p>
<p>Whenever a character is in the presence of his </p>
<p>phobia, he subtracts 2 from all his Trait tests as </p>
<p>a Minor Hindrance, and 4 if the fear is a Major </p>
<p>Phobia.</p>
<p>Phobias  shouldn’t  be  too  obvious—everyone </p>
<p>should be afraid of vampires, for example, so it’s </p>
<p>not a phobia—it’s common sense. Instead, the </p>
<p>phobia usually centers on some random element </p>
<p>the mind focused on during whatever encounter </p>
<p>caused  such  a  fright.  Remember,  phobias  are </p>
<p><i>irrational</i> fears.</p>
<p>Poverty.(Minor)</p>
<p>It’s said a fool and his money are soon parted. </p>
<p>Your hero is that fool. He starts with half the usual </p>
<p>money for your setting and just can’t seem to hang </p>
<p>onto funds acquired after play begins. In general, </p>
<p>the player halves his total funds every game week.</p>
<p>Quirk.(Minor)</p>
<p>Your hero has some minor foible that is usually </p>
<p>humorous,  but  can  occasionally  cause  him </p>
<p>trouble. A swashbuckler may always try to first </p>
<p>slash his initials on his foes before attacking, a </p>
<p>dwarf may brag constantly about his culture, or a </p>
<p>snobby debutante might not eat, drink, or socialize </p>
<p>with the lower class.</p>
<p>Small.(Major)</p>
<p>Your character is either very skinny, very short, </p>
<p>or both relative to his particular race. Subtract 1 </p>
<p>from his Toughness for his reduced stature.</p>
<p>Stubborn.(Minor)</p>
<p>This stubborn individual always wants his way </p>
<p>and  never  admits  he’s  wrong.  Even  when  it’s </p>
<p>painfully obvious he’s made a mistake he tries to </p>
<p>justify it with half-truths and rationalizations.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--33</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>Ugly.(Minor)</p>
<p>Unfortunately,  this  individual  hit  more  than  a </p>
<p>few ugly sticks on his way down the tree of life. </p>
<p>His Charisma is lowered by 2, and he is generally </p>
<p>shunned by members of the opposite sex.</p>
<p>Vengeful.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>Your  character  always  attempts  to  right  a </p>
<p>wrong he feels was done to him. If this is a Minor </p>
<p>Hindrance, he usually seeks vengeance legally. </p>
<p>The type and immediacy of his vengeance varies </p>
<p>by character, of course. Some plot and scheme for </p>
<p>months to extract what they see as justice. Others </p>
<p>demand immediate results.</p>
<p>If this is a Major Hindrance, your character will </p>
<p>kill to rectify his perceived injustice.</p>
<p>Vow.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>The character has a vow of some sort. Whether </p>
<p>it’s  Major  or  Minor  depends  on  the  Vow  itself. </p>
<p>Some  may  have  Vows  to  particular  orders  or </p>
<p>causes, to the Hippocratic Oath, to rid the world </p>
<p>of evil, and so on. The danger in fulfilling the Vow </p>
<p>and how often it might occur determines the level </p>
<p>of the Hindrance. Whatever the Vow, it’s only a </p>
<p>Hindrance if it actually comes into play from time </p>
<p>to time and causes the character some discomfort.</p>
<p>Wanted.(Minor.or.Major)</p>
<p>Your  hero  has  committed  some  crime  in  his </p>
<p>past  and  will  be  arrested  if  discovered  by  the </p>
<p>authorities. This assumes the setting actually has </p>
<p>laws and police officers to enforce them.</p>
<p> The level of the Hindrance depends on how </p>
<p>serious  the  crime  was. A  hero  with  numerous </p>
<p>unpaid parking tickets (in a game where he might </p>
<p>have to drive occasionally) has a Minor Hindrance, </p>
<p>as  does  someone  wanted  for  more  serious </p>
<p>crimes away from the main campaign area. Being </p>
<p>accused of murder is a Major Hindrance in almost </p>
<p>any setting.</p>
<p>Yellow.(Major)</p>
<p>Not everyone has ice water in his veins. Your </p>
<p>hero is squeamish at the sight of blood and gore </p>
<p>and terrified of coming to harm. He subtracts 2 </p>
<p>from all of his fear-based Spirit checks.</p>
<p>Young.(Major)</p>
<p>Children  are  sometimes  forced  to  go  on </p>
<p>dangerous  adventures  through  unfortunate </p>
<p>circumstances. Think  carefully  before  choosing </p>
<p>this  Hindrance,  for  your  youngster  starts  at  a </p>
<p>significant disadvantage.</p>
<p>Young heroes are generally 8–12 years old (in </p>
<p>human years—adjust this for races with different </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--34</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>aging  paradigms). They  have  only  3  points  to </p>
<p>adjust their attributes and 10 skill points. On the </p>
<p>plus side, youths like these have a fair amount of </p>
<p>luck. They draw one extra Benny at the beginning </p>
<p>of each game session in addition to any additional </p>
<p>Bennies gained from such things as the Luck or </p>
<p>Great Luck Edges.</p>
<p>If  the  character  should  live  long  enough  to </p>
<p>mature, the Hindrance doesn’t have to be bought </p>
<p>off, he’s already paid the price for the Hindrance </p>
<p>by starting at a disadvantage. He stops getting </p>
<p>the  extra  Benny  when  he  reaches  18  years  of </p>
<p>age  however  (or  the  age  of  adulthood  in  your </p>
<p>particular setting).</p>
<p>Edges</p>
<p>Below  is  a  list  of  Edges  common  to  most </p>
<p>settings. You’ll find more Edges in official <i>Savage </i></p>
<p><i>Worlds</i>  setting  books  as  well. The  Edges  are </p>
<p>grouped by type to help during character creation. </p>
<p>Unless an Edge specifically says otherwise, it may </p>
<p>only be selected once.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Below  each  Edge  are  any </p>
<p>skills  and  Rank  required  to  take  it. A  Novice </p>
<p>character  can’t  buy  a  Legendary  Edge,  for </p>
<p>instance. A character may always purchase an </p>
<p>Edge of a Rank lower than his.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Improved Edges: </b>Some Edges have improved </p>
<p>effects if you purchase additional “levels” in them, </p>
<p>such  as Attractive  and  Very Attractive,  or  Rich </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--35</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>and Filthy Rich. To buy an Improved Edge, you </p>
<p>must have all previous versions of an Edge. You </p>
<p>must choose Rich before buying Filthy Rich, for </p>
<p>example.</p>
<p>Background.Edges</p>
<p>These  Edges  are  hereditary  and  background </p>
<p>advantages or learned responses that develop in </p>
<p>a character after prolonged training or exposure </p>
<p>to certain events.</p>
<p>Players can choose these Edges after character </p>
<p>creation but the Game Master might require a little </p>
<p>more rationalization. An individual might choose </p>
<p>the Attractive  Edge,  for  example,  by  cleaning </p>
<p>herself  up,  getting  a  makeover,  and  generally </p>
<p>paying more attention to her looks. Characters </p>
<p>might  be  able  to  gain  the Arcane  Background </p>
<p>Edge as well, should they find a book of forbidden </p>
<p>knowledge or train under another arcane type in </p>
<p>their party. </p>
<p>Design.Note.-.Background.Edges</p>
<p><i>In  previous  versions  of </i> Savage  Worlds,<i> </i></p>
<p><i>Background  Edges  could  only  be  taken  at </i></p>
<p><i>character creation without special permission </i></p>
<p><i>by the Game Master. We’ve changed that rule </i></p>
<p><i>and you may now take Background Edges as </i></p>
<p><i>advances just like any other. If you care about </i></p>
<p><i>the rationalization of such things, you may </i></p>
<p><i>want to link them to an event in your game. </i></p>
<p><i>If a player wants the Fast Healer Edge, for </i></p>
<p><i>example, you might say (or the Game Master </i></p>
<p><i>might require) that  exposure to the party’s </i></p>
<p><i>magical healing, or a new emphasis on health </i></p>
<p><i>and fitness, have given the hero this ability. </i></p>
<p>Alertness</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice</p>
<p>Not much gets by your hero. He’s very observant </p>
<p>and perceptive, and adds +2 to his Notice rolls to </p>
<p>hear, see, or otherwise sense the world around him.</p>
<p>Ambidextrous</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>Your hero is as deft with his left hand as he is </p>
<p>with  his  right.  Characters  normally  suffer  a  –2 </p>
<p>penalty when performing physical tasks with the </p>
<p>off-hand  (characters  are  assumed  to  be  right-</p>
<p>handed). With this Edge, your warrior ignores the </p>
<p>–2 penalty for using his off-hand (see page 85).</p>
<p>Arcane.Background</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Special</p>
<p>This is the Edge your character must purchase </p>
<p>to  have  any  sort  of  magical,  psionic,  or  other </p>
<p>supernatural  ability.  See  Chapter  Five  for  a </p>
<p>complete description of Arcane Backgrounds.</p>
<p>Arcane.Resistance</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Spirit d8+</p>
<p>This individual is particularly resistant to magic </p>
<p>(including psionics, weird science, etc.), whether </p>
<p>by nature or by heritage. He acts as if he had </p>
<p>2 points of Armor when hit by damage-causing </p>
<p>arcane powers, and adds +2 to his Trait rolls when </p>
<p>resisting opposed powers. Even friendly arcane </p>
<p>powers must subtract this modifier to affect the </p>
<p>resistant hero.</p>
<p>Improved.Arcane.Resistance</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Arcane Resistance</p>
<p> As above but Armor and resistance are </p>
<p>increased to 4.</p>
<p>Attractive</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Vigor d6+</p>
<p>It’s  no  secret  that  beautiful  people  have  an </p>
<p>easier  time  getting  their  way  in  life. This  Edge </p>
<p>grants your beautiful or handsome character +2 </p>
<p>to Charisma.</p>
<p>Very.Attractive</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Attractive</p>
<p>Your  hero  is  drop-dead  gorgeous.  His </p>
<p>Charisma is increased to +4.</p>
<p>Berserk</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice</p>
<p>Immediately after suffering a wound (including a </p>
<p>Shaken result from physical damage), your hero </p>
<p>must make a Smarts roll or go Berserk.</p>
<p>While Berserk, his Parry is reduced by 2 but he </p>
<p>adds +2 to all Fighting, Strength, melee damage </p>
<p>rolls,  and  Toughness.  The  warrior  ignores  all </p>
<p>wound modifiers while Berserk, but cannot use </p>
<p>any  skills,  Edges,  or  maneuvers  that  require </p>
<p>concentration, including Shooting and Taunt, but </p>
<p>not Intimidation.</p>
<p>Berserkers  attack  with  reckless  abandon. </p>
<p>Anytime his Fighting die is a 1 (regardless of his </p>
<p>Wild Die), he hits a random adjacent target (not </p>
<p>the original target). The attack may hit friend as </p>
<p>well as foe. If there are no other adjacent targets, </p>
<p>the blow simply misses.</p>
<p>The  Berserker  may  end  his  rage  by  doing </p>
<p>nothing (not even moving) for one full action and </p>
<p>making a Smarts roll at –2.</p>
<p>Brave</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Spirit d6+</p>
<p>Those with this Edge have learned to master </p>
<p>their fear. Or perhaps are so jaded or emotionally </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--36</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>distant they’ve just lost their normal “fight or flight” </p>
<p>responses. Either way, your hero adds +2 to Fear </p>
<p>tests. If the character is in a setting that uses Guts </p>
<p>as a Setting Rule, it adds to that as well.</p>
<p>Brawny</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Novice,  Strength  and </p>
<p>Vigor d6+</p>
<p>Your bruiser is very large or perhaps just very </p>
<p>fit.  His  bulk  resists  damage  better  than  most </p>
<p>and adds +1 to his Toughness. In addition, the </p>
<p>character can carry more than most proportional </p>
<p>to his Strength. He can carry 8 times his Strength </p>
<p>in pounds without penalty instead of the usual 5 </p>
<p>times his Strength.</p>
<p>Fast.Healer</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Vigor d8+</p>
<p>Some individuals just seem to heal faster than </p>
<p>others. Those with this blessing add +2 to Vigor </p>
<p>rolls when checking for natural healing. See page </p>
<p>87 for complete rules on Healing.</p>
<p>Fleet-Footed</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d6+</p>
<p>The hero’s Pace is increased by +2 and he </p>
<p>rolls a d10 instead of a d6 when running. </p>
<p>Linguist</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Smarts d6+</p>
<p>The character has an ear for languages and a </p>
<p>rare  talent  for  recognizing  similarities  between </p>
<p>them. A  character  with  this  Edge  starts  with  a </p>
<p>number  of  languages  equal  to  his  Smarts  die, </p>
<p>and can make a Smarts roll at –2 to make herself </p>
<p>understood in any language or dialect she has </p>
<p>heard spoken for at least a week.</p>
<p>Luck</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice</p>
<p>The adventurer seems to be blessed by fate, </p>
<p>karma, the gods, or whatever external forces he </p>
<p>believes in (or believe in him!)</p>
<p>He draws one extra Benny at the beginning of </p>
<p>each game session, allowing him to succeed at </p>
<p>important tasks more often than most, and survive </p>
<p>incredible dangers.</p>
<p>Great.Luck.</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice, Luck</p>
<p>The  player  draws  two  extra  Bennies </p>
<p>instead of one at the start of each session.</p>
<p>Noble</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice</p>
<p>Those born of noble blood have many perks in </p>
<p>life, but often have just as many responsibilities. </p>
<p>Nobles  have  high  status  in  their  societies,  are </p>
<p>entitled to special treatment from their foes, gain </p>
<p>+2 Charisma, and also have the Rich Edge. This </p>
<p>gives  the  hero  several  Edges  for  the  price  of </p>
<p>one, but the responsibilities more than offset the </p>
<p>additional perks. Nobles often have troops under </p>
<p>their control, as well as land, a family home, and </p>
<p>other assets. All of this must be determined by the </p>
<p>GM, and balanced by the grave responsibilities </p>
<p>the character faces. </p>
<p>As  an  example,  a  character  in  a  fantasy </p>
<p>campaign might have a company of swordsmen, a </p>
<p>small keep, and even a magical sword he inherited </p>
<p>from his father. But he also has an entire region </p>
<p>to manage, criminals to judge, justice to mete out, </p>
<p>and a jealous neighbor who covets his lands and </p>
<p>constantly plots against him at court.</p>
<p>Quick</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>Quick  characters  have  lightning-fast  reflexes </p>
<p>and a cool head. Whenever you are dealt a 5 or </p>
<p>lower in combat, you may discard and draw again </p>
<p>until you get a card higher than 5.</p>
<p>Characters  with  both  the  Level  Headed  and </p>
<p>Quick Edges draw their additional card and take </p>
<p>the best as usual. If that card is a Five or less, the </p>
<p>Quick Edge may be used to draw a replacement </p>
<p>until it’s Six or higher.</p>
<p>Rich</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice</p>
<p>Whether the individual was born with a silver </p>
<p>spoon in his mouth or earned it through hard work, </p>
<p>he’s  got  more  money  than  most.  Rich  heroes </p>
<p>start with three times the normal starting funds </p>
<p>for the setting. If a regular income is appropriate </p>
<p>for this setting, the hero receives the modern day </p>
<p>equivalent of a $150,000 annual salary.</p>
<p>Filthy.Rich</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Rich or Noble</p>
<p>This character is very wealthy. He has five </p>
<p>times the starting funds for the setting and, </p>
<p>if  appropriate,  a  yearly  income  of  around </p>
<p>$500,000.</p>
<p>Wealthier characters should have a very </p>
<p>complete background as well. This needs </p>
<p>to be worked out with the GM, and comes </p>
<p>with many more assets as well as onerous </p>
<p>responsibilities.</p>
<p>Combat.Edges</p>
<p>These Edges are designed to help your hero </p>
<p>dish  out  terrible  damage—or  survive  it—in  the </p>
<p>bloody battles of <i>Savage Worlds.</i></p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--37</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>Block</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Fighting d8+</p>
<p>Warriors who engage in frequent hand-to-hand </p>
<p>combat are far more skilled in personal defense </p>
<p>than most others. They’ve learned not only how to </p>
<p>attack, but how to block their opponent’s blows as </p>
<p>well. A fighter with this Edge adds +1 to his Parry.</p>
<p>Improved.Block</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran, Block</p>
<p>As  above,  but  the  hero  adds  +2  to  his </p>
<p>Parry.</p>
<p>Brawler</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Str d8+</p>
<p>Frequent fights with his bare hands have </p>
<p>given this thug a powerful punch. When he </p>
<p>hits  a  foe  with  a  successful  bare-handed </p>
<p>Fighting roll, he adds +2 to his damage.</p>
<p>Bruiser</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Brawler</p>
<p>When the bruiser gets a raise on his bare-</p>
<p>handed Fighting attack, he rolls a d8 instead </p>
<p>of a d6.</p>
<p>Combat.Reflexes</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p>Your  adventurer  recovers  quickly  from  shock </p>
<p>and trauma. He adds +2 to his Spirit roll when </p>
<p>attempting to recover from being Shaken.</p>
<p>Counterattack</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Fighting d8+</p>
<p>Fighters with this Edge know how to respond </p>
<p>instantly to an enemy’s mistakes. Once per round </p>
<p>(if not Shaken), the character receives one free </p>
<p>Fighting  attack  against  one  adjacent  foe  who </p>
<p>failed a Fighting attack against him. This attack </p>
<p>is made at –2, and the Counterattack must be a </p>
<p>normal attack (no Disarm, Wild Attack, or other </p>
<p>maneuvers),  and  may  not  be  combined  with </p>
<p>Frenzy or Sweep. It may be used with the Defend </p>
<p>maneuver, but not Full Defense.</p>
<p>Improved.Counterattack</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran, Counterattack</p>
<p>As  above  but  the  character  may  ignore </p>
<p>the –2 penalty.</p>
<p>Dodge</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Agility d8+</p>
<p>Some  crafty  types  know  how  to  get  out  of </p>
<p>harm’s way. This Edge allows them to use cover, </p>
<p>movement, and concealment to make them harder </p>
<p>to  hit.  Unless  they  are  the  victim  of  a  surprise </p>
<p>attack and taken completely unaware, attackers </p>
<p>must subtract 1 from their ranged attack rolls when </p>
<p>targeting them (even in close combat).</p>
<p>Characters who attempt to evade area effect </p>
<p>attacks  may  add  +1  to  their Agility  roll  as  well </p>
<p>(when allowed).</p>
<p>Improved.Dodge</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran, Dodge</p>
<p>As  above  but  attackers  subtract  2  from </p>
<p>their attack rolls, and the character adds +2 </p>
<p>to evade area effect weapons when allowed.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--38</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Elan</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Spirit d8+</p>
<p>When  this  spirited  hero  puts  his  heart  into </p>
<p>something it tends to pay off in big ways. When </p>
<p>you spend a Benny on a Trait roll (including Soak </p>
<p>rolls), add +2 to the final total.</p>
<p>Extraction</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>When  a  character  normally  withdraws  from </p>
<p>a  melee,  his  attacker  gets  a  free  attack  before </p>
<p>he  does  so—a  very  dangerous  proposition  for </p>
<p>most. Your  hero  is  adept  at  retreating  from  an </p>
<p>engagement.</p>
<p>Make an Agility roll. If successful, one opponent </p>
<p>doesn’t get a free attack anytime you disengage </p>
<p>(see page 87).</p>
<p>Improved.Extraction</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Extraction</p>
<p>As above but if you succeed with a raise </p>
<p>all  opponents  currently  in  melee  with  the </p>
<p>character  lose  their  free  attack  as  your </p>
<p>warrior withdraws.</p>
<p>First.Strike</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>Once per turn the hero (if not Shaken) gets a free </p>
<p>Fighting attack against a single foe who moves </p>
<p>adjacent to him. This automatically interrupts the </p>
<p>opponent’s action and does not cost the hero his </p>
<p>action if he is on Hold or has not yet acted this </p>
<p>round.</p>
<p>Improved.First.Strike</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Heroic, First </p>
<p>Strike</p>
<p>As  above  but  the  hero </p>
<p>may  make  one  free </p>
<p>attack  against  each </p>
<p>and  every  foe  who </p>
<p>moves  adjacent  to </p>
<p>him.</p>
<p>Florentine</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> </p>
<p>Novice, Agility  d8+, </p>
<p>Fighting d8+</p>
<p>A  character  trained  to  fight </p>
<p>“Florentine” is a master at </p>
<p>wielding  two  weapons  at </p>
<p>once. He adds +1 to his </p>
<p>Fighting  rolls  versus  an </p>
<p>opponent  with  a  single </p>
<p>weapon  and  no  shield.  In </p>
<p>addition, opponents subtract </p>
<p>1 from any “gang up” bonuses they would normally </p>
<p>get against the fighter as his two flashing blades </p>
<p>parry their blows.</p>
<p>Frenzy</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Fighting d10+</p>
<p>Frenzied fighters make fast and furious melee </p>
<p>attacks,  sacrificing  finesse  for  raw  speed. This </p>
<p>allows  them  to  make  an  extra  Fighting  attack </p>
<p>per  round  at  a  –2  penalty  to  all  Fighting  rolls. </p>
<p>This attack must be taken at the same time as </p>
<p>another Fighting attack though it may target any </p>
<p>two foes adjacent to the hero (Wild Cards roll two </p>
<p>Fighting dice and one Wild Die). The –2 penalty </p>
<p>is subtracted from all attacks. </p>
<p>A character armed with two weapons still only </p>
<p>makes one extra attack.</p>
<p>Improved.Frenzy</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran, Frenzy</p>
<p>As above but the character may ignore the </p>
<p>–2 Frenzy penalty.</p>
<p>Giant.Killer</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran</p>
<p>The bigger they are, the harder they are to kill. </p>
<p>At least for most. But your hero knows how to find </p>
<p>the weak points in massive creatures.</p>
<p>Your hero does +1d6 damage when attacking </p>
<p>creatures three sizes or more larger </p>
<p>than  himself. An  ogre  (Size  +3) </p>
<p>with  this  ability,  for  example, </p>
<p>gains the bonus only against </p>
<p>creatures  of  Size  +6  or </p>
<p>greater. A human Giant Killer </p>
<p>(Size  0),  can  claim  the </p>
<p>bonus  against  the  ogre, </p>
<p>however.</p>
<p>Hard.to.Kill</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> </p>
<p>Wild Card, Novice, </p>
<p>Spirit d8+</p>
<p>This adventurer has more </p>
<p>lives than a truckload of cats. </p>
<p>When forced to make Vigor </p>
<p>rolls due to Incapacitation, </p>
<p>he may ignore his wound </p>
<p>modifiers.  This  only </p>
<p>applies to Vigor rolls called </p>
<p>for to resist Incapacitation </p>
<p>or  death  (see  page  77).  He </p>
<p>still suffers from wound modifiers </p>
<p>for other Trait rolls normally.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--39</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>Harder.to.Kill</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran, Hard to Kill</p>
<p>Your hero is tougher to kill than Rasputin. </p>
<p>If he is ever “killed,” roll a die. On an odd </p>
<p>result, he’s dead as usual. On an even roll, </p>
<p>he’s  Incapacitated  but  somehow  escapes </p>
<p>death. He may be captured, stripped of all </p>
<p>his belongings, or mistakenly left for dead, </p>
<p>but he somehow survives.</p>
<p>Improvisational.Fighter</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Smarts d6+ </p>
<p>Heroes  often  find  themselves  fighting </p>
<p>with pieces of equipment or furnishings not </p>
<p>designed for combat. A character with this </p>
<p>Edge has a knack for using such improvised </p>
<p>weapons, and does not suffer the usual –1 </p>
<p>penalty to attack and Parry when wielding </p>
<p>them. See page 83 for details.</p>
<p>Killer.Instinct</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Heroic</p>
<p>This hero hates losing. If he ties on an opposed </p>
<p>roll of any sort, he wins. In addition, if his skill die </p>
<p>on an opposed skill roll is a 1, he can reroll it (but </p>
<p>must keep the second result, even if it’s another 1).</p>
<p>Level.Headed</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Smarts d8+</p>
<p>Fighters who can keep their cool when everyone </p>
<p>else is running for cover are deadly customers </p>
<p>in combat.</p>
<p>A hero with this Edge draws an additional Action </p>
<p>Card in combat and acts on the best of the draw.</p>
<p>Improved.Level.Headed</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Level Headed</p>
<p>As above but the hero draws 3 cards.</p>
<p>Marksman</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p>The hero excels at taking controlled, measured </p>
<p>shots. If he does not move in a turn, he may fire </p>
<p>as if he took the Aim maneuver. Marksman may </p>
<p>never be used with a Rate of Fire greater than 1. </p>
<p>Marksman  works  with  both  Shooting  and </p>
<p>Throwing.</p>
<p>Martial.Artist</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Fighting d6+</p>
<p>This character is highly trained in hand-to-hand </p>
<p>fighting.  He  is  never  considered  unarmed  in </p>
<p>combat and so is never subject to the Unarmed </p>
<p>Defender  rule  (page  87).  With  a  successful </p>
<p>unarmed attack, he adds +d4 to his Strength roll </p>
<p>(as if he were using a small weapon).</p>
<p>Improved.Martial.Artist</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Veteran,  Martial Arts, </p>
<p>Fighting d10+</p>
<p>The character now adds +d6 to his bare-</p>
<p>handed damage.</p>
<p>Nerves.of.Steel</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Wild  Card,  Novice,  Vigor </p>
<p>d8+</p>
<p>Your hero has learned to fight on through the </p>
<p>most intense pain. He may ignore 1 point of wound </p>
<p>penalties.</p>
<p>Improved.Nerves.of.Steel</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice, Nerves of Steel</p>
<p>The  hero  ignores  2  points  of  wound </p>
<p>penalties.</p>
<p>No.Mercy</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p>The character may spend a Benny to reroll any </p>
<p>one  damage  roll,  including  those  made  for  area </p>
<p>effect attacks.</p>
<p>Quick.Draw</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>This  Edge  allows  a  hero  to  draw  a  weapon </p>
<p>as  a  free action (and thus  ignore  the usual –2 </p>
<p>multi-action penalty if he chooses to fire as well). </p>
<p>If the character must make an Agility roll to draw </p>
<p>a weapon (see page 74), he adds +2 to the roll.</p>
<p>Rock.and.Roll!</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Shooting d8+</p>
<p>Some veteran shooters learn to compensate for </p>
<p>the recoil of fully automatic weapons. If a character </p>
<p>with this Edge does not move, he may ignore the </p>
<p>recoil penalty for firing a weapon on full automatic.</p>
<p>Steady.Hands</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>Your  hero  ignores  the  “unstable  platform” </p>
<p>penalty  for  firing  from  the  backs  of  animals  or </p>
<p>while riding in moving vehicles. In addition, when </p>
<p>performing actions while Running (see page 74), </p>
<p>his penalty is –1 instead of –2.</p>
<p>Sweep</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Novice,  Strength  d8+, </p>
<p>Fighting d8+</p>
<p>Sweep  allows  a  character  to  make  a  single </p>
<p>Fighting attack and apply it against all currently </p>
<p>adjacent  targets  at  a  –2  penalty  (friends  and </p>
<p>foes  alike—be  careful).  Resolve  each  damage </p>
<p>roll separately. The attack is applied immediately </p>
<p>when rolled and only affects targets adjacent at </p>
<p>that time.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--40</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>A character may not use Sweep in the same </p>
<p>round she uses Frenzy, nor may she Sweep more </p>
<p>than once per round, or with a second weapon </p>
<p>held  in  another  hand.  In  effect,  the  hero  may </p>
<p>only perform Sweep once per action unless she </p>
<p>somehow gets two entire actions (perhaps under </p>
<p>the effects of a spell or power, for example). </p>
<p>Improved.Sweep</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran, Sweep</p>
<p>As above but the hero may ignore the –2 </p>
<p>penalty.</p>
<p>Trademark.Weapon</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Novice,  Fighting  or </p>
<p>Shooting of d10+</p>
<p>The hero knows one unique weapon (<i>Excalibur, </i></p>
<p><i>Old Betsy, Sting</i>) like the back of his hand. When </p>
<p>using that weapon, he adds +1 to his Fighting, </p>
<p>Shooting, or Throwing rolls. A hero can take this </p>
<p>Edge  multiple  times,  applying  it  to  a  different </p>
<p>weapon each time. If a Trademark Weapon is lost, </p>
<p>the hero can replace it, but the benefit of the Edge </p>
<p>doesn’t kick in for two game weeks.</p>
<p>Improved.Trademark.Weapon</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Veteran,  Trademark </p>
<p>Weapon</p>
<p>As above but the bonus when using the </p>
<p>weapon increases to +2.</p>
<p>Two-Fisted</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>A  Two-Fisted  hero  isn’t  ambidextrous—he’s </p>
<p>simply learned to fight with two weapons (or both </p>
<p>fists) at once. When attacking with a weapon in </p>
<p>each hand, he rolls each attack separately but </p>
<p>ignores the multi-action penalty (see page 75).</p>
<p>Leadership.Edges</p>
<p>Leadership  Edges  grant  bonuses  to </p>
<p>subordinates,  making  them  more  effective, </p>
<p>reliable, or durable. These Edges apply only to a </p>
<p>number of subordinates within 5” (the “command </p>
<p>radius”), and are not cumulative with the same </p>
<p>Edge  from  other  leaders.  Subordinates  may </p>
<p>benefit from  different  Leadership Edges by the </p>
<p>same or different leaders.</p>
<p>Command</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Smarts d6+</p>
<p>Command is the ability to give clear instructions </p>
<p>to  surrounding  allies  and  enforce  your  hero’s </p>
<p>will  upon  them.  This  makes  your  character’s </p>
<p>compatriots more willing to fight on despite their </p>
<p>wounds,  and  so  adds  +1  to  their  Spirit  rolls  to </p>
<p>recover from being Shaken.</p>
<p>Command.Presence</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Command</p>
<p>A booming voice, effective commands, natural </p>
<p>charisma,  or  simple  training  results  in  a  much </p>
<p>more effective combat element. At the center of </p>
<p>that element is the officer in command. A hero with </p>
<p>this Edge has a “command radius” of 10” instead </p>
<p>of the usual 5”.</p>
<p>Fervor</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Veteran,  Command, </p>
<p>Spirit d8+</p>
<p>A simple phrase uttered by a great leader can </p>
<p>sometimes have momentous results. A leader with </p>
<p>this ability can inspire his men to bloody fervor </p>
<p>by yelling a motto, slogan, or other inspirational </p>
<p>words. Those in the command radius add +1 to </p>
<p>their Fighting damage rolls.</p>
<p>Hold.the.Line!</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Seasoned,  Command, </p>
<p>Smarts d8+</p>
<p>This Edge strengthens the will of the men under </p>
<p>the hero’s command. The troops add +1 to their </p>
<p>Toughness.</p>
<p>Inspire</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Command</p>
<p>Leaders  with  exceptional  reputations  and </p>
<p>experience in battle inspire the soldiers around </p>
<p>them. They add +2 to Spirit rolls when recovering </p>
<p>from being Shaken (this includes the original +1 </p>
<p>bonus for the Command Edge).</p>
<p>Leader.of.Men</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Veteran, Command</p>
<p>Command  comes  easy  to  this  commander. </p>
<p>Those under his command work like a well-oiled </p>
<p>machine when he’s in charge.</p>
<p>Allies under the leader’s command roll a d10 </p>
<p>as  the  Wild  Die  instead  of  a  d6  when  making </p>
<p>group rolls.</p>
<p>Natural.Leader</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Command, Spirit </p>
<p>d8+</p>
<p>This  Edge  signifies  a  special  link  between  a </p>
<p>leader  and  his  men.  With  it,  he  may  share  his </p>
<p>Bennies with any troops under his command. </p>
<p>Tactician</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Seasoned,  Command, </p>
<p>Wild Card, Smarts d8+, Knowledge (Battle) </p>
<p>d6+</p>
<p>The  leader  has  a  natural  grasp  of  small  unit </p>
<p>tactics and can frequently take advantage of a </p>
<p>rapidly changing situation.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--41</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>At  the  beginning  of  a  fight  and  before  any </p>
<p>Action  Cards  are  dealt,  the  hero  makes  a </p>
<p>Knowledge  (Battle)  roll.  For  each  success  and </p>
<p>raise  he  receives  one Action  Card. These  are </p>
<p>kept separate from his regular Action Cards and </p>
<p>are not placed back into the deck until used or </p>
<p>the combat ends (including Jokers!). At the start </p>
<p>of any round, the hero may give one or more of </p>
<p>these extra cards to his allies, whether Extras or </p>
<p>Wild Cards, who then use it as their Action Card </p>
<p>for the round in place of the one dealt them. This </p>
<p>allows Extras to operate independently of Wild </p>
<p>Card  characters  for  one  round  if  they  receive </p>
<p>their own card.</p>
<p>Only  one  character  per  encounter  may  use </p>
<p>this Edge.</p>
<p>Power.Edges</p>
<p>Power  Edges  are  for  those  with  Arcane </p>
<p>Backgrounds.  See  Chapter  Five  for  more </p>
<p>information on each type of Arcane Background, </p>
<p>how to use them, and the powers available.</p>
<p>New.Power</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Arcane Background</p>
<p>An arcane character may learn a new power </p>
<p>by  choosing  this  Edge  (which  may  be  taken </p>
<p>multiple times). He may choose from any powers </p>
<p>normally available to his particular Arcane </p>
<p>Background.</p>
<p>Power.Points</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Novice, Arcane </p>
<p>Background</p>
<p>Wizards, weird scientists, and other </p>
<p>arcane  types  always  want  more </p>
<p>power. This Edge grants them an </p>
<p>additional 5 Power Points.</p>
<p>Power  Points  may  be  selected </p>
<p>more  than  once,  but  only  once  per </p>
<p>Rank.</p>
<p>Rapid.Recharge</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Seasoned, Spirit d6+, </p>
<p>Arcane Background</p>
<p>This  Edge  allows  an  arcane  character </p>
<p>to regain 1 Power Point every 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Improved.Rapid.Recharge</p>
<p><b> Requirements:</b> Veteran, Rapid Recharge</p>
<p>The character regains 1 Power Point every </p>
<p>15 minutes.</p>
<p>Soul.Drain</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b>  Seasoned, Arcane  Background </p>
<p>(any  but  Weird  Science),  Knowledge </p>
<p>(Arcana) d10+</p>
<p>Spellcasters,  mentalists,  and  other  arcane </p>
<p>types in dire need of Power Points may use this </p>
<p>Edge to drain energy from their own souls. To use </p>
<p>this dangerous ability, the arcane character first </p>
<p>decides how many Power Points he wants to draw </p>
<p>from himself. Then he makes a Spirit roll minus </p>
<p>the number of points he’s trying to drain. (This is </p>
<p>a free action.) On a Spirit total of 1 or less, the </p>
<p>character suffers a wound and falls unconscious </p>
<p>for 1d6 hours. On a failure, the character suffers </p>
<p>a wound. On a success or better, the character </p>
<p>gets the points he needed and may attempt to </p>
<p>cast a spell with them immediately (they may not </p>
<p>be saved).</p>
<p>Professional.Edges</p>
<p>Professional Edges are very special abilities that </p>
<p>reflect many years of practicing a particular trade. </p>
<p>In some cases they may also represent special </p>
<p>blessings from higher powers as well.</p>
<p>These Edges help you create a character who </p>
<p>is  far  more  competent  in  his  chosen  field  than </p>
<p>most others. If you want to make a very effective </p>
<p>Mad Scientist, for example, you could combine </p>
<p>the Arcane Background (Weird Science) with the </p>
<p>Gadgeteer and Mr. Fix It Edges.</p>
<p>Professional  Edges  represent  many  years  of </p>
<p>training  so  their  Requirements  are  quite  high. </p>
<p>Players may purchase Professional Edges after </p>
<p>character creation, but should usually lead up </p>
<p>to  it  story-wise  by  practicing  the  affected </p>
<p>trade  during  down-time  or  in  between </p>
<p>adventures. The  time  spent  acquiring </p>
<p>one of these abilities is subjective and </p>
<p>up  to  the  Game  Master,  but  makes </p>
<p>the game much more believable if a </p>
<p>little narrative time is spent training.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Stacking:</b>  Bonuses  to  the </p>
<p>same  Trait  from  different </p>
<p>Professional  Edges  do  not </p>
<p>stack.  If  you  make  a  hero </p>
<p>with  both  the  Woodsman </p>
<p>and the Thief Edges, for </p>
<p>example, he gains +2 </p>
<p>to  his  Stealth  skill, </p>
<p>not +4.</p>
<p>Ace</p>
<p><b>R e q u i r e m e n t s : </b></p>
<p>Novice, Agility d8+</p>
<p>Aces  are  special  pilots  and </p>
<p>drivers who feel more comfortable </p>
<p>behind the wheel, throttle, or flight </p>
<p>stick than on their own two feet.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--42</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Aces add +2 to Boating, Driving, and Piloting </p>
<p>rolls. In addition, they may also spend Bennies </p>
<p>to make Soak rolls for any vehicle or vessel they </p>
<p>control. This is a Boating, Driving, or Piloting roll </p>
<p>at –2 (cancelling their usual +2). Each success </p>
<p>and raise negates a wound and any critical hit </p>
<p>that would have resulted from it.</p>
<p>Acrobat</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b> Novice,  Agility  d8+, </p>
<p>Strength d6+</p>
<p>Those who have formal training in the acrobatic </p>
<p>arts  or  are  naturally  agile  may  take  this  Edge. </p>
<p>It  adds  +2  to  all Agility  rolls  made  to  perform </p>
<p>acrobatic maneuvers (including Trick maneuvers), </p>
<p>and also adds +1 to a character’s Parry as long </p>
<p>as he has no encumbrance penalty.</p>
<p>Adept</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  </p>
<p>Novice,  Arcane </p>
<p>Background (Miracles), Martial Artist, Faith </p>
<p>d8+, Fighting d8+</p>
<p>Adepts  are  holy  warriors  who  have  trained </p>
<p>themselves to be living weapons. Some do so to </p>
<p>be ultimate warriors; others do it in the service of </p>
<p>a cause or deity.</p>
<p>As a free action, an adept can spend 1 Power </p>
<p>Point to gain AP 2 with all of his unarmed attacks </p>
<p>until his next action.</p>
<p>In addition, upon taking this Edge and at each </p>
<p>new  Rank,  they  may  choose  to  change  the </p>
<p>trappings of one of the following powers to work </p>
<p>only  on  themselves  but  be  activated  as  a  free </p>
<p>action: <i>boost/lower trait, deflection, healing, smite, </i></p>
<p>or<i> speed</i>. The Adept must have the power to begin </p>
<p>with, and this does not allow him to activate more </p>
<p>than one power in a round.</p>
<p>Assassin</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Novice,  Agility  d8+, </p>
<p>Climbing d6+, Fighting d6+, Stealth d8+</p>
<p>Assassins are trained killers who know how to </p>
<p>kill  with  deadly  precision — if  they  can  properly </p>
<p>approach  their  prey. Assassins  add  +2  to  any </p>
<p>damage  roll  where  they  strike  a  foe  unawares </p>
<p>(even with ranged attacks).</p>
<p>Champion</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b></p>
<p>Novice,  Arcane </p>
<p>Background (Miracles), Spirit d8+, Strength </p>
<p>d6+, Vigor d8+, Faith d6+, Fighting d8+</p>
<p>Champions are holy (or unholy) men and women </p>
<p>chosen to fight for a particular deity or religion. </p>
<p>Most are pious souls ready and willing to lay down </p>
<p>their lives for a greater cause, but some may have </p>
<p>been born into the role and follow their path with </p>
<p>some reluctance.</p>
<p>Champions  fight  the  forces  of  darkness  (or </p>
<p>good).  They  add  +2  damage  when  attacking </p>
<p>supernaturally evil (or good) creatures, and have </p>
<p>+2  Toughness  when  suffering  damage  from </p>
<p>supernaturally evil (or good) sources, including </p>
<p>arcane powers and the weapons, claws, teeth, </p>
<p>etc., of such creatures.</p>
<p>Gadgeteer</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b> Novice, Arcane  Back-</p>
<p>ground (Weird Science), Smarts d8+, Repair </p>
<p>d8+, Weird Science d8+, at least two other </p>
<p>scientific Knowledge skills at d6+</p>
<p>These  mechanical  gurus  are  so  technically </p>
<p>savvy they can quickly build a machine to handle </p>
<p>nearly any situation.</p>
<p>Once  per  game  session,  a  gadgeteer  can </p>
<p>create  a  “jury-rigged”  device  from  spare  parts. </p>
<p>The  device  functions  just  like  any  other  Weird </p>
<p>Science  device,  and  uses  any  power  available </p>
<p>to Weird Scientists in that setting (though this is </p>
<p>still subject to Rank restrictions). It has half the </p>
<p>inventor’s Power Points, and once these are used </p>
<p>up, the gadget burns out and does not recharge. </p>
<p>The inventor must have access to some parts and </p>
<p>a reasonable amount of time (GM’s call, but at </p>
<p>least 1d20 minutes) to create the gizmo.</p>
<p>Holy/Unholy.Warrior</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b></p>
<p>Novice,  Arcane </p>
<p>Background (Miracles), Spirit d8+, Faith d6+</p>
<p>Acolytes,  clerics,  paladins,  holy  slayers,  and </p>
<p>other avatars of the gods are frequently tasked </p>
<p>with battling the forces of evil in the mortal world. </p>
<p>This Edge gives them a slight advantage against </p>
<p>such foes.</p>
<p>As an action, a priest or other holy person may </p>
<p>call upon his chosen deity to repulse supernaturally </p>
<p>evil creatures, such as the undead, demons, and </p>
<p>the like. It also works on evil characters with the </p>
<p>Arcane Background (Miracles) Edge.</p>
<p>Repulsing evil costs 1 Power Point and has a </p>
<p>range of the character’s Spirit. Targeted creatures </p>
<p>within that range must make a Spirit roll. Failure </p>
<p>means the creature is Shaken; a 1 means it is </p>
<p>destroyed. Wild Cards suffer an automatic Wound </p>
<p>instead.</p>
<p>A  character  may  also  be  an  Unholy  Warrior </p>
<p>working  for  the  forces  of  evil.  In  this  case, </p>
<p>he  repulses  good  creatures,  such  as  angels, </p>
<p>paladins,  or  good  characters  with  Arcane </p>
<p>Background (Miracles).</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--43</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>Investigator</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b> Novice,  Smarts  d8+, </p>
<p>Investigation d8+, Streetwise d8+</p>
<p>Investigators have spent a great deal of time </p>
<p>researching ancient legends, working the streets, </p>
<p>or  deducing  devilish  mysteries.  Some  of  these </p>
<p>heroes  are  actual  Private  Investigators  for  hire </p>
<p>while others may be sleuthing mages in a fantasy </p>
<p>world  or  perhaps  inquisitive  college  professors </p>
<p>stumbling upon Things Man Was Not Meant to </p>
<p>Know in the dark of night. Investigators add +2 </p>
<p>to Investigation and Streetwise rolls, as well as </p>
<p>Notice rolls made to search through evidence.</p>
<p>Jack-of-All-Trades</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Smarts d10+</p>
<p>Through  advanced  schooling,  book-learning, </p>
<p>computer-enhanced  skill  programs,  or  just </p>
<p>amazing  intuitive  perception,  your  hero  has  a </p>
<p>talent for picking up skills on the fly. There is little </p>
<p>he can’t figure out given a little time and a dash </p>
<p>of luck.</p>
<p>Any time he makes an unskilled roll for a Smarts-</p>
<p>based skill, he may do so at d4 instead of the </p>
<p>usual d4–2.</p>
<p>McGyver</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Novice,  Smarts  d6+, </p>
<p>Repair d6+, Notice d8+</p>
<p>This character can improvise something when </p>
<p>the need for a tool arises. He suffers no negative </p>
<p>penalties on Trait rolls for lack of equipment in </p>
<p>most situations.</p>
<p>In  addition,  given  a  few  simple  tools,  props, </p>
<p>or devices, he can generally rig devices to help </p>
<p>escape from death-traps, weapons to match some </p>
<p>bizarre  need,  or  otherwise  create  something </p>
<p>that’s  needed  when  such  a  thing  isn’t  actually </p>
<p>present. The extent of this is completely up to the </p>
<p>Game Master, but creativity should be rewarded, </p>
<p>particularly  in  dire  situations  where  few  other </p>
<p>answers are possible.</p>
<p>Mentalist</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b></p>
<p>Novice,  Arcane </p>
<p>Background  (Psionics),  Smarts  d8+, </p>
<p>Psionics d6+</p>
<p>Mentalists  are  masters  of  mind  control  and </p>
<p>psionics. Some are pulp heroes, others are trained </p>
<p>in  secret  government  academies  to  root  out </p>
<p>traitors. Their frequent toying with human minds </p>
<p>gives them a +2 on any opposed Psionics roll, </p>
<p>whether they are using their powers against a foe </p>
<p>or are trying to defend against a rival Mentalist.</p>
<p>Mr..Fix.It</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b></p>
<p>Novice,  Arcane </p>
<p>Background (Weird Science), Smarts d10+, </p>
<p>Repair d8+, Weird Science d8+, at least two </p>
<p>other scientific Knowledge skills at d6+</p>
<p>The  inventor  adds  +2  to  Repair  rolls.  With  a </p>
<p>raise, he halves the time normally required to fix </p>
<p>something. This means that if a particular Repair </p>
<p>job already states that a raise repairs it in half the </p>
<p>time, a Mr. Fix It could finish the job in one-quarter </p>
<p>the time with a raise.</p>
<p>Scholar</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b> Novice,  d8+  in  affected </p>
<p>skill</p>
<p>Learned  professors,  devoted  students,  and </p>
<p>amateur enthusiasts spend months of their lives </p>
<p>studying particular subjects. They become experts </p>
<p>in these fields, and rarely fail to answer questions </p>
<p>in their particular area of expertise.</p>
<p>Pick any two Knowledge skills the Scholar has </p>
<p>a d8 or better in. Add +2 to your total whenever </p>
<p>these skills are used. Those who study military </p>
<p>history have a natural edge when commanding </p>
<p>troops in Mass Battles (see page 106)—a +2 to </p>
<p>a Knowledge (Battle) roll can mean the difference </p>
<p>between a rousing victory and a crushing defeat.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--44</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Thief</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b> Novice,  Agility  d8+, </p>
<p>Climbing d6+, Lockpicking d6+, Stealth d8+</p>
<p>Thieves  specialize  in  deceit,  treachery,  and </p>
<p>acrobatics. They can be invaluable where traps </p>
<p>must  be  detected,  walls  must  be  climbed,  and </p>
<p>locks must be picked.</p>
<p>Thieves add +2 to Climbing, Lockpick, Stealth, </p>
<p>as well as Notice or Repair rolls that relate to traps </p>
<p>and similar devices. The bonus to Stealth does </p>
<p>not apply when the character is in a wilderness </p>
<p>environment—only in urban areas.</p>
<p>Wizard</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b></p>
<p>Novice,  Arcane </p>
<p>Background  (Magic),  Smarts  d8+, </p>
<p>Knowledge (Arcana) d8+, Spellcasting d6+</p>
<p>Wizards  range  from  young  apprentices  to </p>
<p>frighteningly powerful supreme sorcerers. They </p>
<p>are  often  physically  weak,  however,  and  rarely </p>
<p>have  the  divine  powers  or  healing  abilities  of </p>
<p>priestly spellcasters. What they lack in spiritual </p>
<p>favor, however, they more than make up for in </p>
<p>utility and eldritch might.</p>
<p>Wizards tend to learn their craft in formalized </p>
<p>institutions or under the tutelage of experienced </p>
<p>masters.  Each  raise  a  Wizard  gets  on  his </p>
<p>Spellcasting roll reduces the cost of the spell by </p>
<p>1 Power Point. The Wizard must have the points </p>
<p>available to cast the spell in the first place before </p>
<p>rolling.</p>
<p>Woodsman</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b> Novice,  Spirit  d6+, </p>
<p>Survival d8+, Tracking d8+</p>
<p>Woodsmen  are  rangers,  scouts,  and  hunters </p>
<p>who are more at home in the wilderness than in </p>
<p>urban areas. They are skilled trackers and scouts, </p>
<p>and know how to live off the land for months at </p>
<p>a time. Woodsmen gain +2 to Tracking, Survival, </p>
<p>and  Stealth  rolls  made  in  the  wilderness  (not </p>
<p>towns, ruins, or underground).</p>
<p>Social.Edges</p>
<p>Getting people to do what you want is a critical </p>
<p>skill in most any setting. These Edges help your </p>
<p>hero do just that.</p>
<p>Charismatic</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Spirit d8+</p>
<p>Your hero has learned how to work with others, </p>
<p>even those who might be somewhat opposed to </p>
<p>him or his efforts. This adds +2 to his Charisma.</p>
<p>Common.Bond</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Wild  Card,  Novice,  Spirit </p>
<p>d8+</p>
<p>This Edge signifies a special link between close </p>
<p>companions—such as a typical party. It doesn’t </p>
<p>matter whether or not the characters get along </p>
<p>perfectly or not, they’ve just formed a close and </p>
<p>common bond during their epic adventures.</p>
<p>A  character  with  this  Edge  may  freely  give </p>
<p>his  Bennies  to  any  other  Wild  Card  he  can </p>
<p>communicate with. This represents the character </p>
<p>giving his verbal or spiritual support to the ally. </p>
<p>The  player  should  say  what  his  character  is </p>
<p>doing to give the support. The gesture could be </p>
<p>as complex as a rousing speech, or as simple as </p>
<p>a knowing nod.</p>
<p>Connections</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice</p>
<p>Whether  it’s  to  the  Feds,  the  cops,  the  Mob, </p>
<p>or  some  big  corporation,  your  heroine  knows </p>
<p>someone on the inside—someone who is willing </p>
<p>to lend her a hand on occasion (usually once per </p>
<p>game session).</p>
<p>This  Edge  may  be  taken  more  than  once, </p>
<p>but  each  time  must  be  applied  to  a  different </p>
<p>organization.  The  GM  should  also  ensure </p>
<p>the  organization  is  limited  to  a  single,  unique </p>
<p>organization. A  hero  may,  for  instance,  have </p>
<p>Connections (US Army), but he shouldn’t have a </p>
<p>blanket Connections (Military).</p>
<p>To use a character’s Connections requires that </p>
<p>she  first get  in  touch  with  one of  her  contacts. </p>
<p>This  requires  a  Streetwise  roll.  Failure  means </p>
<p>the particular contact wasn’t available, their cell </p>
<p>phone wasn’t on, or they were otherwise tied up.</p>
<p>Once  in  contact,  the  hero  must  make  a </p>
<p>Persuasion roll. The GM should feel free to modify </p>
<p>both the Persuasion roll and any results based on </p>
<p>the circumstances.</p>
<p>A  failure  indicates  the  heroine’s  contacts  just </p>
<p>couldn’t come through this time, or perhaps just </p>
<p>weren’t  persuaded  that  their  help  was  really </p>
<p>necessary. </p>
<p>On  a  success,  the  contact  might  share </p>
<p>information, but won’t do anything too risky to help. </p>
<p>On a raise, the contact is willing to leak sensitive </p>
<p>information, but stops short of outright betrayal.</p>
<p>Two  or  more  raises  means  the  heroine  has </p>
<p>pushed  the  right  buttons  and  can  count  on </p>
<p>serious  help. The  Connection  will  risk  serious </p>
<p>consequences for the heroine, and if she needs </p>
<p>financial assistance, may provide more than he’s </p>
<p>comfortable with. If the heroine asks for muscle, </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--45</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>the  contact  delivers  either  one  expert  (a  safe-</p>
<p>cracker, wheel-man, security expert, etc.) or five </p>
<p>average fighter-types for the contact’s particular </p>
<p>organization (a mob boss sends five thugs, the </p>
<p>Army sends five infantrymen, etc.).</p>
<p>Strong.Willed</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice, Intimidation d6+, </p>
<p>Taunt d6+</p>
<p>Characters  with  strong  willpower  use  their </p>
<p>voice,  steely  stares,  or  quick  wits  to  unnerve </p>
<p>their  opponents.  Strong  Willed  adds  +2  to  a </p>
<p>character’s Intimidation and Taunt rolls, as well </p>
<p>as his Spirit and Smarts rolls when resisting Test </p>
<p>of Wills attacks.</p>
<p>Weird.Edges</p>
<p>Weird Edges are slightly supernatural and only </p>
<p>appropriate in games with those elements. </p>
<p>Beast.Bond</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice</p>
<p>Some individuals can exert incredible will over </p>
<p>their animal companions. These characters may </p>
<p>spend their own Bennies for any animals under </p>
<p>their control, including mounts, pet dogs, familiars, </p>
<p>and so on.</p>
<p>Beast.Master</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice, Spirit d8+</p>
<p>Animals  like  your  hero,  and  won’t  attack  him </p>
<p>unless he attacks them first or they are enraged </p>
<p>for some reason. His “animal magnetism” is so </p>
<p>great he’s attracted a loyal animal of some sort </p>
<p>as  well. This  is  typically  a  dog,  wolf,  or  raptor, </p>
<p>though the GM may allow other companions if it </p>
<p>fits the setting. </p>
<p>The beast is an Extra (not a Wild Card). If it </p>
<p>should be killed, the hero finds a replacement in </p>
<p>2d6 days.</p>
<p>Danger.Sense</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice</p>
<p>Your hero can sense when something bad is </p>
<p>about to happen. Anytime he’s about to be the </p>
<p>victim of a surprise attack, ambush, or other nasty </p>
<p>surprise, he gets a Notice roll at –2 just before the </p>
<p>attack or event occurs. If successful, the character </p>
<p>knows something is about to happen and may take </p>
<p>appropriate action against it. This means the hero </p>
<p>is on Hold for the first round of a combat. Should </p>
<p>the hero fail his roll, he still follows the normal </p>
<p>Surprise rules, if applicable (see page 73).</p>
<p>Healer</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice, Spirit d8+</p>
<p>A hero with this Edge adds +2 to all Healing </p>
<p>rolls (including natural healing rolls for his own </p>
<p>wounds), whether natural or magical in nature. </p>
<p>Up to five companions traveling with a Healer add </p>
<p>the bonus to their natural healing rolls as well.</p>
<p>Liquid.Courage</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Novice, Vigor d8+</p>
<p>Your hero processes alcohol far differently than </p>
<p>most. The  round  after  consuming  a  stiff  drink </p>
<p>(at least 8 ounces of hard liquor or equivalent), </p>
<p>the character’s Vigor increases by one die type </p>
<p>(increasing Toughness as well). The hard drinker </p>
<p>can  also  ignore  one  level  of  wound  modifiers </p>
<p>(which  stacks  with  other  abilities  that  do  the </p>
<p>same).</p>
<p>The effect lasts for one hour after it begins. If the </p>
<p>drunkard seeks inebriation he suffers –2 to Smarts </p>
<p>and Agility-based rolls for as long as he continues </p>
<p>to drink and the next 1d6 hours thereafter.</p>
<p>Scavenger</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Novice, Luck</p>
<p>Once  per  session  the  hero  may  “suddenly </p>
<p>remember”  that  he  has  a  much-needed  piece </p>
<p>of equipment on his person. The item must be </p>
<p>capable of being stored in the hero’s pocket or bag </p>
<p>(assuming he has one), and the Game Master has </p>
<p>the final word on what can be found.</p>
<p>Wild.Card.Edges</p>
<p>The  following  Edges  work  only  when  the </p>
<p>character  is  dealt  a  Joker  during  combat. The </p>
<p>Edge’s effects are in addition to the usual effects </p>
<p>of being dealt a Joker.</p>
<p>Dead.Shot</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Wild  Card,  Seasoned, </p>
<p>Shooting/Throwing d10+</p>
<p>The character doubles his total damage when </p>
<p>making a successful Shooting or Throwing attack </p>
<p>this round.</p>
<p>Mighty.Blow</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Wild  Card,  Seasoned, </p>
<p>Fighting d10+</p>
<p>The character doubles his total damage when </p>
<p>making a successful Fighting attack this round.</p>
<p>Power.Surge</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Wild  Card,  Seasoned, </p>
<p>arcane skill d10+</p>
<p>This Edge is for those characters with Arcane </p>
<p>Backgrounds. When dealt a Joker, the character </p>
<p>recovers 2d6 Power Points. He may not exceed </p>
<p>his usual limit.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--46</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Legendary.Edges</p>
<p>Most Legendary Edges are very specific to their </p>
<p>campaign world—such as gaining a stronghold </p>
<p>or divine favor—but a few fit most anywhere, as </p>
<p>shown below.</p>
<p>Followers</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Wild Card, Legendary</p>
<p>Heroes  often  acquire  dedicated  warbands, </p>
<p>“merry men,” or others who voluntarily follow the </p>
<p>hero on his adventures.</p>
<p>Each time this Edge is chosen, five followers join </p>
<p>the hero’s band. Casualties are not automatically </p>
<p>replaced, so a hero may need to choose this Edge </p>
<p>again on occasion to replenish his losses. The </p>
<p>followers must have some way to eat and earn </p>
<p>income, and generally want a piece of whatever </p>
<p>loot, treasure, or other rewards the hero acquires. </p>
<p>Otherwise, they are completely dedicated to their </p>
<p>idol and risk their lives for him under any normal </p>
<p>conditions. They won’t knowingly throw their lives </p>
<p>away except under very special circumstances.</p>
<p>The GM determines the followers’ statistics, but </p>
<p>in general, use the Soldier statistics presented on </p>
<p>page 93. Followers generally come with only basic </p>
<p>equipment depending on their particular setting </p>
<p>(warriors  in  fantasy  come  with  at  least  leather </p>
<p>armor and short swords, for example). The hero </p>
<p>must purchase any additional equipment for his </p>
<p>Followers himself.</p>
<p>Martial.Arts.Master</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Legendary,  Improved </p>
<p>Martial Arts, Fighting d12+</p>
<p>The warrior is deadly with his hands. He adds +2 </p>
<p>to his bare-handed damage every time he takes </p>
<p>this Edge, up to a maximum of five times for a </p>
<p>total damage bonus of +10.</p>
<p>Professional</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Legendary, d12 in affected </p>
<p>Trait</p>
<p>The character is an expert at a particular skill or </p>
<p>attribute (his choice). That Trait becomes d12+1. </p>
<p>This  Edge  may  be  selected  more  than  once, </p>
<p>but it may never be applied to the same skill or </p>
<p>attribute twice.</p>
<p>Expert</p>
<p><b>Requirements: </b>Legendary, Professional </p>
<p>in affected Trait</p>
<p>As above, but the Trait increases to d12+2.</p>
<p>Master</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Wild  Card,  Legendary, </p>
<p>Expert in affected Trait</p>
<p>The character’s Wild Die increases to a </p>
<p>d10  when  rolling  a  particular Trait  of  his </p>
<p>choice. This Edge may be chosen multiple </p>
<p>times,  though  it  only  affects  a  particular </p>
<p>Trait once.</p>
<p>Sidekick</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Wild Card, Legendary</p>
<p>A  character  who  triumphs  over  evil  time  and </p>
<p>time  again  becomes  an  inspiration  to  others. </p>
<p>Eventually,  one  of  these  young  crusaders  may </p>
<p>attempt to join the hero in his epic quests.</p>
<p>The hero gains a  Novice Rank sidekick. The </p>
<p>sidekick  is  a  Wild  Card,  gains  experience  as </p>
<p>usual, and has abilities that complement or mimic </p>
<p>his hero’s.</p>
<p>The player character should control his sidekick </p>
<p>just like any other ally. Of course, the sidekick may </p>
<p>occasionally cause trouble (by getting captured, </p>
<p>running into danger when he’s not supposed to, </p>
<p>etc.). The player should be prepared for his “Edge” </p>
<p>to occasionally become a “Hindrance.”</p>
<p>If the sidekick dies, he isn’t replaced unless the </p>
<p>hero chooses this Edge again.</p>
<p>Tough.as.Nails</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Legendary</p>
<p>Your  hero  is  a  grizzled  veteran.  Increase  his </p>
<p>Toughness by +1.</p>
<p>Improved.Tough.as.Nails</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Legendary, Tough as Nails</p>
<p>Increase  your  hero’s  Toughness  by </p>
<p>another +1.</p>
<p>Weapon.Master</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b> Legendary, Fighting d12</p>
<p>Increase your hero’s Parry by +1.</p>
<p>Master.of.Arms</p>
<p><b>Requirements:</b>  Legendary,  Weapon </p>
<p>Master</p>
<p>Increase your hero’s Parry by another +1.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--47</p>
<p>Character.Creation</p>
<p>Advancement</p>
<p>At  the  end  of  each  game  session  (usually </p>
<p>4-6  hours  of  gaming),  the  GM  awards  1  to  3 </p>
<p>Experience Points to everyone in the group, based </p>
<p>on these guidelines.</p>
<p>Experience.Awards</p>
<p><b>  Award </b></p>
<p><b>Situation</b></p>
<p> </p>
<p>1 </p>
<p>The group accomplished little or had </p>
<p>a very short session.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>2 </p>
<p>The group had more successes than </p>
<p>failures.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>3 </p>
<p>The group succeeded greatly, and their </p>
<p>adventure had a significant impact on </p>
<p>the overall story.</p>
<p>Ranks</p>
<p>As a character gains more Experience Points, </p>
<p>he goes up in “Rank.” This is a rough measure of </p>
<p>how powerful the hero is. As characters progress </p>
<p>in experience, new Ranks allow access to more </p>
<p>powerful Edges.</p>
<p>Rank.Table</p>
<p><b> </b></p>
<p><b>Experience Points </b></p>
<p><b>Rank</b></p>
<p> </p>
<p>0-19 </p>
<p>Novice</p>
<p> </p>
<p>20-39 </p>
<p>Seasoned</p>
<p> </p>
<p>40-59 </p>
<p>Veteran</p>
<p> </p>
<p>60-79 </p>
<p>Heroic</p>
<p> </p>
<p>80+ </p>
<p>Legendary</p>
<p>Every 5 points accumulated grants a hero an </p>
<p>Advance. An Advance lets a character do one of </p>
<p>the following:</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Gain a new Edge.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Increase a skill that is equal to or greater than </p>
<p>its linked attribute by one die type.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Increase two skills that are lower than their </p>
<p>linked attributes by one die type each.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Buy a new skill at d4.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Increase one attribute by a die type.*</p>
<p><i>*You  may  only  choose  this  option  once </i></p>
<p><i>per Rank. No Trait may be raised above a </i></p>
<p><i>d12  (but  see  the  Professional  and  Expert </i></p>
<p><i>Legendary  Edges).  Legendary  characters </i></p>
<p><i>may raise an attribute every other Advance.</i></p>
<p>Starting.With.Experienced.Characters</p>
<p>If the GM lets you make a character who has </p>
<p>already earned some experience, simply make a </p>
<p>character as usual and then grant her that many </p>
<p>Advances. A  Veteran  character,  for  example, </p>
<p>has 40 Experience Points, so you would make a </p>
<p>normal character and grant her eight Advances.</p>
<p>Additional  goods,  equipment,  or  other  assets </p>
<p>must  be  determined  by  the  Game  Master  and </p>
<p>the particular setting. As a quick rule of thumb, a </p>
<p>character’s starting funds double with each Rank </p>
<p>after Novice.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Replacement Characters:</b> When a character </p>
<p>dies,  his  new  hero  begins  play  with  one  less </p>
<p>Advance than his last.</p>
<p>Legendary.Characters</p>
<p>Legendary  characters  are  major  forces  in </p>
<p>their worlds, and often have political power and </p>
<p>influence  as  well  as a  host of  Edges  to defeat </p>
<p>those who oppose them.</p>
<p>Once  a  hero  reaches  Legendary  status,  the </p>
<p>rules for Advances change a bit. The character </p>
<p>now Advances  every  time  he  accumulates  10 </p>
<p>Experience  Points  instead  of  5,  but  a  world  of </p>
<p>new Edges opens up to him as well. “Legendary </p>
<p>Edges”  allow  heroes  to  accumulate  followers, </p>
<p>build  castles,  start  massive  corporations,  and </p>
<p>otherwise become major players in their campaign </p>
<p>world.</p>
<p>Legendary  characters  may  also  choose  to </p>
<p>improve  an  attribute  every  other Advance. A </p>
<p>few Legendary Edges are included in this book. </p>
<p>Many more are quite specific to their particular </p>
<p>campaign  worlds,  and  so  are  covered  in  other </p>
<p>Savage Settings.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--48</p>
<p>Character.Creation.Summary</p>
<p>1).Race</p>
<p>• Choose any race available in your setting.</p>
<p>2).Traits</p>
<p>• Your hero starts with a d4 in each attribute, and </p>
<p>has 5 points with which to raise them. Raising an </p>
<p>attribute a die type costs 1 point.</p>
<p>• You have 15 points for skills. Each die type in a </p>
<p>skill costs 1 point up to the linked attribute. Going </p>
<p>over the linked attribute costs 2 points per level.</p>
<p>•  Charisma  is  equal  to  the  total  bonuses  or </p>
<p>penalties given by Edges and Hindrances.</p>
<p>• Pace is 6”.</p>
<p>• Parry is equal to 2 plus half Fighting.</p>
<p>• Toughness is equal to 2 plus half Vigor. Go </p>
<p>ahead and add the bonus granted by the armor </p>
<p>worn on your torso to this value as well for speed’s </p>
<p>sake, but remember it may not count if attacks </p>
<p>target other parts of the body.</p>
<p>3).Edges.&amp;.Hindrances</p>
<p>• You  gain  additional  points  for  taking  up  to </p>
<p>one  Major  Hindrance  (2  points)  and  two  Minor </p>
<p>Hindrances (1 point each).</p>
<p><b>For 2 points you can:</b></p>
<p>• Gain another attribute point, or</p>
<p>• Choose an Edge</p>
<p><b>For 1 point you can:</b></p>
<p>• Gain another skill point, or</p>
<p>• Increase starting funds by 100%</p>
<p>4).Gear</p>
<p>• Start with $500 unless your setting book </p>
<p>says otherwise.</p>
<p>5).Background.Details</p>
<p>•  Fill  in  any  other  background  details  you </p>
<p>care to add.</p>
<p>Skills</p>
<p><b>Skill ......................................Attribute</b></p>
<p>Boating ................................... Agility</p>
<p>Climbing ............................... Strength</p>
<p>Driving .................................... Agility</p>
<p>Fighting .................................. Agility</p>

<p>Healing .................................. Smarts</p>
<p>Intimidation ..............................Spirit</p>
<p>Investigation .......................... Smarts</p>
<p>Knowledge ............................ Smarts</p>
<p>Lockpicking ............................ Agility</p>
<p>Notice .................................... Smarts</p>
<p>Persuasion ..............................Spirit</p>
<p>Piloting ................................... Agility</p>
<p>Repair.................................... Smarts</p>
<p>Riding ..................................... Agility</p>
<p>Shooting ................................. Agility</p>
<p>Stealth .................................... Agility</p>
<p>Streetwise ............................. Smarts</p>

<p>All Thumbs ................. Minor ..............–2 Repair; Roll of 1 causes malfunction</p>
<p>Anemic....................... Minor ..............–2 to Fatigue tests</p>
<p>Arrogant ..................... Major ..............Must humiliate opponent, challenge the ‘leader’</p>
<p>Bad Eyes .............. Minor/Major .........–2 to attack or notice something more than 5” distant</p>
<p>Bad Luck.................... Major ..............One less Benny per session</p>
<p>Big Mouth .................. Minor ..............Unable to keep a secret, blabs at the worst time</p>
<p>Blind........................... Major ..............–6 to all actions that rely on vision; –2 on social rolls, gain </p>
<p>additional Edge</p>
<p>Bloodthirsty ................ Major ..............Never takes prisoners</p>
<p>Cautious .................... Minor ..............Character is overly careful</p>
<p>Clueless ..................... Major ..............–2 to most Common Knowledge rolls</p>
<p>Code of Honor ........... Major ..............Character keeps his word and acts like a gentleman</p>
<p>Curious ...................... Major ..............Character wants to know about everything</p>
<p>Death Wish ................ Minor ..............Hero wants to die after completing some task</p>
<p>Delusional ............. Minor/Major .........Character suffers from grave delusions</p>
<p>Doubting Thomas ...... Minor ..............Character doesn’t believe in the supernatural</p>
<p>Elderly........................ Major ..............Pace –1, –1 to Strength and Vigor die types; +5 skill points </p>
<p>for any skill linked to Smarts</p>
<p>Enemy .................. Minor/Major .........Character has a recurring nemesis of some sort</p>
<p>Greedy .................. Minor/Major .........Character is obsessed with wealth</p>
<p>Habit ..................... Minor/Major .........</p>
<p>Charisma –1; Fatigue rolls when deprived of Major Habits</p>
<p>Hard of Hearing .... Minor/Major .........–2 to Notice sounds; automatic failure if completely deaf</p>
<p>Heroic ........................ Major ..............Character always helps those in need</p>
<p>Illiterate ...................... Minor ..............Hero is unable to read or write</p>
<p>Lame.......................... Major ..............–2 Pace and running die is a d4</p>
<p>Loyal .......................... Minor ..............The hero tries to never betray or disappoint his friends</p>
<p>Mean.......................... Minor ..............–2 to his Charisma for ill-temper and surliness</p>
<p>Obese ........................ Minor ..............+1 Toughness, –1 Pace, d4 running die</p>
<p>One Arm .................... Major ..............–4 to tasks requiring two arms</p>
<p>One Eye..................... Major ..............–1 Charisma, –2 to rolls requiring depth perception</p>
<p>One Leg ..................... Major ..............Pace –2, d4 running die, –2 to rolls requiring mobility, –2 to </p>
<p>Swimming skill</p>
<p>Outsider ..................... Minor ..............–2 Charisma, treated badly by those of dominant society</p>
<p>Overconfident ............ Major ..............The hero believes he can do anything</p>
<p>Pacifist .................. Minor/Major .........</p>
<p>Character fights only in self-defense as a Minor Hindrance;</p>
<p>won’t harm living creatures as Major Hindrance</p>
<p>Phobia .................. Minor/Major .........–2 or –4 to Trait tests when near the phobia</p>
<p>Poverty ...................... Minor ..............Half starting funds, inability to hang onto future income</p>
<p>Quirk .......................... Minor ..............Character has some minor but persistent foible</p>
<p>Small.......................... Major ..............–1 Toughness</p>
<p>Stubborn .................... Minor ..............Hero always wants his way</p>
<p>Ugly ........................... Minor ..............–2 Charisma due to appearance</p>
<p>Vengeful................ Minor/Major .........Character holds a grudge; will kill as a Major Hindrance</p>
<p>Vow ....................... Minor/Major .........A pledge to a group, deity, or religion</p>
<p>Wanted ................. Minor/Major .........The character is a criminal of some sort</p>
<p>Yellow ........................ Major ..............The character is cowardly and suffers –2 to Fear checks</p>
<p>Young ........................ Major ..............3 points for Attributes, 10 skill points, +1 Benny per session</p>

<p>Power Surge .........................WC, S, arcane skill d10 ........... +2d6 Power Points when dealt a Joker</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--52</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
