<p>with  the <i> bolt</i>  power  and  10  Power  Points,  for </p>
<p>example, could make a ray gun that fires electrical </p>
<p>beams. The gun has 10 Power Points it can use </p>
<p>to fire the beams just like a wizard would cast the </p>
<p><i>bolt</i> spell.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Malfunction:</b>  Weird  science  devices  are </p>
<p>never  perfect  technology.  They  often  suffer </p>
<p>from  spectacular  and  deadly  malfunctions.  If  a </p>
<p>gadgeteer uses a device and rolls a 1 on the skill </p>
<p>die used to activate the gizmo, it has malfunctioned </p>
<p>in some way and does not work. Draw a card and </p>
<p>consult the Malfunction Table below:</p>
<p>Weird.Science.Malfunction.Table</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Clubs—Catastrophic  Malfunction:</b>  The </p>
<p>device explodes for 2d6 damage in a Large </p>
<p>Burst Template.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Hearts—Major  Malfunction:</b>  The  device </p>
<p>breaks  down. The  gadgeteer  may  not  use </p>
<p>it  again  until  it’s  repaired,  which  requires  a </p>
<p>Repair roll and 2d6 hours of work.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Diamonds—Minor Malfunction:</b> The device </p>
<p>suffers a minor hang-up. It can be fixed with </p>
<p>a Repair roll at –2.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Spades—Glitch:</b>  The  gizmo  activates  but </p>
<p>does  the  reverse  of  its  intent. An <i> invisibility</i> </p>
<p>belt makes the caster glow brightly, a weapon </p>
<p>fires at a random target, and so on. If a reverse </p>
<p>effect  makes  no  sense,  treat  it  as  a  Major </p>
<p>Malfunction instead.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>New  Powers:</b>  Each  time  a  Weird  Scientist </p>
<p>takes the New Power Edge, he has invented a </p>
<p>new  gadget.  He  simply  chooses  a  power  and </p>
<p>decides what kind of gizmo it’s contained in as </p>
<p>usual. He can also repeat a power he’s already </p>
<p>taken. A mad scientist might want to create two </p>
<p>ray-guns, for example, so that he can use one and </p>
<p>give one to a companion.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Maintaining  Powers:</b>  Because  weird </p>
<p>scientists use inventions rather than cast spells, </p>
<p>they  don’t  suffer  any  penalties  for  maintaining </p>
<p>powers, but their devices still pay the maintenance </p>
<p>costs in Power Points as usual.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Recharging:</b>  Devices  regain  Power  Points </p>
<p>just like a character, at the rate of one point per </p>
<p>hour. Recharging may represent the device being </p>
<p>plugged into  an outlet, gathering  solar  rays, or </p>
<p>even fritzing out for a while until it miraculously </p>
<p>just  starts  working  again.  Regardless  of  the </p>
<p>description, however, it regains Power Points at </p>
<p>the rate of one per hour just like other power types.</p>
<p>The  Power  Edges  Rapid  Recharge  and </p>
<p>Improved  Rapid  Recharge  apply  to  all  of  the </p>
<p>inventor’s devices rather than the inventor himself. </p>
<p>More.on.Weird.Science</p>
<p>Weird Science is a little more complicated than </p>
<p>other Arcane Backgrounds and requires a bit more </p>
<p>explanation. First off, it’s important to understand </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--121</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p>Weird  Science  isn’t  used  to  make  mundane </p>
<p>devices, even if they are extraordinary. As long as </p>
<p>they’re possible and aren’t too far above the given </p>
<p>tech level of the world, they’re just “high-tech.” </p>
<p>Only actual weird science, inspired by, created </p>
<p>by, or powered by some sort of supernatural force </p>
<p>qualifies.</p>
<p>It’s  also  important  to  remember  that  Weird </p>
<p>Science  doesn’t  allow  a  character  to </p>
<p>make anything he wants. He can </p>
<p>only make a device that utilizes </p>
<p>one of the powers in this book (or </p>
<p>an appropriate Savage Setting).</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Sharing:</b> An  inventor  can </p>
<p>hand  his  device  over  to  a </p>
<p>companion  to  use.  The </p>
<p>device  works  the  same </p>
<p>for  the  companion  as  it </p>
<p>does  for  the  owner.  If  the </p>
<p>Weird Science skill is required, </p>
<p>the  companion  must  make </p>
<p>a </p>
<p>default  roll  as  usual. That  means </p>
<p>gizmos  are  typically  more  effective  when  used </p>
<p>by weird scientists than in the hands of others.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Soul Drain:</b> Weird Scientists cannot take the </p>
<p>Soul Drain Edge.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>More  Power  Points:</b>  When  an  inventor </p>
<p>gains  more  Power  Points,  he’s  assumed </p>
<p>to tinker with his existing devices and </p>
<p>upgrade  them  as  well. This  means </p>
<p><i>all</i> of his devices gain the additional </p>
<p>Power  Points.  In  effect,  if  an </p>
<p>inventor  has  20  Power  Points, </p>
<p>each  of  his  devices  have  20 </p>
<p>Power Points as well.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Losing  Devices:</b>  If  an </p>
<p>inventor’s  gizmo  is  taken  away, </p>
<p>lost,  or  destroyed,  he  can  make </p>
<p>another in 2d6 hours as long as he has </p>
<p>access to a workshop and some basic </p>
<p>components. This  requires  a  Repair  roll. A </p>
<p>raise halves the time needed to create the device.</p>
<p>If the original should somehow be returned, it </p>
<p>no longer functions (the character doesn’t get a </p>
<p>“free” duplicate in this way).</p>
<p><i><b>Example:</b> Doctor Gold starts play with a </i></p>
<p><i>vibroknife (a knife with the </i>smite<i> power) and </i></p>
<p><i>10 Power Points. Later on, he levels up and </i></p>
<p><i>chooses the New Power Edge. With that he </i></p>
<p><i>invents a ray-gun with the </i>bolt<i> power. Both </i></p>
<p><i>devices have 10 Power Points.</i></p>
<p><i>In a fight, Doctor Gold first “turns on” his </i></p>
<p><i>vibroknife by making a Weird Science roll. He </i></p>
<p><i>gets a raise so the knife does +4 damage for </i></p>
<p><i>its duration. The ray-gun doesn’t have to be </i></p>
<p><i>activated. The Doc simply makes a Shooting </i></p>
<p><i>roll  whenever  he  fires  it  (just  like  a  mage </i></p>
<p><i>would make a Spellcasting roll).</i></p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--122</p>
<p>Trappings.&amp;.Effects</p>
<p>Trappings are the heart and soul of the powers </p>
<p>system.  With  just  a  few  simple  twists,  a <i> bolt</i> </p>
<p>power can represent rays of ice, streaks of light, </p>
<p>or swarms of stinging bees.</p>
<p>The powers themselves are designed to be as </p>
<p>simple to use and remember as possible. This </p>
<p>helps the Game Master remember what all the </p>
<p>powers  do,  and  helps  players  remember  the </p>
<p>rules for common powers even between different </p>
<p>settings. But just because these powers work the </p>
<p>same from setting to setting doesn’t mean they </p>
<p>have  to  look  the  same,  have  the  same  names </p>
<p>(to  the  characters  in  that  world),  or  even  have </p>
<p>the <i>exact</i> same effects—that’s where Trappings </p>
<p>come in. </p>
<p>For the most part, Trappings should be merely </p>
<p>cosmetic. But sometimes it makes sense for there </p>
<p>to be additional effects. A heat ray should have a </p>
<p>chance of catching combustible objects on fire, for </p>
<p>example, and an electric blast should do slightly </p>
<p>more damage to targets in full metal armor.</p>
<p>Below  are  examples  of  effects  players  and </p>
<p>Game Masters can use for common Trappings.</p>
<p>Acid</p>
<p>Acid is most commonly an attack Trapping, but </p>
<p>could  be  used  defensively  against  those  who </p>
<p>touch  it  (such  as <i> armor</i>  that  corrodes  anyone </p>
<p>who touches it).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Corrosion:</b>  If  the  subject  with  an  acidic </p>
<p>Trapping  is  touched  the  victim  must  make </p>
<p>a Vigor roll or suffer Fatigue (the equivalent </p>
<p>of  Bumps  and  Bruises).  If  the  ability  is  a </p>
<p>damaging attack that results in a Shaken or </p>
<p>higher result, roll a d6. On a 6, any material </p>
<p>the acid hit is ruined (armor loses a point of </p>
<p>protection instead).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Burn:</b> A  power  that  does  fixed  damage </p>
<p>reduces  its  die  type  by  one,  but  does  one </p>
<p>less  die  of  damage  on  the  caster’s  next </p>
<p>action  unless  counteracted  in  some  way </p>
<p>(taking an action to wash it off or stripping off </p>
<p>the acid-covered item). For instance, a 2 PP </p>
<p>acid <i>bolt</i> causes 3d4 when it hits and 2d4 on </p>
<p>the caster’s action as well (unless the target </p>
<p>neutralizes it with liquid).</p>
<p>Cold/Ice</p>
<p>Cold and ice cause freezing effects, and can be </p>
<p>both positive and negative.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor:</b> Beneficial powers provide +2 Armor </p>
<p>versus cold, ice, fire, and heat, but fire and </p>
<p>heat attacks count as a <i>dispel</i> against them.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fatigue:</b> Harmful powers require a Vigor roll </p>
<p>(at –2 on a raise) to avoid cold-based Fatigue, </p>
<p>but the power’s range is reduced to half (non-</p>
<p>ranged powers have their Power Point cost </p>
<p>doubled).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Skate:</b> A success on a beneficial power (like </p>
<p><i>armor</i>) results in ice not counting as Difficult </p>
<p>Ground as ice spikes or skates form on the </p>
<p>target’s feet.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Slow:</b> A raise with a detrimental power (like </p>
<p><i>stun</i>) results in the target’s movement counting </p>
<p>as Difficult Ground while the power is active </p>
<p>(or his next movement for Instant powers) due </p>
<p>to the slick ice frozen on him.</p>
<p>Darkness</p>
<p>Darkness is frequently tied to another trapping </p>
<p>such  as  cold  or  necromantic,  so  those  options </p>
<p>can apply as well.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Darkening:</b> Targets suffer a penalty to oppose </p>
<p>the  power  equal  to  the  current  darkness </p>
<p>penalty. The  caster  suffers  a  –2  penalty  in </p>
<p>normal  light,  and  the <i> light</i>  power  works  as </p>
<p><i>dispel</i> against the power.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Shroud:</b> The target is momentarily shrouded </p>
<p>in  tendrils  of  darkness. Targets  of  negative </p>
<p>powers suffer a –1 penalty to all vision-based </p>
<p>trait rolls while the power is active or on their </p>
<p>next action for Instant powers. Positive effects </p>
<p>slightly obscure the character, making him –1 </p>
<p>to be hit by ranged attacks.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Stealth:</b>  For  beneficial  powers,  adding  +1 </p>
<p>Power Point to the cost causes the darkness </p>
<p>to cling to the target and increases Stealth by </p>
<p>one die type, or two on a raise.</p>
<p>Electricity</p>
<p>Electricity  has  a  strong  impact  on  the  body’s </p>
<p>nervous and muscular systems.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor Piercing:</b> The electricity arcs to a foe’s </p>
<p>exposed areas, ignoring some armor (AP 2) </p>
<p>at a cost of +1 Power Point. </p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Conduction:</b>  Damaging  powers  reduce </p>
<p>damage by one die type, but add an additional </p>
<p>die  of  damage  to  targets  in  the  following </p>
<p>situations: carrying more than 10 pounds of </p>
<p>conductive metal, contacting a source of water, </p>
<p>or otherwise touching an electrical conductor </p>
<p>of some kind. For instance, an electrical <i>blast</i> </p>
<p>at  maximum  effect  does  3d4  damage  in  a </p>
<p>Large Burst Template, but if the targets are </p>
<p>standing in water, they take 4d4 damage.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Jazz:</b> Beneficial powers “jazz” the target. They </p>
<p>cost +1 Power Point to cast, but on a success </p>
<p>add +2 to Pace and on a raise increase Agility </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--123</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p>one die type for the duration of the power.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Jolt:</b> Helpful powers shock a target out of their </p>
<p>distraction on a raise, providing an immediate </p>
<p>free roll to recover from being Shaken.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Spasms:</b>  Harmful  powers  cause  temporary </p>
<p>muscle  contraction  if  cast  with  a  raise;  the </p>
<p>target  has  to  make  a  Vigor  roll  or  be  at  –2 </p>
<p>Parry until his next action.</p>
<p>Fire/Heat</p>
<p>Fire is a very common trapping for attack powers </p>
<p>with  heat  having  similar  but  less  combustible </p>
<p>effects.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor Piercing:</b> Fire and heat bypass cracks </p>
<p>in armor. A damaging power gains AP 2 by </p>
<p>increasing the base cost by +1 Power Point. </p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Aura:</b> Beneficial powers surround a subject </p>
<p>with a hot or fiery aura, and as a replacement </p>
<p>for their normal benefit on a raise, the target </p>
<p>gains the effect of the <i>damage field</i> power that </p>
<p>causes 2d4 damage.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fatigue:</b> A heat trapping on an attack forces </p>
<p>the victim to make a Vigor roll or suffer Fatigue.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Flammable:</b> With a hit by a fire power, roll for </p>
<p>any potentially flammable objects to catch fire </p>
<p>(see page 101). For a heat trapping, liquids on </p>
<p>the target (water, potions, etc.) evaporate on a </p>
<p>6 on a d6 with a success or a 4–6 on a raise.</p>
<p>Light</p>
<p>Light typically represents goodness, sunshine, </p>
<p>or holiness.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Beam:</b>  Light-based  damaging  attacks  are </p>
<p>like a focused laser, providing armor piercing </p>
<p>capability.  Reduce  the  damage  by  one  die </p>
<p>type, but add AP 4 to the effect.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Enhance:</b> This  trapping  applies  directly  to </p>
<p>the <i>light</i> power. Reduce it to a Medium Burst </p>
<p>Template and extend the duration to 1 hour (1/</p>
<p>hour) or give it a range of Smarts x 2 affecting </p>
<p>animate  targets  as  well  (an  unwilling  target </p>
<p>gets an opposed Agility roll to avoid). Reduce </p>
<p><i>light</i>  to  a  Small  Burst Template  and  give  it </p>
<p>both abilities. </p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Glow:</b>  Subjects  affected  with  a  raise  glow </p>
<p>for  the  duration,  creating  light  in  a  Small </p>
<p>Burst Template centered on them. This can </p>
<p>give them light, but also make them targets. </p>
<p>An  Instant  power  with  that  effect  allows  a </p>
<p>character on Hold or with the Joker to make </p>
<p>an attack for the split second the subject is </p>
<p>illuminated (avoiding any darkness penalties </p>
<p>to  hit  them).  The  character  must  take  his </p>
<p>action immediately after the caster’s turn to </p>
<p>gain the benefit.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Sunlight:</b> In a setting with vampires and other </p>
<p>such creatures, <i>light</i> is equivalent to natural </p>
<p>sunlight.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--124</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Necromantic</p>
<p>Necromantic trappings may involve a “negative </p>
<p>energy” opposed to life or symbols of death like </p>
<p>bones and skulls.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fear:</b>  All  Undead  (depending  on  their </p>
<p>prevalence) are considered to have a level of </p>
<p>Arcane Resistance versus the power, and the </p>
<p>living must make Fear checks when hit with it.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Feign Undeath:</b> A raise on the roll provides a </p>
<p>–1 to be hit by Undead as they see the subject </p>
<p>as one of their own.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Shards:</b> Ranged attacks splinter on impact, </p>
<p>creating shrapnel that does +1 damage versus </p>
<p>unarmored targets but –1 damage versus foes </p>
<p>with Armor.</p>
<p>Sound</p>
<p>Sound is a common trapping for sonic or music-</p>
<p>based spellcasters. Sound-based powers should </p>
<p>never work in a vacuum!</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Absorbtion:</b>  Beneficial  powers  absorb  the </p>
<p>subject’s  sound,  so  Stealth  is  increased  a </p>
<p>die  type,  but  they  have  to  yell  to  be  heard </p>
<p>normally  and  speaking  becomes  a  normal </p>
<p>action instead of a free one.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Aquatic Boom:</b> Sound travels better in water </p>
<p>than  in  air.  Underwater,  an  attack  power </p>
<p>causes +2 damage. In air, however, it causes </p>
<p>–2 damage.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Deafen:</b> A raise with the power (or a Shaken </p>
<p>or better from damage) results in a –2 penalty </p>
<p>to  hearing-based  Notice  rolls  for  the  target </p>
<p>until  the  power  ends  or  they  recover  from </p>
<p>being Shaken.</p>
<p>Design.Note.-.The.Power.of.Names</p>
<p><i>What really makes powers stand out in a </i></p>
<p><i>setting are their names, particularly if they’re </i></p>
<p><i>spells  or  miracles.  Nickodemus’  Necrotic </i></p>
<p><i>Surge sounds  much more frightening  than </i></p>
<p><i>bolt.</i></p>
<p><i>It’s  important  for  official </i> Savage  Worlds </p>
<p><i>books to use the simpler nomenclature for </i></p>
<p><i>ease  of  reference.  We  don’t  want  you  to </i></p>
<p><i>have to look up every power listed under a </i></p>
<p><i>spellcaster’s repertoire after you’ve become </i></p>
<p><i>familiar with the standard powers. You should </i></p>
<p><i>encourage  your  players,  however,  to  use </i></p>
<p><i>more descriptive names.</i></p>
<p><i>If the group in a modern-day horror game </i></p>
<p><i>finds a scroll of </i>armor<i>, that’s probably much </i></p>
<p><i>more rare and exciting than it would be </i></p>
<p><i>in a fantasy game. Give it a name like </i></p>
<p><i>Blessing of the Faithful and then tell </i></p>
<p><i>them  it  works  “just  like  the </i> armor<i> </i></p>
<p><i>spell.” They’ll get the idea and the </i></p>
<p><i>extremely  functional  and  flexible  powers </i></p>
<p><i>system will convey much more flavor and </i></p>
<p><i>excitement.</i></p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--125</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p>Listed below are a number of powers available </p>
<p>in  most  Savage  Settings.  Each  power  has  the </p>
<p>following statistics:</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> This is the Rank a character must be </p>
<p>in order to learn this power: Novice, Seasoned, </p>
<p>Veteran, Heroic, or Legendary.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> The number of points it costs to </p>
<p>use the power. Some powers allow the character </p>
<p>to pay additional points for additional effects. This </p>
<p>is always determined—and paid for—before the </p>
<p>dice are rolled.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Range: </b>The maximum distance the target of </p>
<p>the power can be from the user when the power is </p>
<p>first activated (it remains in effect even if the target </p>
<p>moves out of Range as long as it’s maintained). </p>
<p>A Range of Smarts, for example, means 10” for </p>
<p>a character with a Smarts of d10. If a power lists </p>
<p>three Ranges, such as 12/24/48, these are read </p>
<p>just  like  missile  weapon  Ranges,  and  subtract </p>
<p>the standard penalties for each Range bracket </p>
<p>(0/–2/–4). The arcane character’s skill roll acts as </p>
<p>both his “casting” and attack total for these type </p>
<p>powers (Weird Scientists use Fighting or Shooting </p>
<p>as usual instead).</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b>How long the power lasts in rounds. </p>
<p>A power with a Duration of 1 lasts until the heroes’ </p>
<p>next action. A Duration of 2 means it lasts for two </p>
<p>actions, and so on.</p>
<p>If the Duration of a power has a second entry </p>
<p>in parentheses, such as 3 (1/round), it means the </p>
<p>power has a Duration of 3 rounds and may then </p>
<p>be maintained from round to round by spending </p>
<p>the listed number of Power Points (1 in this case). </p>
<p>Each power maintained subtracts 1 from future </p>
<p>uses of the hero’s arcane skill.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Listed  here  are  some  ideas  for </p>
<p>what the power might look like in different types </p>
<p>of settings. In a science fiction game, <i>armor</i> might </p>
<p>represent the psyker’s telekinetic force pushing </p>
<p>attacks away from him. The same power used by </p>
<p>a superhero might be a force field, or a body of </p>
<p>flame that melts incoming projectiles.</p>
<p><i><b>Example:</b>  Greywald  the  Melodious  is  a </i></p>
<p><i>bard in a high-fantasy setting. In battle, he </i></p>
<p><i>strums his lyre or sings songs to enable his </i></p>
<p><i>powers.</i></p>
<p><i>His </i>burst<i> is a sonic cone that rattles nerves </i></p>
<p><i>and shatters eardrums. He calls this one “The </i></p>
<p><i>Battle Cry of Evanier.” Greywald’s </i>slumber is<i> </i></p>
<p><i>“Lullaby of the Fallen,” a sad mournful tune </i></p>
<p><i>that puts his enemies to sleep even in the </i></p>
<p><i>heat of battle.</i></p>
<p><i>Greywald’s player has decided for himself </i></p>
<p><i>that  he  won’t  take  powers  that  don’t  work </i></p>
<p><i>well within his theme—such as </i>disguise<i> or </i></p>
<p>elemental manipulation.</p>
<p>Armor</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b>3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> A  mystical  glow,  hardened  skin, </p>
<p>ethereal armor, a mass of insects or worms.</p>
<p><i>Armor</i>  creates  a  field  of  magical  protection </p>
<p>around a character or an actual shell of some sort, </p>
<p>effectively giving the target Armor. Success grants </p>
<p>the recipient 2 points of Armor. A raise grants 4 </p>
<p>points of Armor.</p>
<p>Whether  the <i> armor</i>  is  visible  or  not  depends </p>
<p>largely on the trapping.</p>
<p>Banish</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Veteran</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b>Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Holy items, arcane symbols, handful </p>
<p>of salt.</p>
<p>Whether ghosts, elementals, or demons, <i>banish</i> </p>
<p>removes  them  all.  This  power  can  affect  any </p>
<p>creature that is not native to the current plane of </p>
<p>existence (GM’s determination).</p>
<p>This  spell  is  an  opposed  roll  of  the  caster’s </p>
<p>arcane  skill  versus  the  target’s  Spirit.  On  a </p>
<p>success, the target is Shaken. On a raise, it is </p>
<p>sent to its proper plane of existence.</p>
<p>If  the  target  is  a  Wild  Card,  each  casting  of </p>
<p><i>banish</i>  causes  a  wound  instead.  If  the  target </p>
<p>already has three wounds, it is then banished to </p>
<p>its native plane—but it is not slain.</p>
<p>Barrier</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1/section</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1 per section, per round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Fire, ice, thorns, force, bones.</p>
<p><i>Barrier</i> creates a solid, immobile wall to protect </p>
<p>the user against attack or to entrap an opponent.</p>
<p>Regardless of what the <i>barrier</i> is made of (ice, </p>
<p>thorns, stone, energy, etc.), it has a Toughness </p>
<p>of 10. Every Power Point spent creates a 1” wide </p>
<p>section of wall. The <i>barrier</i> ranges in thickness </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--126</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>from a few “real world” inches for stone or other </p>
<p>hard materials up to a foot for things like bones </p>
<p>or ice. (If you’re using a gridded mat to play, draw </p>
<p>the <i>barrier</i> between the squares directly along the </p>
<p>grid-lines.) The exact placement of each section </p>
<p>is defined by the caster, but each section must </p>
<p>be connected to at least one other section after </p>
<p>the first.</p>
<p>When the spell expires or a section is broken, </p>
<p>it crumbles to dust or dissipates. Trappings are </p>
<p>never left behind.</p>
<p>Each section of the <i>barrier</i> may be destroyed by </p>
<p>an attack that equals its Toughness of 10. Physical </p>
<p>walls are treated exactly like inanimate objects; </p>
<p>they are considered to have a Parry of 2 (ranged </p>
<p>attacks work as normal), but raises on the attack </p>
<p>roll do not grant bonus damage nor do damage </p>
<p>dice Ace. Opponents may climb the <i>barrier</i> at –2 to </p>
<p>their Climbing roll if it is made of something solid. </p>
<p>Fiery versions of the barrier cause 2d4 damage </p>
<p>to anyone who wishes to leap through instead.</p>
<p>Beast.Friend</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> Special</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 100 yards</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b>10 minutes</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> The mage concentrates and gestures </p>
<p>with his hands.</p>
<p>This  spell  allows  mages  to  speak  with  and </p>
<p>guide  the  actions  of  nature’s  beasts.  It  works </p>
<p>only  on  creatures  with  animal  intelligence,  not </p>
<p>humanoids. Nor does it work on conjured, magical, </p>
<p>or otherwise “unnatural” animals.</p>
<p>The  target  must  be  within  the  sorcerer’s </p>
<p>range — it is not conjured.</p>
<p>The cost to control a creature depends on its </p>
<p>Size. The base cost is 3, plus twice its Size for </p>
<p>creatures with a Size greater than 0. A great white </p>
<p>shark (Size +4) costs 3 plus 8 (2x4), or 11 points. </p>
<p>A roc (Size +8) costs 19 Power Points to control.</p>
<p>Swarms may also be controlled. Small swarms </p>
<p>cost 3, Mediums 5, and Large 8. Thus a single </p>
<p>rat costs 3 to control, as does a small swarm of </p>
<p>the creatures.</p>
<p>Blast</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2–6</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> 24/48/96</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Balls  of  fire,  ice,  light,  darkness, </p>
<p>colored bolts, swarm of insects.</p>
<p><i>Blast</i> is an area effect power that can put down </p>
<p>many opponents at once. The caster first picks </p>
<p>where he wants to center the <i>blast</i>, then makes </p>
<p>the  appropriate  skill  roll.  Normal  ranged  attack </p>
<p>modifiers apply.</p>
<p>The area of effect is a Medium Burst Template. If </p>
<p>the roll is failed, the <i>blast</i> deviates as a launched </p>
<p>projectile.</p>
<p>Targets within the blast suffer 2d6 damage. <i>Blast </i></p>
<p>counts as a Heavy Weapon.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional  Effects:</b>  For  double  the  Power </p>
<p>Points, the blast does 3d6 damage, <i>or</i> the size </p>
<p>is increased to a Large Burst Template. For triple </p>
<p>the points, it does both.</p>
<p>Blind</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2–6</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> 12/24/48</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Bright  flash  of  light,  sand  in  eyes, </p>
<p>sticky shadows.</p>
<p>This power temporarily blinds a target or targets. </p>
<p>Those affected must make an Agility roll at –2 to </p>
<p>avert their gaze and avoid the effect (at –4 if the </p>
<p>caster got a raise on the attack roll). On a failure, </p>
<p>victims  are  Shaken  and  –2  to  Parry  until  their </p>
<p>next action. If the target rolls a 1 on his Agility die </p>
<p>(regardless of the Wild Die), he’s Shaken and fully </p>
<p>blind until he recovers from being Shaken. Blinded </p>
<p>victims suffer a –6 penalty to all Trait rolls that </p>
<p>require vision and have their Parry reduced to 2.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Effects:</b> For 2 Power Points, the </p>
<p>power affects a single target. For 4 Power Points, </p>
<p>the  power  affects  everyone  in  a  Medium  Burst </p>
<p>Template. For 6 points, it affects everyone in a </p>
<p>Large Burst Template.</p>
<p>Bolt</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1 per missile</p>
<p><b>Range: </b>12/24/48</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b>Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Fire,  ice,  light,  darkness,  colored </p>
<p>bolts, insects.</p>
<p><i>Bolt </i>is a standard attack power of wizards, and </p>
<p>can also be used for ray guns, bursts of energy, </p>
<p>streaks of holy light, and other ranged attacks. </p>
<p>The damage of the <i>bolt </i>is 2d6.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional  Bolts: </b> The  character  may  cast </p>
<p>up to 3 <i>bolts </i>by spending a like amount of Power </p>
<p>Points. The <i>bolts </i>may be spread among targets </p>
<p>as the character chooses. This is rolled just like </p>
<p>fully-automatic weapons fire but without the full-</p>
<p>auto penalty—the character rolls a spellcasting </p>
<p>die for each <i>bolt</i> and compares each to the Target </p>
<p>Number separately. If the caster is a Wild Card, </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--127</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p>he also rolls a Wild Die, which may replace any </p>
<p>of the casting dice.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Damage: </b>The caster may instead </p>
<p>cast a single 3d6 <i>bolt</i> for 2 Power Points. He may </p>
<p>not cast multiple <i>bolts</i> when using this ability.</p>
<p>Boost/Lower.Trait</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b>3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Physical  change,  glowing  aura, </p>
<p>potions.</p>
<p>This power allows a character to increase any </p>
<p>of a target’s Traits by one die type for a standard </p>
<p>success, or by two with a raise. The affected Trait </p>
<p>can exceed d12. Each step over d12 adds +1 to </p>
<p>his Trait total. For example, a raise on someone </p>
<p>who already has a d12 in the affected Trait grants </p>
<p>him d12+2 for the duration of the power.</p>
<p>The  power  can  also  be  used  to  lower  an </p>
<p>opponent’s Trait. This is an opposed roll against </p>
<p>the victim’s Spirit. Success lowers any Trait of the </p>
<p>caster’s choice one step, a raise lowers it two </p>
<p>steps. A Trait cannot be lowered below a d4. </p>
<p>Multiple  castings  stack,  though  the  caster </p>
<p>must  keep  track  of  when  each  casting </p>
<p>expires as usual.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional  Targets:</b>  The  power  may </p>
<p>affect  an  additional  target  for  every  additional </p>
<p>Power  Point  spent,  up  to  a  maximum  of  five </p>
<p>targets. All  targets  share  the  same  effect  and </p>
<p>Trait affected.</p>
<p>Burrow</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 2</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (2/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Dissolving  into  the  earth  and </p>
<p>appearing elsewhere.</p>
<p><i>Burrow</i> allows a mage standing on raw earth </p>
<p>to meld into it. He can remain underground if he </p>
<p>wants in a sort of “limbo” or <i>burrow</i> to anywhere </p>
<p>with a Pace equal to the power’s Range. A mage </p>
<p>with a Smarts of d8 could therefore move up to </p>
<p>16” (32 yards) on the first round, then maintain </p>
<p>the spell and stay submerged for the second and </p>
<p>move another 16”.</p>
<p>A <i>burrowing</i> earth mage can attempt to surprise </p>
<p>a foe (even one who saw him <i>burrow</i>) by making </p>
<p>an opposed Stealth versus Notice roll. If the mage </p>
<p>wins,  he  gains  +2  to  attack  and  damage  that </p>
<p>round, or +4 with a raise. Targets on Hold may </p>
<p>attempt to interrupt the attack as usual.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The power may affect an </p>
<p>additional target for every additional Power Point </p>
<p>spent, up to a maximum of five targets.</p>
<p>Burst</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Cone Template</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> A  shower  of  flames,  light,  or  other </p>
<p>energy.</p>
<p><i>Burst</i> produces a large fan of energy that bathes </p>
<p>its targets in red-hot fire or other damaging energy.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--128</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>When  cast,  place  the  thin  end  of  the  Cone </p>
<p>Template at the character’s front. Targets within </p>
<p>the  template  may  make Agility  rolls  versus  the </p>
<p>caster’s arcane skill roll to avoid the blaze. Those </p>
<p>who fail suffer 2d10 damage. This counts as a </p>
<p>Heavy Weapon.</p>
<p>Confusion</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1 </p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 2</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Hypnotic lights, brief illusions, loud </p>
<p>noises.</p>
<p>Instilling confusion in enemies is a powerful aid </p>
<p>in combat, and this power provides that ability. </p>
<p>On a success, a target must make a Smarts roll </p>
<p>at –2 or be Shaken, and on a raise, the roll is </p>
<p>made at –4.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The character may affect </p>
<p>up to five targets by spending a like amount of </p>
<p>additional Power Points. </p>
<p>Damage.Field</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 4</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (2/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Fiery aura, spikes, electrical field.</p>
<p><i>Damage  field</i>  creates  an  effect  around  a </p>
<p>character  that  deals  damage  to  anyone  who </p>
<p>contacts  them  in  close  combat.  The  damage </p>
<p>affects  any  adjacent  character  who  makes  a </p>
<p>successful attack roll against the subject. It has </p>
<p>no effect on non-adjacent attackers (for example, </p>
<p>Reach or ranged attacks).</p>
<p>If  a  character  with  a <i> damage  field</i>  strikes </p>
<p>someone in unarmed combat, the target takes the </p>
<p>field’s damage plus the character’s Strength die </p>
<p>(Str+2d6). The character may also simply touch </p>
<p>the opponent (+2 to Fighting) and do the field’s </p>
<p>damage  only. A  target  who  is  grappled  suffers </p>
<p>the field’s damage each round on the attacker’s </p>
<p>action;  if  the  attacker  chooses  on  following </p>
<p>rounds  to  actively  damage  the  target,  he  adds </p>
<p>his Strength die to the damage roll as above and </p>
<p>may get a bonus die for a raise.</p>
<p>With a success, the power does 2d6 damage. </p>
<p>With a raise, <i>damage field</i> causes 2d8 damage.</p>
<p>Darksight</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 1 hour (1/hour)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Glowing eyes, dilated pupils, sonic </p>
<p>sight.</p>
<p>Whereas <i>light</i> creates a source of illumination </p>
<p>usable by others, <i>darksight</i> affects only a single </p>
<p>person and can be much more clandestine.</p>
<p>On a success, this spell halves any darkness </p>
<p>penalty for the subject (round down). For example, </p>
<p>a character in Dim (–1) lighting would suffer no </p>
<p>penalty,  and  one  in Pitch  Darkness  (–4)  would </p>
<p>only suffer a –2. On a raise, the spell negates </p>
<p>all darkness penalties up to the maximum of –6.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The character may affect </p>
<p>up to five targets by spending a like amount of </p>
<p>additional Power Points. </p>
<p>Deflection</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Mystical shield, gust of wind, phantom </p>
<p>servant that intercepts the missiles.</p>
<p><i>Deflection</i>  powers  work  in  a  variety  of  ways. </p>
<p>Some  actually  deflect  incoming  attacks,  others </p>
<p>blur the target’s form or produce other illusionary </p>
<p>effects.  The  end  result  is  always  the  same </p>
<p>however — to  misdirect  incoming  melee  and </p>
<p>missile attacks from the user. </p>
<p>With  a  standard  success,  attackers  must </p>
<p>subtract 2 from any Fighting, Shooting, or other </p>
<p>attack rolls directed at the user. A raise increases </p>
<p>the penalty to –4. This also acts as Armor against </p>
<p>area effect weapons.</p>
<p>Detect/Conceal.Arcana</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Sight</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round) or 1 hour (1/hour)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Waving hands, whispered words.</p>
<p><i>Detect/conceal  arcana</i>  allows  a  character </p>
<p>to  sense  supernatural  persons,  objects,  or </p>
<p>effects within sight. This includes invisible foes, </p>
<p>enchantments on people or items, mad science </p>
<p>devices, and so on.</p>
<p>The power can also be reversed to conceal a </p>
<p>single supernatural item, being, or effect. This has </p>
<p>the same cost, but the duration is much longer — 1 </p>
<p>hour with a maintenance cost of 1 per hour. When </p>
<p>used in this way, those who wish to see through </p>
<p>the ruse with <i>detect arcana</i> use their arcane skill </p>
<p>roll  as  an  opposed  roll  against  the  concealer’s </p>
<p>skill (rolled anew each time <i>detect arcana</i> is cast). </p>
<p>The detecting character may only attempt to see </p>
<p>through concealed powers once per fresh casting.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--129</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p>Disguise</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3 – 5</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 10 minutes (1/10 minutes)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Malleable  features,  illusionary </p>
<p>appearance, hair of new form.</p>
<p><i>Disguise</i>  allows  the  character  to  assume  the </p>
<p>appearance (but none of the abilities) of another </p>
<p>person. The base cost is 3 Power Points, plus </p>
<p>1 point per level of Size difference between the </p>
<p>character and the person she is impersonating. </p>
<p>The  character  cannot  emulate  someone  more </p>
<p>than 2 Size levels different from themselves. It </p>
<p>requires a Notice roll at –2 to see through <i>disguise</i> </p>
<p>if  someone  is  familiar  with  the  specific  person </p>
<p>mimicked;  the  penalty  increases  to  –4  with  a </p>
<p>raise. If unfamiliar, the penalties are –4 and –6 </p>
<p>respectively.</p>
<p>Dispel</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Waving hands, whispered words.</p>
<p><i>Dispel</i> allows a hero to negate enemy spells, </p>
<p>miracles, mad science, or super powers. It has </p>
<p>no effect on innate powers, such as a dragon’s </p>
<p>breath or a banshee’s scream. Neither does <i>dispel</i> </p>
<p>work on magic items or permanent enchantments </p>
<p>unless  the  specific  item  or  enchantment  says </p>
<p>otherwise.</p>
<p><i>Dispel</i> can be used on a power already in effect </p>
<p>or to counter an enemy power as it’s being used. </p>
<p>The latter requires the countering mage to be on </p>
<p>Hold and interrupt his foe’s action as usual.</p>
<p>In either case, <i>dispelling</i> the opponent’s power </p>
<p>is an opposed roll of arcane skills. The <i>dispelling</i> </p>
<p>character  suffers  a  –2  modifier  if  the  target </p>
<p>power  is  of  another  type  (magic  vs.  miracles, </p>
<p>superpowers vs. mad science, etc).</p>
<p>Divination</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Heroic</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Self</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 1 minute</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Contact spirits of dead, commune with </p>
<p>deity, demonic interrogation.</p>
<p>This  power  allows  the  caster  to  contact  an </p>
<p>otherworldly being to gain information. Due to the </p>
<p>extraplanar nature of this power, it is very draining </p>
<p>to the caster.</p>
<p>On a success, the caster may ask one question </p>
<p>that can be answered by “Yes,” “No,” or “Possibly” </p>
<p>(if there is no absolute answer). On a raise, the </p>
<p>question may be answered in five words or less </p>
<p>(the GM may allow a longer, more detailed answer </p>
<p>in cryptic form).</p>
<p>The spell’s duration is one minute, during which </p>
<p>the caster may take no other actions or movement. </p>
<p>If the caster is Shaken during that time, he must </p>
<p>make a Smarts roll or the power is disrupted.</p>
<p>If the question relates to a living being (including </p>
<p>beings who may “live” by mystical means such </p>
<p>as  undead,  constructs,  elementals,  etc.),  then </p>
<p>the  arcane  skill  roll  is  opposed  by  their  Spirit. </p>
<p><i>Divination</i>  is  also  opposed  by <i> conceal  arcana</i>. </p>
<p>In  the  case  of <i> conceal  arcana</i>  on  a  being,  the </p>
<p><i>divination</i>  must  first  beat  the <i> conceal  arcana</i>, </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--130</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>and then if successful, the subject may roll Spirit </p>
<p>against the <i>divination</i> result.</p>
<p>Drain.Power.Points</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Heroic</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Prayer, whispered words, gestures.</p>
<p>This  spell  removes  a  spellcaster’s  source  of </p>
<p>power, limiting his ability to cast magic.</p>
<p>The  caster  picks  a  single  target  within  range </p>
<p>and  makes  an  opposed  arcane  skill  roll.  The </p>
<p>caster suffers a –2 modifier if the target power is </p>
<p>of another type (magic vs. miracles, superpowers </p>
<p>vs. mad science, for example).</p>
<p>With a success, he drains 1d6+1 Power Points </p>
<p>from the victim. On a raise, the victim loses 1d8+2 </p>
<p>Power Points. These rolls don’t Ace. Targets with </p>
<p>Arcane  Background:  Weird  Science  lose  the </p>
<p>Power Points from all “gizmos” on their person </p>
<p>equally.</p>
<p>The victim cannot be reduced below zero Power </p>
<p>Points. Drained Power Points are not taken by the </p>
<p>caster — they are simply lost to the victim. Drained </p>
<p>Power Points recharge as normal. The spell works </p>
<p>only on creatures with an Arcane Background — it </p>
<p>has no effect on magic items except those created </p>
<p>through Arcane Background: Weird Science as </p>
<p>noted above.</p>
<p>Elemental.Manipulation</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 2</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> A few simple gestures.</p>
<p>A  character  who  chooses  this  power  can </p>
<p>perform basic “tricks” using the four elements: air, </p>
<p>earth, fire, and water (these elements may vary </p>
<p>depending on the setting). The GM is the final </p>
<p>arbiter on what effects can be performed (nothing </p>
<p>that mimics another power), but some examples </p>
<p>are listed below.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Air:</b> The caster can create lesser air currents </p>
<p>to blow out a candle, fan a flame, lift a skirt, or </p>
<p>cool his body in oppressive heat (+1 to a single </p>
<p>Fatigue roll caused by heat).</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Earth:</b> A wave of the hand can open a one-foot </p>
<p>square hole in soft earth (or half that in stone), </p>
<p>or  cause  a  spray  of  sand  that  might  blind  an </p>
<p>opponent (+1 to a Trick roll).</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Fire:</b> The caster can snap his fingers to create </p>
<p>a small flame (about the size of a hot match). With </p>
<p>existing fire, he can urge it to spread (+1 to see if a </p>
<p>fire spreads), cause it to flare (perhaps as part of a </p>
<p>Trick maneuver), or slowly light an object over the </p>
<p>course of a few rounds (as if holding a match to it).</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Water:</b> The caster can conjure up to a pint </p>
<p>of water somewhere within his sight (not “inside” </p>
<p>objects or people). A wave of his hand also purifies </p>
<p>one  gallon  of  water,  whether  it  be  poisoned  or </p>
<p>simply salt-water. Those who have been poisoned </p>
<p>within the last minute also get a second chance </p>
<p>to resist any remaining effects.</p>
<p>Entangle</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2 – 4</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Special</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Glue bomb, vines, handcuffs, webs.</p>
<p>This power allows the character to restrain a </p>
<p>target with snaking vines, lengths of hair, spider </p>
<p>webs, or some other vine-like trapping.</p>
<p>The arcane skill roll is opposed by the target’s </p>
<p>Agility. Success indicates partial restraint so that </p>
<p>the target suffers a –2 penalty to Pace and skills </p>
<p>linked  to Agility  and  Strength. A  raise  restrains </p>
<p>the target fully. He cannot move or use any skills </p>
<p>linked to Agility or Strength.</p>
<p>Each following action, an <i>entangled</i> target may </p>
<p>make a Strength or Agility roll to break free. Other </p>
<p>characters may also attempt to free the ensnared </p>
<p>person by making a Strength roll at –2. </p>
<p>For 2 Power Points <i>entangle</i> targets a single </p>
<p>opponent. For 4 points it affects everyone in a </p>
<p>Medium Burst Template.</p>
<p>Environmental.Protection</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 1 hour (1/hour)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> A mark on the forehead, potions, gills.</p>
<p>Adventurers  sometimes  travel  beneath  the </p>
<p>waves, in space, or other hazardous environments. </p>
<p>This  power  protects  them  from  the  crushing </p>
<p>depths or blazing sun as they do.</p>
<p>This power allows the target to breathe, speak, </p>
<p>and move at his normal Pace while in one normally </p>
<p>harmful  environment,  such  as  underwater,  a </p>
<p>zero-G vacuum, the lava of a volcano, or even </p>
<p>the heat of the sun. Pressure, atmosphere, air, </p>
<p>etc, are all provided for.</p>
<p>The power does not protect against attacks with </p>
<p>similar trappings though. A fire attack still causes </p>
<p>normal damage, for example. With a raise on the </p>
<p>casting  roll,  maintaining  the  power  becomes  1 </p>
<p>Power Point per two hours.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--131</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The character may affect </p>
<p>up to five targets by spending a like amount of </p>
<p>additional Power Points. </p>
<p>Farsight</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Invisibly  marked  targets,  guiding </p>
<p>winds, eagle eyes.</p>
<p>This spell endows the recipient to see over great </p>
<p>distances. With a success, ranged penalties are </p>
<p>halved for the subject (–1 at Medium and –2 at </p>
<p>Long). If a raise is achieved, all range increments </p>
<p>for the subject are doubled in addition (12/24/48 </p>
<p>becomes 24/48/96).</p>
<p>Fear</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 2</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Gestures, eldritch energy, cold chills.</p>
<p>This  power  causes  the  target  overwhelming </p>
<p>dread and horror. The area of effect is the Large </p>
<p>Burst  Template.  Every  creature  beneath  the </p>
<p>template must make a Fear check, at –2 if the </p>
<p>caster got a raise. Wild Cards who fail roll on the </p>
<p>Fear Table. Extras are Panicked instead.</p>
<p>Fly</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Veteran</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3/6</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Gusty winds, wings, broomsticks.</p>
<p><i>Fly</i> allows a character to fly at his basic Pace </p>
<p>with a Climb of 0. He may double his Pace by </p>
<p>spending twice the number of Power Points.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The character may affect </p>
<p>up to five targets by spending a like amount of </p>
<p>additional Power Points. </p>
<p>Greater.Healing</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Veteran</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 10/20</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--132</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Laying on hands, touching the victim </p>
<p>with a holy symbol, praying, giving a drink of water.</p>
<p><i>Greater  healing</i>  restores  wounds  more  than </p>
<p>one hour old. This use of the power requires 10 </p>
<p>Power Points and otherwise works exactly like the </p>
<p><i>healing</i> power. It can also be used to neutralize </p>
<p>any poison, disease, or sickness.</p>
<p><i>Greater  healing</i>  can  also  heal  Permanent </p>
<p>Crippling Injuries. This requires an arcane skill roll </p>
<p>at –4, 1d6 hours of time, and 20 Power Points. </p>
<p>Only one casting is permitted per injury — if it fails, </p>
<p>the injury really is permanent.</p>
<p>Growth/Shrink</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2+</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (2/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Gestures, words of power, potions.</p>
<p><i>Growth</i> doubles the overall size of the target. </p>
<p>The subject gains +1 Size for each 2 Power Points </p>
<p>invested when the spell is cast. Each step of Size </p>
<p>grants the target a one-step increase to Strength </p>
<p>and a point of Toughness. This spell may be cast </p>
<p>multiple  times  on  the  same  target,  though  the </p>
<p>caster must track each casting separately.</p>
<p><i>Shrink</i> reduces the Size of the subject by one </p>
<p>step for each 2 Power Points, down to a minimum </p>
<p>of  Size  –2  (approximately  the  size  of  a  rat). </p>
<p>Each level of Size reduction reduces the target’s </p>
<p>Strength by one die type (minimum of d4) and his </p>
<p>Toughness by 1 (minimum of 2).</p>
<p>Subjects  from  Size  +4  to  +7  have  the  Large </p>
<p>ability and fill a 2” square on the table-top. From </p>
<p>Size  +8 to  +10,  they are  Huge  and  occupy an </p>
<p>area 3” square. If the target is +11 or more, he is </p>
<p>considered Gargantuan and occupies a 4” square </p>
<p>area. Creatures of Size –2 have the Small ability. </p>
<p>For unwilling targets, the caster’s arcane skill </p>
<p>roll is opposed by their Spirit.</p>
<p>Havoc</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2 – 4</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 2</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Whirlwind,  chaotic  poltergeists, </p>
<p>repulsion field.</p>
<p>While unpredictable, this spell allows a wizard to </p>
<p>change the field of battle in an instant as targets </p>
<p>are thrown in every direction.</p>
<p>With  a  success,  the  caster  places  a  Medium </p>
<p>Burst  Template  anywhere  within  range. Any </p>
<p>character  touched  by  the  template  must  make </p>
<p>a Strength roll (at –2 if the caster gets a raise). </p>
<p>Any target that fails is knocked 2d6” in a random </p>
<p>direction (roll a d12 and read the result as a clock </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--133</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p>facing) and becomes prone. If the target strikes </p>
<p>an inanimate object, he is Shaken as well. Targets </p>
<p>with cover may subtract the cover modifier from </p>
<p>the  total  distance  moved  (to  a  minimum  of  0), </p>
<p>and flying targets suffer an additional –2 to their </p>
<p>Strength roll. Additionally, roll a d6 to see if the </p>
<p>flyer is moved toward the ground (1 – 2), stays level </p>
<p>(3 – 4), or is moved away from the ground (5 – 6).</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional  Effects:</b>  For  double  the  Power </p>
<p>Points, <i>havoc</i> affects a Large Burst Template.</p>
<p>Healing</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Laying on hands, touching the victim </p>
<p>with a holy symbol, prayer.</p>
<p><i>Healing</i> repairs recent bodily damage. It must </p>
<p>be used within the “Golden Hour,” though, for it </p>
<p>has no effect on wounds more than one hour old.</p>
<p>For Wild Cards, each use of the <i>healing</i> spell </p>
<p>removes a wound with a success, two with a raise. </p>
<p>The  roll  suffers  a  penalty  equal  to  the  victim’s </p>
<p>wounds (in addition to any the caster might be </p>
<p>suffering himself). </p>
<p> For Extras, the GM must first determine if the </p>
<p>ally is dead (see Aftermath on page 88). If so, no </p>
<p>healing  may be  attempted.  If not,  a successful </p>
<p>arcane  skill  roll  returns  the  ally  to  the  game </p>
<p>Shaken.</p>
<p><i>Healing</i>  can  also  cure  poison  and  disease  if </p>
<p>used within 10 minutes of the event.</p>
<p>Intangibility</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Heroic</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (2/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Ghost form, body of shadow, gaseous </p>
<p>transformation.</p>
<p>With  a  successful  arcane  skill  roll,  the  user </p>
<p>becomes incorporeal. He is unable to affect the </p>
<p>physical world, and it in turn cannot affect him. </p>
<p>He  can  travel  through  walls,  and  non-magical </p>
<p>weapons  pass  straight  through  him. Any  items </p>
<p>carried at the time of casting are also incorporeal.</p>
<p>While incorporeal, the mage may affect other </p>
<p>incorporeal  beings  (including  himself),  and  he </p>
<p>is  still  susceptible  to  magic  attacks,  including </p>
<p>physical powers, such as <i>bolt</i>, and magic items. </p>
<p>The character may not become corporeal while </p>
<p>within someone or something. If that occurs, the </p>
<p>caster is instantly shunted to the nearest open </p>
<p>space, and he is Shaken.</p>
<p>Invisibility</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Self</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Powder, potion, iridescent lights.</p>
<p>Being invisible is a powerful aid in combat and </p>
<p>useful  for  spying  on  maidens’  changing  rooms </p>
<p>as well. </p>
<p>With a success, the character is transparent, but </p>
<p>a vague outline is visible. A character may detect </p>
<p>the invisible presence if he has a reason to look </p>
<p>and makes a Notice roll at –4. Once detected, he </p>
<p>may attack the foe at –4 as well. With a raise, the </p>
<p>character is completely invisible. The penalty to </p>
<p>Notice or hit him is –6. </p>
<p>In either case, the power affects the character </p>
<p>and his personal items. Anything picked up after </p>
<p>the power was cast remains visible.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The character may affect </p>
<p>up to five targets by spending a like amount of </p>
<p>additional Power Points. </p>
<p>Light/Obscure</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points: </b>2</p>
<p><b>Range: </b>Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b> 30  minutes  (1/10  minutes)  or  3  (1/</p>
<p>round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings: </b>Illusionary torch, sunlight, darkness, </p>
<p>thick fogs.</p>
<p>The ability to affect visibility (create or remove </p>
<p>obscurement) is a pretty simple but very effective </p>
<p>power.</p>
<p><i>Light/obscure </i> can  be  cast  on  an  inanimate </p>
<p>object,  but  if  the  item  is  in  an  opponent’s </p>
<p>possession,  the  arcane  skill  roll  is  opposed  by </p>
<p>Agility.</p>
<p><i>Light </i> negates  any  darkness/obscurement </p>
<p>penalty  up  to  –6  in  an  area  equal  to  a  Large </p>
<p>Burst Template  for  30  minutes  (1/10  minutes). </p>
<p>The reverse of the power, <i>obscure,</i> creates a –6 </p>
<p>obscurement penalty of the same size lasting for </p>
<p>3 (1/round).</p>
<p>Mind.Reading</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points: </b>3</p>
<p><b>Range: </b>Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration: </b>1</p>
<p><b>Trappings: </b>Psionic invasion, soulsight.</p>
<p>Mind  reading  allows  a  character  to  read </p>
<p>another’s  thoughts.  This  is  an  opposed  roll </p>
<p>versus the target’s Smarts. A success allows the </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--134</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>character  to  gain  one  truthful  answer  from  the </p>
<p>subject. The target is aware of the mental intrusion </p>
<p>unless the mind reader gets a raise. The GM may </p>
<p>apply  modifiers  based  on  the  subject’s  mental </p>
<p>Hindrances or current state of mind.</p>
<p>Pummel</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Cone Template</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Rippling  earth,  buffeting  winds, </p>
<p>rushing waters.</p>
<p><i>Pummel</i>  allows  a  character  to  knock  down </p>
<p>multiple foes. The caster makes an arcane skill </p>
<p>roll and then places a Cone Template in front of </p>
<p>him. Any friend or foe touched by the template </p>
<p>must  make  a  Strength  roll  (at  –2  if  the  caster </p>
<p>gets a raise). Any target that fails is knocked back </p>
<p>2d6” and becomes prone. If the target strikes an </p>
<p>inanimate object, he is Shaken as well. Targets </p>
<p>with cover may subtract the cover modifier from </p>
<p>the  total  distance  moved  (to  a  minimum  of  0), </p>
<p>and flying targets suffer an additional –2 to their </p>
<p>Strength roll.</p>
<p>Puppet</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Veteran</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Glowing  eyes,  trance-like  state,  a </p>
<p>swinging pocket watch, voodoo dolls.</p>
<p>Sometimes  it  pays  to  persuade  others  to  do </p>
<p>your  fighting  for  you.  Some  do  this  by  blatant </p>
<p>mind control, others do it by manufacturing visual </p>
<p>and auditory illusions. <i>Puppet</i> is an opposed roll </p>
<p>of the character’s arcane skill versus the target’s </p>
<p>Spirit. The user must score a success and beat the </p>
<p>target’s roll to gain complete control. The victim will </p>
<p>attack friends and even commit suicide, though </p>
<p>such acts allow the victim another opposed Spirit </p>
<p>roll to break the spell.</p>
<p>Quickness</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 4</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (2/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Blurred motion, hyperactivity.</p>
<p>This  power  grants  incredible  swiftness  to </p>
<p>the  recipient.  With  success  the  target  has  two </p>
<p>separate  turns  per  round  on  his  action  card </p>
<p>instead of the usual one. Each turn is handled </p>
<p>independently  with  its  own  actions,  but  the </p>
<p>character must resolve one turn entirely before </p>
<p>beginning the second. With a raise, the recipient </p>
<p>can redraw any initiative cards lower than Eight </p>
<p>each round.</p>
<p>Shape.Change</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Special</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> Special</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Self</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 1 minute (1/minute)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> “Morphing,” talismans, tattoos.</p>
<p>Many  cultures  have  legends  of  shamans  or </p>
<p>wizards who take on the shape of animals. This </p>
<p>power does just that. This version of the power </p>
<p>only  allows  a  user  to  transform  into  mundane </p>
<p>animals,  but  more  bizarre  transmutations  may </p>
<p>be found.</p>
<p>A character may learn this spell while of Novice </p>
<p>Rank but cannot transform into the more powerful </p>
<p>creatures until he attains the appropriate Rank. </p>
<p>The cost in Power Points depends on the type </p>
<p>of creature the character wishes to change into. </p>
<p>Use the Shape Change table as a guideline for </p>
<p>unlisted creatures. </p>
<p>Weapons  and  other  personal  effects  are </p>
<p>assumed  into  the  animal’s  form  and  reappear </p>
<p>when  the  power  ends,  but  other  objects  are </p>
<p>dropped. </p>
<p>While  transformed,  the  character  retains  his </p>
<p>own Smarts, Spirit, and linked skills (though he </p>
<p>may  not  be  able  to  use  them  since  he  cannot </p>
<p>speak). He gains the animal’s Agility, Strength, </p>
<p>and linked skills and cannot use most devices. </p>
<p>He has no capacity for speech and cannot use </p>
<p>powers,  though  he  may  continue  to  maintain </p>
<p>powers previously activated. Vigor is the higher </p>
<p>of the caster’s or the creature’s.</p>
<p>The GM has final say on what an animal can and </p>
<p>cannot do. A shaman in dog-form might be able </p>
<p>to pull the trigger on a shotgun, for instance, but </p>
<p>would use a default skill roll of d4–2 as the animal </p>
<p>has no Shooting score of its own. The shaman’s </p>
<p>Persuasion functions normally, but might suffer a </p>
<p>–4 or worse penalty without speech, depending </p>
<p>on what he tries to accomplish.</p>
<p>Shape.Change</p>
<p><b> </b></p>
<p><b>Cost </b></p>
<p><b>Rank </b></p>

<p> </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Legendary </p>
<p>Dragon</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--135</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p>Slow</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 2</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (2/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Tying  a  knot  in  a  piece  of  string, </p>
<p>slowing time, distracting invisible ghost monkey.</p>
<p>Skilled fighters and monsters with fast reflexes </p>
<p>can strike before lesser beings have time to blink. </p>
<p>Slowing their reflexes reduces their advantage.</p>
<p>The caster makes an arcane skill roll opposed </p>
<p>by the target’s Spirit. With a success, movement </p>
<p>becomes  an  action,  giving  the  target  a  multi-</p>
<p>action penalty if he wants to move and act in the </p>
<p>same round. With a raise, the target must redraw </p>
<p>initiative cards above 10, except Jokers.</p>
<p>A  victim  who  usually  draws  multiple  initiative </p>
<p>cards discards only those with a value higher than </p>
<p>the spell allows.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The character may affect </p>
<p>up to five targets by spending a like amount of </p>
<p>additional Power Points. </p>
<p>Slumber</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts x 2</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 1 minute (1/minute)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> A lullaby, blowing powder or sand at </p>
<p>targets.</p>
<p>Blasting  a  hoard  of  enemies  into  tiny  pieces </p>
<p>may be popular with some mages, but those who </p>
<p>favor stealth or have a pacifistic bent are drawn </p>
<p>to this spell.</p>
<p>The caster picks where he wants to center the </p>
<p>spell and places a Medium Burst Template. He </p>
<p>then makes an arcane skill roll. Any living creature </p>
<p>(not undead or constructs) within the area must </p>
<p>make a Spirit roll, at –2 if the caster scored a raise. </p>
<p>Those who fail fall asleep. </p>
<p>Loud noises awaken the sleepers as if they were </p>
<p>a normal sleeper (Notice roll). When the duration </p>
<p>expires, the sleepers naturally wake up.</p>
<p>Smite</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> A colored glow, runes, sigils, crackling </p>
<p>energy, barbs grow from the blade.</p>
<p>This power is cast on a weapon of some sort. If it’s </p>
<p>a ranged weapon, it affects one entire magazine, </p>
<p>20 bolts, shells, or arrows, or one full “load” of </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--136</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>ammunition  (the  GM  may  have  to  determine </p>
<p>the exact quantity for unusual weapons). While </p>
<p>the  spell  is  in  effect,  the  weapon’s  damage  is </p>
<p>increased by +2 or +4 with a raise.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Additional Targets:</b> The character may affect </p>
<p>up to five targets by spending a like amount of </p>
<p>additional Power Points. </p>
<p>Speak.Language</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 10 minutes (1/10 minutes)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Words, pictures, hand motions.</p>
<p>This power allows a character to speak, read, </p>
<p>and  write  a  language  other  than  his  own. The </p>
<p>language  must  be  of  an  advanced  form — not </p>
<p>animalistic. A raise on the arcane skill roll allows </p>
<p>the user to project a particular dialect as well.</p>
<p>Speed</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Blurred motion, “floating,” acrobatics.</p>
<p>Warriors  who  need  to  close  with  their  foes </p>
<p>quickly  often  use  this  power,  as  do  those  who </p>
<p>sometimes need to outrun things Man Was Not </p>
<p>Meant to Know. <i>Speed</i> allows the target of the </p>
<p>power to move faster than usual. With a success, </p>
<p>the recipient’s basic Pace is doubled. With a raise, </p>
<p>running becomes a free action, so he may ignore </p>
<p>the usual –2 running penalty.</p>
<p>Stun</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> 12/24/48</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Special</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b> Bolts of energy, stun bombs, sonic </p>
<p>booms, burst of blinding light.</p>
<p><i>Stun</i>  shocks  those  within  a  Medium  Burst </p>
<p>Template  with  concussive  force,  sound,  light, </p>
<p>magical energy, or the like.</p>
<p>If the arcane character scores a success, targets </p>
<p>within the  area  of  effect must  make  Vigor  rolls </p>
<p>or be Shaken. With a raise, victims must make </p>
<p>Vigor rolls at –2.</p>
<p>Succor</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 1</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Touch</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> Instant</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Prayer,  laying  on  hands,  curative </p>
<p>tonic.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--137</p>
<p>Powers</p>
<p><i>Succor</i> removes one Fatigue level, two with a </p>
<p>raise. It can also remove a character’s Shaken </p>
<p>status.</p>
<p><i>Succor</i> may be used to restore consciousness </p>
<p>to  those  who  have  been  Incapacitated  due  to </p>
<p>wounds  as  well,  though  the  wounds  remain.  It </p>
<p>does not stop bleeding or otherwise stop mortal </p>
<p>wounds from worsening, however.</p>
<p>Summon.Ally</p>
<p><b>Rank:</b> Novice</p>
<p><b>Power Points:</b> 3+</p>
<p><b>Range:</b> Smarts</p>
<p><b>Duration:</b> 3 (1/round)</p>
<p><b>Trappings:</b>  Call  elemental,  ghostly  dog, </p>
<p>dimensional double.</p>
<p>This power allows the character to summon a </p>
<p>loyal  and  obedient  servant.  On  a  success,  the </p>
<p>ally is placed at any point within the range of the </p>
<p>power. On a raise, the ally is more durable and </p>
<p>gains  the  Hardy  ability. A  summoned  ally  acts </p>
<p>on the initiative card of the caster and gets an </p>
<p>immediate action as soon as it is summoned.</p>
<p>All Allies are Extras, even Mirror Selves (see </p>
<p>below).</p>
<p>A character may learn this spell while of Novice </p>
<p>Rank, but he cannot summon more powerful allies </p>
<p>until he attains the appropriate Rank. The cost </p>
<p>in Power Points depends on the type of ally the </p>
<p>character wishes to summon. Use the Summon </p>
<p>Ally table as a guideline for unlisted creatures.</p>
<p>A  caster  of  sufficient  Rank  to  summon  more </p>
<p>powerful allies may instead choose to summon </p>
<p>additional lower Rank allies instead at the same </p>
<p>cost. For each decrease in Rank, he gains one </p>
<p>additional  ally.  For  example,  a  Veteran  caster </p>
<p>could  spend  5  Power  Points  to  summon  one </p>
<p>Veteran-Rank-allowed ally, two Seasoned-Rank-</p>
<p>allowed  allies,  or  three  Novice-Rank-allowed </p>
<p>allies. Allies summoned by a single casting must </p>
<p>all be of the same type.</p>
<p>See the Bestiary for statistics of some of the </p>
<p>creatures listed below.</p>

<p>Bodyguard</p>

<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +4:</b> Stone skin.</p>
<p>•	</p>

<p>no  additional  damage  from  called  shots; </p>
<p>constructs  do  not  suffer  from  poison  or </p>
<p>disease.</p>

<p>•	</p>
