<p>Kraken, leviathan</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Minimum  Toughness:</b>  Normal  creatures </p>
<p>have  a  minimum  Toughness  of  2  regardless </p>
<p>of  modifiers.  Only  insects  and  the  like  have </p>
<p>Toughness scores of 1.</p>
<p>Small/Large/Huge</p>
<p>Creatures  the  size  of  rats  or  pixies  are  very </p>
<p>difficult to hit, especially when moving. Assuming </p>
<p>such a creature is active, attackers subtract 2 from </p>
<p>any attack rolls directed at it.</p>
<p>Large creatures, at least the size of a rhino, are </p>
<p>somewhat easier to hit. Attackers may add +2 to </p>
<p>any attack rolls directed at Large targets. Truly </p>
<p>Huge creatures, at least as big as a dragon, are </p>
<p>+4 to be hit.</p>
<p>This  ability  is  both  cumulative  and  relative, </p>
<p>meaning  the  inverse  of  the  modifier  applies  to </p>
<p>attacks made <i>by</i> the creature. So if an elephant </p>
<p>strikes at a human, it subtracts 2 from its roll, but </p>
<p>if attacking another elephant, the modifiers negate </p>
<p>each other.</p>
<p>Strength</p>
<p>Strength  is  a Trait,  not  a  special  ability,  but </p>
<p>because very large creatures exceed the normal </p>
<p>human  range  of  d4  to  d12,  you  might  need  a </p>
<p>little  more  information  when  creating  your  own </p>
<p>creatures.</p>
<p>Creatures of human or lesser Strength should </p>
<p>be expressed as a d4 through a d12, as you think </p>
<p>appropriate. Stronger creatures, such as gorillas, </p>
<p>ogres, and so on, have a d12 plus a bonus. The </p>
<p>bonus depends on how strong the creature is and </p>
<p>how well it can use that strength in combat. Just </p>
<p>as  with  humans,  there  is  variation  within  each </p>
<p>species, however. A mother gorilla may have a </p>
<p>Strength of d12+1, while her much larger mate </p>
<p>has a Strength of d12+3.</p>
<p>Here’s a quick comparison to help you figure </p>
<p>out what Strength creatures of your own creation </p>
<p>should have.</p>
<p>Creature.Strength</p>
<p><b> </b></p>
<p><b>Creature </b></p>
<p><b>Strength</b></p>
<p> </p>
<p>Gorilla, bear, ogre </p>
<p>d12+1 to +3</p>
<p> </p>
<p>Rhino, great white </p>
<p>d12+3 to +6</p>
<p> </p>
<p>Elephant, drake, T-Rex </p>
<p>d12+5 to +8</p>
<p> </p>
<p>Dragon </p>
<p>d12+9 to +12</p>
<p>Stun</p>
<p>A creature with this ability often has an electrical </p>
<p>attack, mild toxin, mind lash, or similar trapping. </p>
<p>When it successfully hits a character (even if it </p>
<p>causes no damage), the victim must make a Vigor </p>
<p>roll minus any listed penalties or be Shaken. He </p>
<p>cannot attempt to recover from being Shaken for </p>
<p>1d6 rounds.</p>
<p>Undead</p>
<p>Zombies, skeletons, and similar Undead horrors </p>
<p>are particularly difficult to destroy. Below are the </p>
<p>benefits of being such an abomination.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Undead add +2 to their basic Toughness.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Undead add +2 when attempting to recover </p>
<p>from being Shaken.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Undead don’t suffer additional damage from </p>
<p>called shots.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Undead Wild Cards never suffer from Wound </p>
<p>Modifiers.</p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Undead do not suffer from disease or poison.</p>
<p>Wall.Walker</p>
<p>Some creatures have the ability to walk on walls. </p>
<p>These creatures only make Climbing rolls in the </p>
<p>most adverse and stressful situations—otherwise </p>
<p>they  automatically  walk  on  vertical  or  inverted </p>
<p>surfaces just as a human walks on the earth.</p>
<p>A Wall Walker’s Pace when walking on walls </p>
<p>is  its  standard  movement  rate.  It  may  run  as </p>
<p>usual when walking on walls unless the specific </p>
<p>creature’s text says otherwise.</p>
<p>Weakness</p>
<p>Some  creatures  suffer  additional  damage  or </p>
<p>other effects when attacked by their Weakness. </p>
<p>A creature made of ice, for example, might take </p>
<p>double damage from fire. A vampire suffers from </p>
<p>a Weakness to sunlight, causing it to catch fire </p>
<p>and burn when exposed to its rays.</p>
<p>See the creature’s description for the particular </p>
<p>effects of its Weakness.</p>
<p>Some  creatures  can  only  be  killed  by  their </p>
<p>Weakness. They may feel pain or even become </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--156</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Shaken from other attack types, but only suffer </p>
<p>wounds  when  struck  by  their  Weakness. A </p>
<p>vampire,  for  instance,  ignores  wounds  from </p>
<p>swords and bullets, but suffers damage normally </p>
<p>if hit in the heart with a wooden stake.</p>
<p>Bestiary</p>
<p>Below is a sampling of some common animals </p>
<p>and monsters common to many Savage Settings. </p>
<p>Note  that  for  some  creatures,  Smarts  is  listed </p>
<p>relative to the animal world, and is thus followed by </p>
<p>an (A) to remind you that this is animal intelligence, </p>
<p>not people intelligence, so don’t expect a dolphin </p>
<p>to drive off in your tank just because it’s a <i>relatively</i> </p>
<p>smart animal. Creatures with animal intelligence </p>
<p>do  not  typically Advance  as Allies—this  only </p>
<p>happens if the animal is gained via an Edge.</p>
<p>Alligator/Crocodile</p>
<p>Alligators  and  crocs  are </p>
<p>staples  of  most  pulp-genre </p>
<p>adventure </p>
<p>games.  The </p>
<p>statistics  here  represent  an </p>
<p>average  specimen  of  either </p>
<p>species. Much larger versions </p>
<p>are often found in more remote </p>
<p>areas.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d4, Smarts d4 (A), Spirit d6, </p>
<p>Strength d10, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Notice d6, Swimming d8</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 3; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 9 (2)</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +2:</b> Thick skin.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Aquatic:</b> Pace 5.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str+d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Rollover:</b> Both gators and crocs are notorious </p>
<p>for grasping their prey in their vice-like jaws </p>
<p>and  rolling  over  and  over  with  their  flailing </p>
<p>victims in their mouth. If one of these large </p>
<p>amphibians hits with a raise, it causes an extra </p>
<p>2d4 rollover damage to its prey in addition to </p>
<p>its regular Strength damage.</p>
<p>Bear,.Large</p>
<p>Large bears covers grizzlies, </p>
<p>kodiaks,  and  massive  polar </p>
<p>bears.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts </p>
<p>d6  (A),  Spirit  d8,  Strength </p>
<p>d12+4, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Fighting  d8,  Notice  d8, </p>
<p>Swimming d6</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 8; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 10</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bear  Hug:</b>  Bears  don’t  actually  “hug”  their </p>
<p>victims, but they do attempt to use their weight </p>
<p>to pin their prey and rend it with their claws and </p>
<p>teeth. A bear that hits with a raise has pinned </p>
<p>his  foe. The  opponent  may  only  attempt  to </p>
<p>escape the “hug” on his action, which requires </p>
<p>a raise on an opposed Strength roll.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws:</b> Str+d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +2:</b> These creatures can stand up to 8’ </p>
<p>tall and weigh over 1000 pounds.</p>
<p>Bull</p>
<p>B u l l s  </p>
<p>a r e  </p>
<p>u s u a l l y  </p>
<p>o n l y </p>
<p>aggressive  toward  humans </p>
<p>when enraged. Of course, if </p>
<p>you’re looking up the statistics </p>
<p>here,  it’s  probably  already </p>
<p>seeing red.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts </p>
<p>d4  (A),  Spirit  d8,  Strength  d12+2, </p>

<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Horns:</b> Str+d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Gore:</b>  Bulls  charge  maneuver  to  gore  their </p>
<p>opponents with their long horns. If they can </p>
<p>move at least 6” before attacking, they add </p>
<p>+4 to their damage total.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +2:</b> Bulls are large creatures.</p>
<p>Cat,.Small</p>
<p>This is an ordinary house cat, the </p>
<p>sort that might be a familiar for </p>
<p>a spellcaster, a Beast Master’s </p>
<p>animal friend, or an alternate </p>
<p>form  for  the <i> shape  change</i> </p>
<p>power.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d6 (A), Spirit d10, Strength d4, </p>

<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Acrobat:</b> +2 to Agility rolls to perform acrobatic </p>
<p>maneuvers; +1 to Parry if unencumbered.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite/Claw:</b> Str.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Low Light Vision:</b> Cats ignore penalties for </p>
<p>Dim and Dark lighting.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size  –2:</b>  Cats  are  typically  less  than  a  foot </p>
<p>high. </p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Small: </b>Attackers subtract 2 from their attacks </p>
<p>to hit.</p>

<p>Bestiary</p>
<p>Dire.Wolf</p>
<p>Dire  wolves  are  very  large </p>
<p>and  feral  wolves  often  used </p>
<p>by orcs as attack dogs. They </p>
<p>may also be found roaming in </p>
<p>packs in the deepest, darkest </p>
<p>woods.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d4 </p>
<p>(A), Spirit d6, Strength d8, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Intimidation d8, Notice d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>10; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 6</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str+d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Go  for  the  Throat:</b>  Wolves  instinctively  go </p>
<p>for an opponent’s soft spots. With a raise on </p>
<p>its attack roll, it hits the target’s most weakly </p>
<p>armored location.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fleet-Footed:</b> Dire wolves roll d10s instead </p>
<p>of d6s when running.</p>
<p>Dog/Wolf</p>
<p>The  stats  below  are  for  large </p>
<p>attack dogs, such as Rottweilers </p>
<p>and Doberman Pinschers, as </p>
<p>well as wolves, hyenas, and </p>
<p>the like.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d6 (A), Spirit d6, Strength d6, </p>
<p>Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d6, Notice d10</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 8; <b>Parry:</b> 5; <b>Toughness:</b> 4</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str+d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fleet-Footed:</b>  Roll  a  d10  when  running </p>
<p>instead of a d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Go for the Throat:</b> Dogs instinctively go for </p>
<p>an opponent’s soft spots. With a raise on its </p>
<p>attack  roll,  it  hits  the  target’s  most  weakly </p>
<p>armored location.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size –1:</b> Dogs are relatively small.</p>
<p>X</p>
<p>Drake</p>
<p>Drakes are non-flying dragons </p>
<p>with animal intelligence (rather </p>
<p>than  the  more  human-like </p>
<p>sentience  of  true  dragons). </p>
<p>T h e y  </p>
<p>a r e  </p>
<p>m u c h  </p>
<p>m o r e </p>
<p>aggressive  in  direct  combat </p>
<p>than  their  distant  cousins, </p>
<p>however.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts d6 (A), Spirit d10, </p>
<p>Strength d12+6, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d10, Intimidation d12, Notice d8</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 7; <b>Toughness:</b> 17 (4)</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +4:</b> Scaly hide.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws/Bite: </b>Str+d8.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fear:</b>  Drakes  are  frightening  creatures  to </p>
<p>behold.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fiery Breath:</b> Drakes breathe fire using the </p>
<p>Cone Template. Every target within this cone </p>
<p>may  make  an Agility  roll  at  –2  to  avoid  the </p>
<p>attack. Those  who  fail  suffer  2d10  damage </p>
<p>and must check to see if they catch fire (see </p>
<p><b>Fire</b>). A drake may not attack with its claws or </p>
<p>bite in the round it breathes fire.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Large:</b> Attackers add +2 to their attack rolls </p>
<p>when attacking a drake due to its large size.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +5:</b> Drakes are over 20’ long from snout </p>
<p>to tail, and weigh in at over 3000 pounds.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Tail Lash:</b> A drake can sweep all opponents in </p>
<p>its rear facing in a 3” long by 6” wide rectangle. </p>
<p>This is a standard Fighting attack, and damage </p>
<p>is equal to the creature’s Strength –2.</p>
<p>X</p>
<p>Dragon</p>
<p>Dragons  are  fire-</p>
<p>breathing  monsters </p>
<p>that  bring  doom </p>
<p>and  despair  to </p>
<p>t h e  </p>
<p>v i l l a g e s </p>
<p>they  ravage. </p>
<p>Such creatures </p>
<p>should  not  be </p>
<p>fought  lightly </p>
<p>a s  </p>
<p>t h e y  </p>
<p>a r e </p>
<p>m o r e  </p>
<p>t h a n  </p>
<p>a </p>
<p>match  for  even  a </p>
<p>party  of  experienced </p>
<p>adventurers. These beasts </p>
<p>are quite intelligent as well, and use all of their </p>
<p>advantages when confronted by would-be dragon-</p>
<p>slayers.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d8,  Spirit  d10, </p>
<p>Strength d12+9, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d10, Intimidation d12, Notice d12</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>8; <b>Parry:</b> 7; <b>Toughness:</b> 20 (4)</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +4:</b> Scaly hide.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws/Bite: </b>Str+d8.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fear –2:</b> Anyone who sees a mighty dragon </p>
<p>must make a Fear check at –2.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fiery Breath:</b> Dragons breathe fire using the </p>
<p>Cone Template. Every target within this cone </p>
<p>may  make  an Agility  roll  at  –2  to  avoid  the </p>
<p>attack. Those  who  fail  suffer  2d10  damage </p>
<p>and  must  check  to  see  if  they  catch  fire. A </p>
<p>dragon may not attack with its claws or bite in </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--158</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>the round it breathes fire.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Flight:</b>  Dragons  have  a  Flying  Pace  of  24” </p>
<p>and Climb 0.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Hardy: </b>The creature does not suffer a wound </p>
<p>from being Shaken twice.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Huge:</b> Attackers add +4 to their Fighting or </p>
<p>Shooting rolls when attacking a dragon due </p>
<p>to its massive size.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Improved Frenzy:</b> If a dragon does not use its </p>
<p>Fiery Breath ability, it may make two Fighting </p>
<p>attacks with no penalty.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Level Headed:</b> Act on best of two cards.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +8:</b> Dragons are massive creatures. This </p>
<p>version is over 40’ long from nose to tail, and </p>
<p>weighs well over 30,000 pounds.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Tail Lash:</b> The dragon can sweep all opponents </p>
<p>in its rear facing in a 3” long by 6” wide square. </p>
<p>This is a standard Fighting attack, and damage </p>
<p>is equal to the dragon’s Strength –2.</p>
<p>Elementals</p>
<p>Elementals are living spirits of earth, fire, water, </p>
<p>and  air. These  are  average  examples  of  such </p>
<p>creatures. They may be more or less powerful in </p>
<p>specific settings.</p>
<p>Earth.Elemental</p>
<p>Earth  elementals  manifest  as </p>
<p>five-foot  tall,  vaguely  man-</p>
<p>shaped  collections  of  earth </p>
<p>and stone. Though amazingly </p>
<p>strong,  they  are  also  quite </p>
<p>slow and ponderous.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts </p>
<p>d4,  Spirit  d6,  Strength  d12+3, </p>
<p>Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Notice d4</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 4; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 11 (4)</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +4:</b> Rocky hide.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bash:</b> Str+d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Burrow (10”):</b> Earth elementals can meld into </p>
<p>and out of the ground.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Elemental:</b> No additional damage from called </p>
<p>shots;  Fearless;  Immune  to  disease  and </p>
<p>poison.</p>
<p>Fire.Elemental</p>
<p>Fire  elementals  appear  as </p>
<p>man-shaped flame.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d12+1, </p>
<p>Smarts d8, Spirit d8, Strength </p>
<p>d4, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills: </b> Climbing  d8,  Fighting </p>
<p>d10, Notice d6, Shooting d8</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 6; <b>Parry:</b> 7; <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Elemental:</b> No additional damage from called </p>
<p>shots;  Fearless;  Immune  to  disease  and </p>
<p>poison.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Invulnerability:</b> Fire Elementals are immune </p>
<p>to  all  non-magical  attacks,  but  suffer  1d6 </p>
<p>damage when doused in at least a gallon of </p>
<p>water, +2 per additional gallon.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fiery Touch:</b> Str+d6; chance of catching fire.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Flame  Strike:</b>  Fire  elementals  can  project </p>
<p>a  searing  blast  of  flame  using  the  Cone </p>
<p>Template.  Characters  within  the  cone  must </p>
<p>beat  the  spirit’s  Shooting  roll  with Agility  or </p>
<p>suffer  2d10  damage,  plus  the  chance  of </p>
<p>catching fire.</p>
<p>Water.Elemental</p>
<p>Water spirits are frothing, man-</p>
<p>shaped creatures of water and </p>
<p>sea-foam.</p>
<p><b>Attributes: </b>Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d6,  Spirit  d6,  Strength  d10, </p>
<p>Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills: </b>Fighting d8, Notice d6, </p>
<p>Shooting d8, Swimming d12+2</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 6; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 7</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Aquatic:</b> Pace 12</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Elemental:</b> No additional damage from called </p>
<p>shots;  Fearless;  Immune  to  disease  and </p>
<p>poison.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Invulnerability:</b> Water elementals are immune </p>
<p>to all non-magical attacks except fire. A torch </p>
<p>or  lantern  causes  them  1d6  damage  but  is </p>
<p>instantly put out if it hits.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Seep: </b>Water elementals can squeeze through </p>
<p>any porous gap as if it were Difficult Ground.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Slam:</b> Str+d6, nonlethal damage.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Waterspout:</b> Water spirits can project a torrent </p>
<p>of water using the Cone Template. Those in </p>
<p>the area may make an Agility roll opposed by </p>
<p>the spirit’s Shooting to avoid it or suffer 2d8 </p>
<p>nonlethal damage. This puts out any normal </p>
<p>fires.</p>
<p>Air.Elemental</p>
<p>Air  elementals  manifest  as </p>
<p>sentient whirlwinds. </p>
<p><b>  Attributes:</b>  Agility  d12, </p>
<p>Smarts d6, Spirit d6, Strength </p>
<p>d8, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills: </b>Fighting d8, Notice d8, </p>
<p>Shooting d6</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> —; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--159</p>
<p>Bestiary</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Elemental:</b> No additional damage from called </p>
<p>shots;  Fearless;  Immune  to  disease  and </p>
<p>poison.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Ethereal: </b> Air  Elementals  can  maneuver </p>
<p>through any non-solid surface. They can seep </p>
<p>through the cracks in doors, bubble through </p>
<p>water, and rush through sails.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Flight:</b> Air Elementals fly at a rate of 6” with a </p>
<p>Climb of 3. They may not run.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Invulnerability:</b>  Immune  to  all  non-magical </p>
<p>attacks except fire.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Push:</b> The air elemental can use an action </p>
<p>to push a single adjacent target 1d6” directly </p>
<p>away  with  a  concentrated  blast  of  air. The </p>
<p>victim  makes  a  Strength  roll,  with  each </p>
<p>success and raise reducing the amount moved </p>
<p>by 1” (to a minimum of 0).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Wind Blast:</b> Air Elementals can send directed </p>
<p>blasts of air at foes using the Cone Template </p>
<p>and  a  Shooting  roll.  Foes  may  make  an </p>
<p>opposed Agility  roll  to  avoid  the  blast. The </p>
<p>damage is 2d6 points of nonlethal damage.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Whirlwind:</b> As long as the air elemental does </p>
<p>not  move  that  turn  it  may  attempt  to  pick </p>
<p>up a foe. Make an opposed Strength check </p>
<p>and  if  the air elemental wins  then its  foe is </p>
<p>pulled into the swirling maelstrom of its body. </p>
<p>While trapped, the target is at –2 on all rolls </p>
<p>including damage, to hit and Strength rolls to </p>
<p>free himself. The air elemental cannot move </p>
<p>as long as it wants to keep foes trapped inside </p>
<p>its form.</p>
<p>X</p>
<p>Giant.Worm</p>
<p>M a s s i v e  </p>
<p>w o r m s </p>
<p>tunneling  beneath </p>
<p>the </p>
<p>earth </p>
<p>to </p>
<p>g o b b l e  </p>
<p>u p </p>
<p>unsuspecting </p>
<p>adventurers </p>
<p>a</p>
<p>r</p>
<p>e </p>
<p>sometimes </p>
<p>f o u n d  </p>
<p>i n </p>
<p>l o n e s o m e </p>
<p>flatlands. The </p>
<p>things  sense </p>
<p>vibrations through </p>
<p>the  earth,  hearing </p>
<p>a  walking  person  at  about </p>
<p>200  yards. The  stats  below  are  for  a  monster </p>
<p>some 50’ long.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts d6 (A), Spirit d10, </p>
<p>Strength d12+10, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d6, Notice d10, Stealth d10</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 5; <b>Toughness:</b> 22 (4)</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +4:</b> Scaly hide.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str+d8.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Burrow  (20”):</b>  Giant  worms  can  disappear </p>
<p>and reappear on the following action anywhere </p>
<p>within 20”.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Gargantuan:</b> The worms are Huge and thus </p>
<p>suffer +4 to attacks against them. Their attacks </p>
<p>count as Heavy Weapons, and their Armor is </p>
<p>Heavy Armor.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Hardy: </b>The creature does not suffer a wound </p>
<p>from being Shaken twice.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +10:</b> Giant worms are usually well over </p>
<p>50’ long and 10’ or more in diameter.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Slam:</b>  Giant  worms  attempt  to  rise  up  and </p>
<p>crush their prey beneath their massive bodies. </p>
<p>This  is  an  opposed  roll  of  the  creature’s </p>
<p>Fighting versus the target’s Agility. If the worm </p>
<p>wins, the victim suffers 4d6 damage.</p>
<p>Ghost</p>
<p>Spectres, shades, and phantoms </p>
<p>sometimes return from death to </p>
<p>haunt the living or fulfill some </p>
<p>lost goal.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts </p>
<p>d6,  Spirit  d10,  Strength  d6, </p>
<p>Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Fighting  d6,  Intimidation </p>
<p>d12+2,  Notice  d12, Taunt  d10,  Stealth  d12+4, </p>
<p>Throwing d12</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 5; <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Thrown objects (Str+d4).</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Ethereal:</b> Ghosts are immaterial and can only </p>
<p>be harmed by magical attacks.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fear  –2:</b>  Ghosts  cause  Fear  checks  at  –2 </p>
<p>when they let themselves be seen.</p>
<p>Goblin</p>
<p>Goblins of myth and legend are </p>
<p>far  more  sinister  creatures </p>
<p>than some games and fiction </p>
<p>portray. In the original tales, </p>
<p>they were terrifying creatures </p>
<p>that stole  into homes in  the </p>
<p>middle of the night to steal and </p>
<p>eat unruly children. The statistics </p>
<p>here work for both dark “fairy tale” goblins as well </p>
<p>as those found alongside orcs in contemporary </p>
<p>roleplaying games.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--160</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d6,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d4, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Climbing  d6,  Fighting  d6,  Notice  d6, </p>
<p>Taunt d6, Shooting d8, Stealth d10, Throwing d6, </p>
<p>Swimming d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>5; <b>Parry:</b> 5; <b>Toughness:</b> 4</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Short spears (Str+d4).</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Infravision:</b> Goblins halve penalties for dark </p>
<p>lighting against living targets (round down).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size –1:</b> Goblins stand 3-4’ tall.</p>
<p>Horse,.Riding</p>
<p>Riding  horses  are  medium-</p>
<p>sized animals that manage a </p>
<p>good  compromise  between </p>
<p>speed and carrying capacity.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d4 (A), Spirit d6, Strength d12, </p>
<p>Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d4, Notice d6</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 10; <b>Parry:</b> 4; <b>Toughness:</b> 8</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fleet-Footed:</b> Horses roll a d8 when running </p>
<p>instead of a d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Kick:</b> Str.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +2:</b> Riding horses weigh between 800 </p>
<p>and 1000 pounds.</p>
<p>Horse,.War</p>
<p>War  horses  are  large  beasts </p>
<p>trained  for  aggression.  They </p>
<p>are trained to fight with both </p>
<p>hooves,  either  to  their  front </p>
<p>or their rear. In combat, the </p>
<p>animal  attacks  any  round </p>
<p>its rider doesn’t make a trick </p>
<p>maneuver of some kind.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts d4 (A), </p>
<p>Spirit d6, Strength d12+2, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Notice d6</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 8; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 10</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fleet-Footed:</b>  War  horses  roll  a  d8  when </p>
<p>running instead of a d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Kick:</b> Str+d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +3:</b> Warhorses are large creatures bred </p>
<p>for their power and stature.</p>
<p>X</p>
<p>Lich</p>
<p>Perhaps the most diabolical </p>
<p>creature in any fantasy land </p>
<p>is the lich—a necromancer so </p>
<p>consumed with the black arts </p>
<p>that  he  eventually  becomes </p>
<p>undead himself.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts d12+2, Spirit d10, </p>
<p>Strength d10, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Intimidation d12, Knowledge </p>
<p>(Occult) d12+2, Notice d10, Spellcasting d12</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 15 (6)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Magical armor (+6), other magical items.</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Death Touch:</b> Liches drain the lives of those </p>
<p>around them with a touch. Instead of a normal </p>
<p>attack, a lich may make a touch attack. Every </p>
<p>raise on its Fighting roll automatically inflicts </p>
<p>one wound to its target.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Spells:</b>  Liches  have  50  Power  Points  and </p>
<p>know most every spell available.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Undead: </b>+2 Toughness; +2 to recover from </p>
<p>being  Shaken;  called  shots  do  no  extra </p>
<p>damage; ignores wound penalties.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Zombie:</b> Liches are necromancers first and </p>
<p>foremost.  The  undead  they  raise  through </p>
<p>the <i>zombie</i> spell are permanent, so they are </p>
<p>usually  surrounded  by  4d10  skeletons  or </p>
<p>zombies as they choose. Some liches have </p>
<p>entire armies of the undead at their disposal.</p>
<p>Lion</p>
<p>The  kings  of  the  jungle  are </p>
<p>fierce  predators,  particularly </p>
<p>in open grassland where their </p>
<p>prey cannot seek refuge.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d6  (A),  Spirit  d10,  Strength </p>
<p>d12, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Notice d8</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 8; <b>Parry:</b> 6;<b> Toughness:</b> 8</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite or Claw:</b> Str+d6.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Improved  Frenzy:</b>  Lions  may  make  two </p>
<p>Fighting attacks each action at no penalty.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Low Light Vision: </b>Lions ignore penalties for </p>
<p>Dim and Dark lighting.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Pounce:</b> Lions often pounce on their prey to </p>
<p>best bring their mass and claws to bear. It can </p>
<p>leap 1d6” to gain +4 to its attack and damage. </p>
<p>Its Parry is reduced by –2 until its next action </p>
<p>when performing the maneuver however.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size  +2:</b>  Male  lions  can  weigh  over  500 </p>
<p>pounds.</p>
<p>Mech.(Sentinel)</p>
<p>The stats below are for a 12’ high mechanized </p>
<p>sentinel such as might be found in a typical hard </p>
<p>sci-fi campaign. This is a light patrol-style platform </p>
<p>with reasonable intelligence, a sensor package, </p>
<p>and high maneuverability.</p>
<p>Larger  mechs  outfitted  for  battle  have </p>
