<p>Bestiary</p>
<p>substantially  more </p>
<p>armor,  are  larger, </p>
<p>and  have  more </p>
<p>spe ci al iz ed </p>
<p>weaponry.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> </p>
<p>Agility  d4, </p>
<p>Smarts  d6, </p>
<p>S p i r i t  </p>
<p>d 4 , </p>
<p>Strength  d6, </p>
<p>Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Fighting </p>
<p>d6,  Notice  d10, </p>
<p>Shooting d8</p>
<p><b>P a c e :  </b></p>
<p>1 0 ;  </p>
<p><b>P a r r y :</b>  </p>
<p>5 ; </p>
<p><b>Toughness:</b> 10 (4)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Typically a machine gun or flamethrower.</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +4</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Construct:</b> +2 to recover from being Shaken; </p>
<p>called shots  do no extra damage; does not </p>
<p>suffer from disease or poison.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fearless:</b>  Mechs  are  immune  to  fear  and </p>
<p>Intimidation, but may be smart enough to react </p>
<p>to fear-causing situations appropriately.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Sensors:</b>  Sentinel  mechs  are  equipped </p>
<p>with  sensor  packages  that  halve  penalties </p>
<p>for  darkness,  can  detect  sounds,  or  record </p>
<p>conversations via directional microphones. </p>
<p>Minotaur</p>
<p>Minotaurs stand over 7’ tall and </p>
<p>have massive, bull-like heads </p>
<p>and  horns.  In  many  fantasy </p>
<p>worlds,  they  are  used  as </p>
<p>guardians  of  labyrinths.  In </p>
<p>others, they are simply another </p>
<p>race of creatures occupying a </p>
<p>fantastically  savage  setting.  In </p>
<p>a l l </p>
<p>cases, they are fierce beasts eager for battle and </p>
<p>the taste of their opponents’ flesh.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d6,  Spirit  d8, </p>
<p>Strength d12+2, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d10, Intimidation d12, Notice d10, </p>
<p>Throwing d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>8; <b>Parry:</b> 8; <b>Toughness:</b> 11 (1)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Leather armor (+1), spear (Str+d6, Reach </p>
<p>1, Parry+1).</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Horns:</b> Str+d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fleet-Footed:</b> Minotaurs roll d10s instead of </p>
<p>d6s when running.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Gore:</b> Minotaurs use this maneuver to gore </p>
<p>their opponents with their horns. If they can </p>
<p>charge at least 6” before attacking, they add </p>
<p>+4 to their damage total.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +2:</b> Minotaurs stand over 7’ tall.</p>
<p>Mule</p>
<p>Mules are a cross between a </p>
<p>donkey and a horse, and are </p>
<p>usually  used  to  haul  heavy </p>
<p>goods or pull wagons.</p>
<p>Like any good pet, the GM </p>
<p>should  feel  free  to  give  the </p>
<p>mule  a  little  personality.  The </p>
<p>expression  “stubborn  as  a  mule” </p>
<p>certainly comes to mind.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d4, Smarts d4 (A), Spirit d6, </p>
<p>Strength d8, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Notice d4</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 6; <b>Parry:</b> 2;<b> Toughness: </b>8</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fleet-Footed:</b>  Mules  roll  d8  instead  of  d6 </p>
<p>when running.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Kick: </b>Str.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Ornery: </b> Mules  are  contrary  creatures. </p>
<p>Characters must subtract 1 from their Riding </p>
<p>rolls when riding them.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +2:</b> Mules are stocky creatures weighing </p>
<p>up to 1000 pounds.</p>
<p>Ogre</p>
<p>Ogres are kin to orcs and lesser </p>
<p>giants. They  are  often  taken </p>
<p>in by orc clans, who respect </p>
<p>the  dumb  brutes  for  their </p>
<p>savagery and strength. Orcs </p>
<p>often  pit  their  “pet”  ogres  in </p>
<p>savage combats against their </p>
<p>rivals’ ogres.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts  d4,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d12+3, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Fighting  d8,  Intimidation  d8,  Notice  d4, </p>
<p>Throwing d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>7; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness: </b>12 (1)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Thick hides (+1), massive club (Str+d8).</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +3:</b> Most ogres are over 8’ tall with pot-</p>
<p>bellies and massive arms and legs.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Sweep:</b>  May  attack  all  adjacent  characters </p>
<p>at –2.</p>
<p>Orc</p>
<p>Orcs  are  savage,  green-</p>
<p>skinned humanoids with pig-</p>
<p>like features, including snouts </p>
<p>and  sometimes  even  tusks. </p>
<p>They have foul temperaments, </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--162</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>and rarely take prisoners.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts  d4,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d8, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Fighting  d6,  Intimidation  d8,  Notice  d6, </p>
<p>Shooting d6, Stealth d6, Throwing d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 5; <b>Toughness:</b> 8 (1)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Leather armor (+1), scimitar (Str+d8).</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +1:</b> Orcs are slightly larger than humans.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Infravision:</b> Halves penalties for poor light vs. </p>
<p>warm targets.</p>
<p>X</p>
<p>Orc,.Chieftain</p>
<p>The  leader  of  small  orc  clans  is </p>
<p>always  the  most  deadly  brute </p>
<p>in  the  bunch.  Orc  chieftains </p>
<p>generally have a magical item </p>
<p>or two in settings where such </p>
<p>things are relatively common </p>
<p>(most  “swords  and  sorcery” </p>
<p>worlds).</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d6, </p>
<p>Spirit d6, Strength d10, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d12, Intimidation d10, Notice d6, </p>
<p>Shooting d8, Stealth d6, Throwing d8</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 8; <b>Toughness:</b> 11 (3)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Plate chest plate (+3), chain arms and legs </p>
<p>(+2), battle axe (Str+d10).</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Infravision:</b> Halves penalties for poor light vs. </p>
<p>heat-producing targets.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +1:</b> Orcs are slightly larger than humans.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Sweep:</b>  May  attack  all  adjacent  characters </p>
<p>at –2 penalty.</p>
<p>Shark,.Great.White</p>
<p>These  statistics  cover  great </p>
<p>whites,  18  to  25  feet  long. </p>
<p>Larger  specimens  surely </p>
<p>exist.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d4  (A),  Spirit  d8,  Strength </p>
<p>d12+4, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d10, Notice d12, Swimming d10</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> —; <b>Parry:</b> 7;<b> Toughness:</b> 12</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Aquatic:</b> Pace 10.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str+d8.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Hardy: </b>The creature does not suffer a wound </p>
<p>from being Shaken twice.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Large:</b> Attackers add +2 to their attack rolls </p>
<p>when attacking a great white due to its large </p>
<p>size.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +4:</b> Great whites can grow up to 25’ in </p>
<p>length.</p>
<p>Shark,.Medium.Maneater</p>
<p>These statistics cover most </p>
<p>medium-sized  mankillers, </p>
<p>such as tiger sharks and bulls.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d4 (A), Spirit d6, Strength d8, </p>
<p>Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Fighting  d8,  Notice  d12, </p>
<p>Swimming d10</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> —; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Aquatic:</b> Pace 10.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str+d6.</p>
<p>Skeleton</p>
<p>The  skin  has  already  rotted </p>
<p>from these risen dead, leaving </p>
<p>them  slightly  quicker  than </p>
<p>their  flesh-laden  zombie </p>
<p>counterparts.  They  are </p>
<p>often  found  swarming  in  vile </p>
<p>necromancers’ legions.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts d4, </p>
<p>Spirit d4, Strength d6, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Fighting  d6,  Intimidation  d6,  Notice  d4, </p>
<p>Shooting d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>7; <b>Parry:</b> 5; <b>Toughness:</b> 7</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Varies.</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bony Claws:</b> Str+d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fearless:</b> Skeletons are immune to Fear and </p>
<p>Intimidation.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Undead:</b> +2 Toughness; +2 to recover from </p>
<p>being  Shaken;  called  shots  do  no  extra </p>
<p>damage.</p>
<p>Snake,.Constrictor</p>
<p>Pythons, boa  constrictors, and </p>
<p>other  snakes  over  15’  long </p>
<p>are  rarely  deadly  to  man  in </p>
<p>the real world because they </p>
<p>aren’t particularly aggressive </p>
<p>toward  such  large  prey.  In </p>
<p>games, however, such snakes </p>
<p>might  be  provoked,  drugged,  or </p>
<p>just plain mean.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d4, Smarts d4 (A), Spirit d8, </p>
<p>Strength d6, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d6, Notice d10</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 4; <b>Parry:</b> 5;<b> Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Constrict:</b> Large constrictors have very little </p>
<p>chance of entangling active man-sized prey </p>
<p>in  the  real  world—they  must  attack  while </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--163</p>
<p>Bestiary</p>
<p>their  victim  is  sleeping,  stunned,  paralyzed, </p>
<p>and  so  on.  Constrictors  in  pulp  and  other </p>
<p>fantastic  genres  might  be  far  more  deadly. </p>
<p>These creatures bite when they succeed at a </p>
<p>Fighting roll, and entangle when they succeed </p>
<p>with a raise. The round they entangle and each </p>
<p>round thereafter, they cause damage to their </p>
<p>prey equal to Str+d6. The prey may attempt </p>
<p>to escape on his action by getting a raise on </p>
<p>an opposed Strength roll.</p>
<p>Snake,.Venomous</p>
<p>Here  are  the  stats  for  Taipans </p>
<p>(Australian  brown  snakes), </p>
<p>cobras,  and  similar  medium-</p>
<p>sized snakes with extremely </p>
<p>deadly poison.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts </p>
<p>d4 (A), Spirit d6, Strength d4, </p>
<p>Vigor d4</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Notice d12</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 4; <b>Parry:</b> 6;<b> Toughness:</b> 2</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite:</b> Str.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Poison:</b> See the Poison rules on page 103.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Quick:</b> Snakes are notoriously fast. They may </p>
<p>discard Action Cards of 5 or lower and draw </p>
<p>another. They  must  keep  the  replacement </p>
<p>card, however.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size –2:</b> Most venomous snakes are 4-6’ in </p>
<p>length, but only a few inches thick.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Small:</b>  Anyone  attacking  a  snake  must </p>
<p>subtract 2 from his attack rolls.</p>
<p>Spider,.Giant</p>
<p>Giant spiders are about the size </p>
<p>of large dogs and live in nests </p>
<p>of  1d6+2  arachnids.  They </p>
<p>frequently go hunting in these </p>
<p>packs when prey is scarce in </p>
<p>their home lair.</p>
<p>Their  dens  are  littered  with </p>
<p>the bones and treasures of their </p>
<p>victims,  often  providing  ripe  pickings  for  those </p>
<p>brave enough to venture within.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d10, Smarts d4 (A), Spirit d6, </p>
<p>Strength d10, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Climbing d12+2, Fighting d8, Intimidation </p>
<p>d10, Notice d8, Shooting d10, Stealth d10</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>8; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite: </b>Str+d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Poison (–4): </b>See the poison rules on page 103.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Wall Walker:</b> Can walk on vertical surfaces </p>
<p>at Pace 8.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Webbing: </b>The  spiders  can  cast  webs  from </p>
<p>their thorax that are the size of Small Burst </p>
<p>Templates. This is a Shooting roll with a range </p>
<p>of  3/6/12. Anything  in  the  web  must  cut  or </p>
<p>break their way free (Toughness 7). Webbed </p>
<p>characters  can  still  fight,  but  all  physical </p>
<p>actions are at –4.</p>
<p>Swarm</p>
<p>Sometimes the most deadly foes </p>
<p>come in the smallest packages. </p>
<p>The  swarm  described  below </p>
<p>can  be  of  most  anything—</p>
<p>from  biting  ants  to  stinging </p>
<p>wasps to filthy rats.</p>
<p>The swarm is treated just like </p>
<p>a creature. When it is wounded, </p>
<p>the swarm is effectively dispersed.</p>
<p>Swarms cover an area equal to a Medium Burst </p>
<p>Template and attack everyone within every round.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d10, Smarts d4 (A), Spirit d12, </p>
<p>Strength d8, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Notice d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>10; <b>Parry:</b> 4; <b>Toughness:</b> 7</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Bite  or  Sting: </b> Swarms  inflict  hundreds  of </p>
<p>tiny bites every round to their victims, hitting </p>
<p>automatically  and  causing  2d4  damage  to </p>
<p>everyone in the template. Damage is applied </p>
<p>to  the  least  armored  location  (victims  in </p>
<p>completely sealed suits are immune).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Split:</b>  Some  swarms  are  clever  enough  to </p>
<p>split  into  two  smaller  swarms  (Small  Burst </p>
<p>Templates)  should  their  foes  split  up.  The </p>
<p>Toughness of these smaller swarms is lowered </p>
<p>by –2 (to 5 each).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Swarm:</b>  Parry  +2;  Because  the  swarm  is </p>
<p>composed of scores, hundreds, or thousands </p>
<p>of creatures, cutting and piercing weapons do </p>
<p>no  real  damage. Area-effect  weapons  work </p>
<p>normally, and a character can stomp to inflict </p>
<p>his damage in Strength each round. Swarms </p>
<p>are usually foiled by jumping in water (unless </p>
<p>they are aquatic pests, such as piranha).</p>
<p>Troll</p>
<p>Trolls  in  myths  and  legends </p>
<p>are  horrid,  flesh-eating </p>
<p>creatures  who  live  in  deep </p>
<p>woods,  beneath  bridges,  or </p>
<p>in  hidden  mountain  caves. </p>
<p>In modern games and fiction, </p>
<p>trolls are monsters with the ability </p>
<p>to regenerate damage and a weakness to fire. </p>
<p>These statistics reflect both backgrounds.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--164</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts  d4,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d12+2, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Intimidation d10, Notice d6, </p>
<p>Swimming d6, Throwing d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>7; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness: </b>10 (1)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Spiked club (Str+d8).</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Armor +1:</b> Rubbery hide.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws:</b> Str+d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Improved  Sweep:</b>  May  attack  all  adjacent </p>
<p>foes at no penalty.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fast  Regeneration:</b>  Trolls  may  attempt </p>
<p>a  natural  healing  roll  every  round  unless </p>
<p>their  wounds  were  caused  by  fire  or  flame. </p>
<p>This occurs whether the troll is a Wild Card </p>
<p>leader or an Extra. If the latter, a downed troll </p>
<p>actually returns to action if it heals itself (and </p>
<p>is  not  Shaken—even  if  it  was  before  being </p>
<p>Incapacitated).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size +2:</b> Trolls are tall, lanky creatures over </p>
<p>8’ tall.</p>
<p>X</p>
<p>Vampire,.Ancient</p>
<p>Blood-drinkers  of  lore  are </p>
<p>common  in  many  fantasy </p>
<p>games. The  statistics  below </p>
<p>are for a vampire somewhat </p>
<p>b e l o w  </p>
<p>t h e  </p>
<p>l e g e n d a r y </p>
<p>Dracula, but far above those </p>
<p>bloodsuckers  fresh  from  the </p>
<p>grave (detailed next). The abilities </p>
<p>listed below are standard—the GM may want to </p>
<p>add other Edges as befits the vampire’s previous </p>
<p>lifestyle.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d10,  Spirit  d10, </p>
<p>Strength d12+3, Vigor d12</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d10, Intimidation d12, Notice d8, </p>
<p>Shooting d8, Swimming d8, Throwing d8</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 7; <b>Toughness:</b> 10</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Change Form:</b> As an action, a vampire can </p>
<p>change into a wolf or bat with a Smarts roll </p>
<p>at  –2.  Changing  back  into  humanoid  form </p>
<p>requires a Smarts roll.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Charm:</b> Vampires can use the <i>puppet</i> power </p>
<p>on  the  opposite  sex  using  their  Smarts  as </p>
<p>their arcane skill. They can cast and maintain </p>
<p>the power indefinitely, but may only affect one </p>
<p>target at a time.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Children of the Night:</b> Ancient vampires have </p>
<p>the ability to summon and control wolves or </p>
<p>rats. This  requires  an  action  and  a  Smarts </p>
<p>roll  at  –2.  If  successful,  1d6  wolves  or  1d6 </p>
<p>swarms of rats (see Swarm) come from the </p>
<p>surrounding wilds in 1d6+2 rounds.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws:</b> Str +d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Improved Frenzy:</b> Vampires may make two </p>
<p>attacks per round without penalty.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Invulnerability:</b> Vampires can only be harmed </p>
<p>by their Weaknesses. They may be Shaken by </p>
<p>other attacks, but never wounded.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Level Headed:</b> Vampires act on the best of </p>
<p>two cards.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Mist:</b>  Greater  vampires  have  the  ability  to </p>
<p>turn into mist. This requires an action and a </p>
<p>Smarts roll at –2.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Sire:</b> Anyone slain by a vampire has a 50% </p>
<p>chance of rising as a vampire themselves in </p>
<p>1d4 days.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Undead: </b>+2 Toughness; +2 to recover from </p>
<p>being  Shaken;  called  shots  do  no  extra </p>
<p>damage (except to the heart—see below). No </p>
<p>wound penalties.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness  (Sunlight):</b>  Vampires  catch  fire </p>
<p>if any part of their skin is exposed to direct </p>
<p>sunlight. After that they suffer 2d10 damage </p>
<p>per round until they are dust. Armor does not </p>
<p>protect.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness (Holy Symbol):</b> A character may </p>
<p>keep a vampire at bay by displaying a holy </p>
<p>symbol. A vampire who wants to directly attack </p>
<p>the victim must beat her in an opposed test </p>
<p>of Spirit.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness (Holy Water):</b> A vampire sprinkled </p>
<p>with holy water is Fatigued. If immersed, he </p>
<p>combusts  as  if  it  were  direct  sunlight  (see </p>
<p>above).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness  (Invitation  Only):</b>  Vampires </p>
<p>cannot enter a private dwelling without being </p>
<p>invited. They  may  enter  public  domains  as </p>
<p>they please.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness  (Stake  Through  the  Heart):</b> A </p>
<p>vampire hit with a called shot to the heart (–4) </p>
<p>must  make  a  Vigor  roll  versus  the  damage </p>
<p>total. If successful, it takes damage normally. </p>
<p>If it fails, it disintegrates to dust.</p>
<p>Vampire,.Young</p>
<p>Blood-drinkers  of  lore  are </p>
<p>common  in  many  fantasy </p>
<p>games. This is a relatively </p>
<p>young vampire minion.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b>  Agility  d8, </p>
<p>Smarts  d8,  Spirit  d8, </p>
<p>Strength d12+1, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Intimidation </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--165</p>
<p>Bestiary</p>
<p>d8,  Notice  d6,  Shooting  d6,  Swimming  d8, </p>
<p>Throwing d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>6; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 9</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws:</b> Str+d4.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Frenzy:</b> Vampires can make two attacks per </p>
<p>round with a –2 penalty to each attack.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Level Headed:</b> Vampires act on the best of </p>
<p>two cards.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Invulnerability:</b> Vampires can only be harmed </p>
<p>by their Weaknesses. They may be Shaken by </p>
<p>other attacks, but never wounded.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Sire:</b> Anyone slain by a vampire has a 50% </p>
<p>chance of rising as a vampire themselves in </p>
<p>1d4 days.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Undead: </b>+2 Toughness; +2 to recover from </p>
<p>being  Shaken;  called  shots  do  no  extra </p>
<p>damage (except to the heart—see below).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness  (Sunlight):</b>  Vampires  catch  fire </p>
<p>if any part of their skin is exposed to direct </p>
<p>sunlight. After that they suffer 2d10 damage </p>
<p>per round until they are dust. Armor does not </p>
<p>protect.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness (Holy Symbol):</b> A character with </p>
<p>a holy symbol may keep a vampire at bay by </p>
<p>displaying a holy symbol. A vampire who wants </p>
<p>to directly attack the victim must beat her in an </p>
<p>opposed test of Spirit.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness (Holy Water):</b> A vampire sprinkled </p>
<p>with holy water is Fatigued. If immersed, he </p>
<p>combusts  as  if  it  were  direct  sunlight  (see </p>
<p>above).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness  (Invitation  Only):</b>  Vampires </p>
<p>cannot enter a private dwelling without being </p>
<p>invited. They  may  enter  public  domains  as </p>
<p>they please.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness  (Stake  Through  the  Heart):</b> A </p>
<p>vampire hit with a called shot to the heart (–4) </p>
<p>must make a Vigor roll versus the damage. If </p>
<p>successful, it takes damage normally. If it fails, </p>
<p>it disintegrates to dust.</p>
<p>Werewolf</p>
<p>When  a  full  moon  emerges, </p>
<p>h u m a n s  </p>
<p>i n f e c t e d  </p>
<p>w i t h </p>
<p>lycanthropy lose control and </p>
<p>become  snarling  creatures </p>
<p>bent  on  murder.  Some </p>
<p>embrace  their  cursed  state </p>
<p>and revel in the destruction they </p>
<p>cause.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d6,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d12+2, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Climbing d8, Fighting d12+2, Intimidation </p>
<p>d10,  Notice  d12,  Swimming  d10,  Stealth  d10, </p>
<p>Tracking d10</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>8; <b>Parry:</b> 9;<b> Toughness:</b> 7</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws:</b> Str+d8.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fear –2:</b> Werewolves chill the blood of all who </p>
<p>see them.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Infection:</b>  Anyone  slain  by  a  werewolf </p>
<p>has  a  50%  chance  of  rising  as  a  werewolf </p>
<p>themselves.  The  character  involuntarily </p>
<p>transforms every full moon. He gains control </p>
<p>of his lycanthropy only after 1d6 years as a </p>
<p>werewolf.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Invulnerability:</b>  Werewolves  can  only  be </p>
<p>Shaken by weapons that are not silver—not </p>
<p>wounded.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Infravision:</b>  Werewolves  can  see  heat  and </p>
<p>halve penalties for bad lighting when attacking </p>
<p>living targets.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness: </b> Werewolves  suffer  normal </p>
<p>damage from silver weapons.</p>
<p>Zombie</p>
<p>These  walking  dead  are </p>
<p>typical groaning fiends looking </p>
<p>for fresh meat. </p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d6, Smarts </p>
<p>d4,  Spirit  d4,  Strength  d6, </p>
<p>Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d6, Intimidation d6, </p>
<p>Notice d4, Shooting d6</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>4; <b>Parry:</b> 5;<b> Toughness:</b> 7</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Claws:</b> Str.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fearless:</b> Zombies are immune to Fear and </p>
<p>Intimidation.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Undead: </b>+2 Toughness; +2 to recover from </p>
<p>being  Shaken;  called  shots  do  no  extra </p>
<p>damage (except to the head).</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Weakness (Head):</b> Shots to a zombie’s head </p>
<p>are +2 damage.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--166</p>
<p>Knight.Errant:.Return.Engagement</p>
<p>Something  has  awakened  at  the  Orpheum, </p>
<p>an  old  building  that  has  been  everything  from </p>
<p>a theatre to a  slaughterhouse. The  heroes  are </p>
<p>employees of Knight Errant, a detective agency </p>
<p>that specializes in the macabre—and has a very </p>
<p>high turnover rate…</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Setting  Rules:</b>  Critical  Failures,  Gritty </p>
<p>Damage</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Characters:</b>  The  heroes  are  investigators </p>
<p>working with the Knight Errant Detective Agency.</p>
<p>The investigators have been sent to look into the </p>
<p>renovation of the Orpheum Theatre in a decaying </p>
<p>area of a nearby city’s downtown. The work has </p>
<p>suffered a number of unexplained setbacks and </p>
<p>the  company  insuring  the  project  has  come  to </p>
<p>suspect that the owner of the theater, Silas Linden, </p>
<p>is deliberately sabotaging the effort in an attempt </p>
<p>at  insurance  fraud.  The  insurance  company </p>
<p>has hired Knight Errant to look into these grave </p>
<p>matters.</p>
<p>In reality, the construction crew has disturbed </p>
<p>a vampire that has lain in a comatose state for </p>
<p>over  half  a  century.  It  was  unwittingly  brought </p>
<p>to the theater as a display in a freak show and </p>
<p>abandoned  in  the  basement  when  the  theater </p>
<p>closed.</p>
<p>The monster was once a poor Chinese railroad </p>
<p>worker who fell victim to another such fiend long </p>
<p>ago. It speaks no English, and in fact is far too </p>
<p>mentally disturbed at this point to speak at all. </p>
<p>It stirred briefly when the building was used as </p>
<p>a  slaughterhouse,  feeding  on  the  blood  of  the </p>
<p>animals that drained down to it only to once again </p>
<p>lapse into torpor when that business closed as </p>
<p>well. The thing was awakened recently by a tragic </p>
<p>accident involving one of the workers.</p>
<p>Visiting.the.Orpheum</p>
<p>The Orpheum is an old building in a rundown </p>
<p>section of the city. Most of the buildings nearby are </p>
<p>abandoned and in poor repair. The theater, thanks </p>
<p>to its renovations, stands out like a diamond in </p>
<p>a coal pile. Inside, ornate filigree, marble tiling, </p>
<p>and generous use of opulent red curtains ooze a </p>
<p>sense of nostalgia for an earlier, more stylish time. </p>
<p>Meeting.Linden</p>
<p>The investigators find Linden, a short, somewhat </p>
<p>heavy-set  man,  very  receptive  to  their  arrival. </p>
<p>Linden  seems  genuinely  concerned  about  the </p>
<p>delays  his  project  has  suffered. A  number  of </p>
<p>workmen have been injured since the job started </p>
<p>Sample.Adventures</p>
<p>On the following pages are a number of “One </p>
<p>Sheet” adventures. You’ll find dozens more on our </p>
<p>website at www.peginc.com.</p>
<p>Why “One Sheet?” Our goal is to give a Game </p>
<p>Master something he can read, understand, and </p>
<p>be ready to run in just a few minutes—hence one </p>
<p>page (front and back) adventures.</p>
<p>Players can make characters appropriate for the </p>
<p>genre (or use the Archetypes on page 18–19) and </p>
<p>be ready to play in minutes as well.</p>
<p>One Sheets also demonstrate what we mean </p>
<p>by “Fast! Furious! Fun!” We get right to the most </p>
<p>important aspects of the adventure—the setup, </p>
<p>what  is  expected  to  happen,  and  the  statistics </p>
<p>for any monsters or villains the heroes are likely </p>
<p>to fight.</p>
<p>You won’t find details on the surroundings or </p>
<p>statistics  for  nonplayer  characters  who  aren’t </p>
<p>directly important to the plot. Those are left for you, </p>
<p>the Game Master, to make up as you go and as </p>
<p>they become important to your session.</p>
<p>If you’re not comfortable filling in the blanks, look </p>
<p>for full-length adventures on our website. Those </p>
<p>are generally designed for multiple sessions and </p>
<p>give  far  more  detail  on  the </p>
<p>world and the nonplayer </p>
<p>characters.</p>
<p>Share!</p>
<p>O n c e  </p>
<p>y o u ’ v e </p>
<p>r u n  </p>
<p>o r  </p>
<p>p l a y e d </p>
<p>some </p>
<p>of </p>
<p>these </p>
<p>adventures,  we </p>
<p>invite  you  to  come </p>
<p>share  your  tale </p>
<p>on  our  forums. </p>
<p>Our  community </p>
<p>loves  to  read </p>
<p>a b o u t  </p>
<p>t h e m </p>
<p>and  see  what </p>
<p>y o u r  </p>
<p>g r o u p </p>
<p>did  differently </p>
<p>than the last.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--167</p>
<p>Adventures</p>
<p>and rumors are beginning to circulate amongst the </p>
<p>men that the building is either haunted or cursed. A </p>
<p>few have apparently been so spooked they simply </p>
<p>walked off the job and never returned.</p>
<p>He answers any of their questions to the best </p>
<p>of  his  ability.  Linden  also  provides  them  with </p>
<p>unfettered access to the theater while the work </p>
<p>progresses, warning them that it is a construction </p>
<p>site  and  the  project  has  been  plagued  by  no </p>
<p>shortage of accidents.</p>
<p>A.Little.History</p>
<p>If asked, Linden tells the heroes the Orpheum </p>
<p>began as a theater back at the turn of the 20</p>
<p>th</p>
<p> </p>
<p>century, but closed its doors in the early 1920s. </p>
<p>The building was converted to a slaughterhouse </p>
<p>during  the  Depression,  however  that  business </p>
<p>folded around the time of the second World War. </p>
<p>Much of the renovation has involved removing and </p>
<p>repairing modifications made during the building’s </p>
<p>time as a slaughterhouse.</p>
<p>It has sat unused and unoccupied since then—</p>
<p>except, he adds, for the usual transients and drug </p>
<p>addicts. Linden admits he never actually saw any </p>
<p>in the theater, but the neighborhood was overrun </p>
<p>with shady characters. Now, most seem to have </p>
<p>moved to less active areas in the city.</p>
<p>Legwork</p>
<p>Depending  on  how  they  approach  the </p>
<p>investigation,  the  characters  can  discover  a </p>
<p>number  of  clues.  Reveal  the  information  as </p>
<p>the  team  investigates  the  theater  and  the </p>
<p>neighborhood. Let them ask questions and think </p>
<p>about how to get these clues—don’t just give them </p>
<p>info based on skill rolls.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Accidents: </b>The first accident occurred while </p>
<p>the crew was removing the old slaughterhouse </p>
<p>equipment. One of the men nearly severed an </p>
<p>arm on a rusty saw and bled out before the </p>
<p>ambulance arrived.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Basement: </b>The lower level is a cluttered mess </p>
<p>of boxes, crates, and furniture forming a virtual </p>
<p>maze. A prop elevator sits at the stage end </p>
<p>and a large area has been cleared around a </p>
<p>floor drain under the old orchestra pit. There </p>
<p>are  deep  red  stains  around  the  drain—left </p>
<p>over from the slaughterhouse blood sluices. </p>
<p>A  Notice  roll  spots  recent  scrapes  around </p>
<p>the drain cover, indicating it may have been </p>
<p>moved.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Financial Ledger: </b>Any investigator scouring </p>
<p>Linden’s  financial  records  can  make  an </p>
<p>Investigation or Knowledge (Accounting) roll. </p>
<p>Success finds that the man is so far in debt </p>
<p>on  the  project  that  even  if  he  defaults  and </p>
<p>collects the insurance, he will have to declare </p>
<p>bankruptcy.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Missing Workers: </b>None of the crew has heard </p>
<p>from any of the other workers who left the site. </p>
<p>In fact, in many cases, no one ever saw them </p>
<p>leave. A Streetwise roll finds that most of the </p>
<p>missing crewmen had been assigned to work </p>
<p>clearing the basement level. </p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Neighborhood: </b> A  Streetwise  roll  discovers </p>
<p>that most of the former homeless inhabitants </p>
<p>of  the  area  left  not  because  of  the  work  at </p>
<p>the  Orpheum. The  few  who  remain  tell  the </p>
<p>investigators  that  “something  woke  up”  in </p>
<p>the Orpheum and it preys on anyone foolish </p>
<p>enough to be caught alone at night.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Newspaper Reports: </b>An Investigation roll on </p>
<p>recent  newspaper  articles  finds  that  shortly </p>
<p>after  the  first  accident  at  the  Orpheum,  a </p>
<p>homeless man was found dead not far from </p>
<p>the theater. The cause of death was massive </p>
<p>blood loss.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Orpheum Records: </b>The records from the first </p>
<p>Orpheum are intact, buried in the basement. </p>
<p>The original theater turned to displays of the </p>
<p>unusual  or  macabre  toward  the  end  of  its </p>
<p>run in an attempt to keep its doors open. An </p>
<p>Investigation  roll  uncovers  the  last  display </p>
<p>was purchased from “Nightlinger’s Traveling </p>
<p>Expedition of the Extraordinary” and included, </p>
<p>among other things, “one coffin and contents.”</p>
<p>The.Final.Act</p>
<p>The vampire has created a few offspring from </p>
<p>workers and homeless victims during its recent </p>
<p>feedings. The creatures hide in the sewers under </p>
<p>the theater, crawling up through the drain mainly </p>
<p>at night. Rarely, they may snatch a lone worker </p>
<p>from the basement during the day.</p>
<p>If the investigators enter the sewers, the undead </p>
<p>immediately attack. Should they set up watch on </p>
<p>the theater during the night hours to catch vandals </p>
<p>or saboteurs, whether inside or out, allow them </p>
<p>Notice rolls to spot the monsters creeping out to </p>
<p>seek prey. </p>
<p>The young vampires, driven by bloodlust, are </p>
<p>feral and fight to the death. The ancient vampire </p>
<p>tries to flee if it suffers two Wounds, attempting to </p>
<p>escape into the sewers under the theater.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Vampire (WC): </b>Use the stats for the Ancient </p>
<p>Vampire found on page 164<i>.</i></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Vampire Spawn (1, plus 1 per 2 heroes): </b></p>
<p>Use  the  stats  for Young  Vampire  found  on </p>
<p>page 164.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--168</p>
<p>The.Orpheum</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--169</p>
<p>Blood.in.the.Snow</p>
<p>The following is a tale of vikings, ice, and death. </p>
<p>It can take place in a fantasy or historical setting </p>
<p>as the Game Master chooses. Players should be </p>
<p>Viking warriors, scouts, or shamans with mystical </p>
<p>powers.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Setting Rules:</b> Born a Hero, Blood &amp; Guts</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Characters:</b> Viking warriors, scouts, shamans, </p>
<p>or villagers. At least one of the characters should </p>
<p>have Tracking.</p>
<p>The  heroes  are  members  of  a  village  called </p>
<p>Trundheim somewhere in the frigid north. They </p>
<p>are  raiders  and  warriors,  but  this  is  the  winter </p>
<p>season  when  they  spend  the  harsh  days  and </p>
<p>nights  enjoying  their  ill-gotten  gains  with  their </p>
<p>families and friends.</p>
<p>To the south are ice-laden seas. To the east and </p>
<p>west are rival clans. To the north are tall mountains </p>
<p>said to be home to fierce trolls and massive packs </p>
<p>of hungry wolves. It is the trolls that pose the most </p>
<p>recent threat to Trundheim.</p>
<p>Two nights ago trolls descended into the village </p>
<p>and took one of the village’s most beautiful girls—</p>
<p>the Jarl’s daughter, Brynhilde. The warriors are </p>
<p>tasked with venturing out during one of the worst </p>
<p>blizzards the elders can remember to bring her </p>
<p>back—or avenge her death with the heads of the </p>
<p>mysterious trolls.</p>
<p>The.Ice.Trolls</p>
<p>The adventure starts in the small hours of dawn. </p>
<p>Sven Sjurson, who was on guard duty the last </p>
<p>part of the night, wakes the village with a cry. He </p>
<p>is covered in blood and suffers from a nasty blow </p>
<p>to the head. Nearby is the home of Jarl Steinar, </p>
<p>headman of the village. The log wall of the longhall </p>
<p>has been pulled down and the jarl lies dead in a </p>
<p>pool of frozen gore. Sven tells the following tale:</p>
<p><i>Something  terrible  came  through  the </i></p>
<p><i>darkness. I turned to fight but the thing was </i></p>
<p><i>so tall it blocked out the moon! I was about </i></p>
<p><i>to strike when it swung a massive club at my </i></p>
<p><i>head. The next thing I know I was lying in </i></p>
<p><i>the snow here and…Jarl Steinar was dead.</i></p>
<p>The  Jarl is a  bloody mess. Long claw marks </p>
<p>cover his body, and it appears the death blow was </p>
<p>delivered to his throat. A quick search of the rest of </p>
<p>the longhall reveals the Jarl’s daughter, Brynhilde, </p>
<p>is missing—her bed violently overturned and furs </p>
<p>strewn about the floor. If anyone thinks to look, the </p>
<p>Jarl’s few valuables are still present.</p>
<p>In  the  nearby  snow  are  massive  barefoot </p>
<p>tracks—the feet at least a foot and a half long. </p>
<p>Farther out the tracks vanish—a fierce snow is </p>
<p>setting in and covering them quickly.</p>
<p>The clan is without leadership, but if the heroes </p>
<p>don’t  think  of  it  on  their  own,  the  town  elders </p>
<p>strongly encourage them to form a rescue party </p>
<p>and set out immediately. The rest of the warriors </p>
<p>will need to stay in town to prevent further raids </p>
<p>and to protect against opportunistic rival clans to </p>
<p>the east and west.</p>
<p>The tracks are fading fast, but they lead to the </p>
<p>mountainous  north. A Tracking  roll  points  the </p>
<p>rescue party in the right direction. A raise on the </p>
<p>Tracking roll reveals there are three distinct sets </p>
<p>of tracks.</p>
<p>What.Really.Happened</p>
<p>Bjorn Thorkellson is the Jarl of the nearby village </p>
<p>of Aldavig. He desperately wants the favor of the </p>
<p>king, but to do so he must expand his control to </p>
<p>more than a single settlement. Trundheim is small </p>
<p>but rich thanks to particularly successful raids the </p>
<p>last few years. Fighting such successful warriors </p>
<p>would be difficult and likely destroy much of the </p>
<p>village, so Thorkellson came up with a more subtle </p>
<p>plan. He gathered a group of his most veteran </p>
<p>warriors and tasked them with feigning an attack </p>
<p>by a monster on the village, killing Jarl Steinar </p>
<p>in  his  sleep,  and  kidnapping  his  daughter.  His </p>
<p>own  hunting  band  would  then  “chance”  across </p>
<p>the  beasts,  kill  them,  and  return  as  heroes  to </p>
<p>Trundheim with the princess. Thorkellson would </p>
<p>be  the  new  Jarl,  and  with  luck,  a  legend  sung </p>
<p>about by the skalds for ages to come for killing </p>
<p>the terrible trolls.</p>
<p>Thorkellson has an ally in the treacherous Sven </p>
<p>the Sjurson, who has been promised land in the </p>
<p>new fiefdom. Sven and the raiders killed the Jarl in </p>
<p>his sleep and knocked his daughter unconscious </p>
<p>(the Jarl’s wife died long ago). Then they quietly </p>
<p>tore down the walls and bashed Sven over the </p>
<p>head before stealing off into the howling storm.</p>
<p>Following.the.Raiders</p>
<p>The  kidnappers  have  headed  due  north. A </p>
<p>Tracking roll at –4 for the gathering snow leads </p>
<p>the rescuers quickly to their trail. If the roll is failed, </p>
<p>the group must make a Vigor roll to resist the cold </p>
<p>and  try  again.  If  the  party  decides  to  stop  and </p>
<p>recover (mandatory if one of the heroes becomes </p>
<p>Incapacitated),  they  must  build  a  temporary </p>
<p>shelter and bundle up. Every 30 minutes in the </p>
<p>shelter removes one level of Fatigue.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--170</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Pack.Tactics</p>
<p>After about half-a-day’s journey north the group </p>
<p>comes to the foothills. The blizzard picks up and </p>
<p>the  scattered  trees  are  leafless  and  bare. As </p>
<p>the rescuers pick their way through the blasted </p>
<p>landscape they hear sudden barking from behind. </p>
<p>Two  black  wolves  stand  out  against  the  snow </p>
<p>field. Unless the characters specifically state they </p>
<p>are not turning to look at the predators they are </p>
<p>ambushed by the rest of the pack hiding behind </p>
<p>scrub-covered hills to their front.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Wolf Pack (6):</b> See Wolves on page 157.</p>
<p>After the fight, the vikings can skin the wolves </p>
<p>for fur and meat. If they do so, this extra layer of </p>
<p>warmth  and  fresh  food  grants  them  +1  to  their </p>
<p>Vigor  rolls  versus  Fatigue  for  the  rest  of  the </p>
<p>adventure.</p>
<p>As they go about the bloody task, have the group </p>
<p>make Notice rolls. Whoever rolls highest finds a </p>
<p>scrap of red cloth on one of the scraggly trees. It </p>
<p>is the rich cloth of a chief’s daughter—Brynhilde.</p>
<p>Icy.Cliffs</p>
<p>By now all traces of the trolls’ footprints are lost, </p>
<p>but legend says the trolls live in the caves higher </p>
<p>in the mountains. To get to those caves the party </p>
<p>must climb a series of sheer cliffs. </p>
<p>Have the group make three Climbing rolls. The </p>
<p>rolls are made at –2 if the party had to find shelter </p>
<p>after leaving the village as the blizzard has grown </p>
<p>in intensity. </p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Total of 1 or less:</b> The character falls for 2d6 </p>
<p>damage if failed on the first roll, 3d6 on the </p>
<p>second, and 4d6 on the third.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Failure:</b> The character suffers a Fatigue level.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Success:</b> The climber ascends this section of </p>
<p>the mountain.</p>
<p>After each of the three ascents the heroes must </p>
<p>rest. Pick a character at random and draw a card </p>
<p>for an Interlude. Give the player a few minutes to </p>
<p>tell his tale, then move on to the next roll, or the </p>
<p>next scene if it was the third Interlude.</p>
<p>The.Trolls</p>
<p>After the grueling ascent, have everyone make </p>
<p>Notice rolls. The highest roll spots smoke coming </p>
<p>from somewhere in the mountains. With a Survival </p>
<p>roll the rescuers  find  the  cave quickly. If failed, </p>
<p>the  group  must  make  a  Vigor  roll  at  –2  before </p>
<p>stumbling upon the troll’s lair.</p>
<p>The  “trolls”  wait  with  the  captive  Brynhilde </p>
<p>beyond a bend in the cave. They have a warm </p>
<p>fire  and  stocks  of  meat  and  mead. Assuming </p>
<p>the rescuers approach quietly, they overhear the </p>
<p>raiders talking to their victim.</p>
<p><i>A heavy voice says: “You were taken by </i></p>
<p><i>trolls, girl. Say otherwise and we’ll kill you. </i></p>
<p><i>You’ll marry Jarl Thorkellson and keep your </i></p>
<p><i>mouth shut.”</i></p>
<p><i>A girl’s voice answers in angry reply, “My </i></p>
<p><i>father raised no weaklings. I’ll not be bullied </i></p>
<p><i>into betraying my clan.”</i></p>
<p><i>“More’s the pity for you then. Thorkellson </i></p>
<p><i>will have his way with you and slit your throat. </i></p>
<p><i>Then  he’ll  take  your  broken  body  back  to </i></p>
<p><i>Trundheim with the sad tale of how we tried </i></p>
<p><i>to rescue you, but with your last words you </i></p>
<p><i>pledged your love and legacy to Thorkellson.”</i></p>
<p>The trolls laugh heartily and then grow quiet, </p>
<p>feasting on hot broth and mead. It’s the perfect </p>
<p>time for the heroes to strike. Five raiders are in </p>
<p>the cave with their war gear nearby. A Notice roll </p>
<p>also  spots  false  “troll  feet”  made  from  various </p>
<p>hides lying in a pile near the fire.</p>
<p>The group should be able to strike with surprise </p>
<p>against the raiders. Unfortunately, the round after </p>
<p>the fight begins, Jarl Thorkellson and his personal </p>
<p>guard show up to the rendezvous and attack from </p>
<p>behind.</p>
<p>Troll-Raiders.(3)</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts  d4,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d8, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Climbing d6, Fighting d8, Intimidation d6, </p>
<p>Notice d6, Stealth d8, Survival d6, Throwing d6, </p>
<p>Tracking d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b> –; <b>Pace:</b> 6; <b>Parry: </b>7; <b>Toughness:</b> 8 (1)</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> —</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> Brawny</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Leather armor (+1), axe (Str+d6), wooden </p>
<p>shield  (+1  Parry),  2  x  throwing  axes  (Range </p>
<p>3/6/12, Damage Str+d6).</p>
<p>Thorkellson’s.House.Guard.(2.+.1.per.Hero)</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts  d4,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d10, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Climbing d6, Fighting d8, Intimidation d6, </p>
<p>Notice d6, Stealth d8, Survival d6, Throwing d6, </p>
<p>Tracking d6</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--171</p>
<p>Adventures</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b>  –; <b> Pace:</b>  6; </p>
<p><b>Parry: </b>7; <b>Toughness:</b> 8 (1)</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> Loyal</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> Brawny</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b>  Leather  armor  (+1), </p>
<p>axe (Str+d6), wooden shield </p>
<p>(+1  Parry),  2  x  throwing  axes </p>
<p>(Range 3/6/12, Damage Str+d6).</p>
<p>X</p>
<p>.Jarl.Thorkellson</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts </p>
<p>d8,  Spirit  d10,  Strength  d12, </p>
<p>Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Climbing  d6,  Fighting </p>
<p>d10,  Intimidation  d6,  Notice </p>
<p>d6, Survival d6, Throwing d6, </p>
<p>Tracking d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b>  –2; <b> Pace:</b>  4; </p>
<p><b>Parry: </b>6; <b>Toughness:</b> 9 (2)</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b>  Arrogant, </p>
<p>Lame, Mean</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> Improved Sweep</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b>  Chain  armor  (+2), </p>
<p>great  axe  (Str+d10,  –1 </p>
<p>Parry),  2  x  throwing  axes </p>
<p>(Range  3/6/12,  Damage </p>
<p>Str+d6).</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--172</p>
<p>The.Salvage.of.the.USS.Kaine</p>
<p>The <i> USS  Kaine</i>  drifts  in  the  cold  reaches  of </p>
<p>space.  The  crew  of  the  salvage  vessel <i> USS </i></p>
<p><i>Clark </i> discovers  the <i> Kaine</i>  and  ventures  out  to </p>
<p>discover its dark secret.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Setting Rules:</b> Critical Failure, Gritty Damage</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Characters:</b> The  heroes are members  of  a </p>
<p>rescue vessel, the <i>USS Clark</i>. One of them must </p>
<p>be the captain and have Piloting and Knowledge </p>
<p>(Astronavigation) at d8 or higher. All of the crew </p>
<p>members must have Repair at d4 or higher.</p>
<p>The.USS.Kaine</p>
<p>The <i> USS  Kaine</i>  is  a  deep-space  probe </p>
<p>designed by the United States Navy to investigate </p>
<p>anomalies—including  signs  of  alien  life.  It  was </p>
<p>reported  missing  after  a  dangerous  mission  to </p>
<p>investigate Black Hole C1263. The ship was to </p>
<p>approach within scanning distance of the black </p>
<p>hole and take detailed readings on some unusual </p>
<p>energy signals detected there.</p>
<p>Unfortunately, the <i>Kaine</i> got too close. It wasn’t </p>
<p>sucked  in—that  would  have  destroyed  it—but </p>
<p>gravitational distortions warped the crew’s mind, </p>
<p>reducing them to blood-crazed lunatics.</p>
<p>The.USS.Clark</p>
<p>The <i>Clark’s</i> computer picked up the <i>Kaine’s</i> faint </p>
<p>distress signal eight hours ago and the captain </p>
<p>set course immediately. The vessel is still located </p>
<p>near  Black  Hole  C1263,  but  not  dangerously </p>
<p>so. The <i>Clark</i> will arrive within 10 minutes—just </p>
<p>enough  time  to  allow  the  group  to  make  any </p>
<p>preparations they want.</p>
<p>Their vessel is equipped with tools of all sorts, </p>
<p>deep space suits with 10 minutes of continuous </p>
<p>propulsion  and  four  hours  of  oxygen,  and  any </p>
<p>other necessities they might think of. The crew </p>
<p>does  not  have  weapons,  but  the  captain  has </p>
<p>a  pistol  and  a  box  of  20  ceramic  bullets  in  his </p>
<p>cabin  if  he  wants  it  (Range  24/48/96,  Damage </p>
<p>2d6-2, Shots 7, will not puncture most inorganic </p>
<p>materials—such as the ship’s hull!)</p>
<p>The thick suits add +1 Toughness due to their </p>
<p>thick  material. A  hero  who  suffers  a  wound  or </p>
<p>more from a cutting or piercing attack must repair </p>
<p>the suit before heading out of life support or he </p>
<p>decompresses and dies in 2d6 rounds.</p>
<p>The.Approach</p>
<p>The <i>USS Kaine</i> is largely intact, though some of </p>
<p>the extending structures have all warped strangely </p>
<p>toward the bow (an effect of the black hole). There </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--173</p>
<p>Adventures</p>
<p>is  no  obvious  damage  other  than  the  warped </p>
<p>superstructure. Scans of the ship show there is </p>
<p>still residual power and life support functioning.</p>
<p>Docking  with  the <i> Kaine</i>  requires  a  standard </p>
<p>Piloting roll. A critical failure means the airlock is </p>
<p>jammed and the salvagers have to go EV (extra-</p>
<p>vehicular—meaning they move around outside the </p>
<p>vessels) to enter from the airlock on the opposite </p>
<p>side. This uses two minutes of propulsion for each </p>
<p>spacesuit.</p>
<p>Life.Support.&amp;.Gravity</p>
<p>Life  support  is  functioning,  but  the  artificial </p>
<p>gravity generator was overloaded in the surge. </p>
<p>The scavengers wear electromagnetic boots that </p>
<p>allow  them  to  walk  normally  (including  on  the </p>
<p>walls and ceilings!), but cuts their Pace by half </p>
<p>and inflicts a –2 penalty to all physical actions.</p>
<p>Should a character turn off the electromagnets </p>
<p>in  his  boots,  he  drifts  in  whatever  direction  he </p>
<p>moved last. Initial Pace while drifting is equal to </p>
<p>whatever it was last round, but a scavenger may </p>
<p>increase or decrease his Pace by 1 or 2 per round </p>
<p>by using their suit’s microthrusters.</p>
<p>Maneuvering  at  a  Pace  of  6  or  less  requires </p>
<p>no roll. At Pace 7 or higher, the hero must make </p>
<p>an Agility roll to turn sharp corners, get through </p>
<p>hatchways, make a melee attack, etc. If failed at </p>
<p>a Pace of less than 10, the character suffers a </p>
<p>Fatigue level from Bumps and Bruises. At a Pace </p>
<p>of 11 or higher, he suffers 1d6 damage for every </p>
<p>5” of Pace (round normally).</p>
<p>The  crew  of  the <i> Kaine</i>  does  not  suffer  any </p>
<p>penalties due to the absence of gravity. They’re </p>
<p>quite  mad  and  have  adjusted  by  now,  so  they </p>
<p>move effortlessly through the ship, scampering </p>
<p>along  the  walls  and  ceilings  like  some  sort  of </p>
<p>insectoids.</p>
<p>Should the scavengers succeed in repairing the </p>
<p><i>Kaine’s </i>artificial gravity, however, the situation is </p>
<p>reversed. and the deranged crew suffers a –2 to </p>
<p>all their physical actions!</p>
<p>Map.of.the.Kaine</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Bridge:</b> The <i>Kaine’s</i> navigational equipment </p>
<p>needs  extensive  repairs  before  she  can  be </p>
<p>piloted. Each Repair attempt takes an entire day </p>
<p>and is made at –2 (in addition to any penalties </p>
<p>for zero-g). </p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Captain’s Cabin:</b> A once neatly maintained </p>
<p>cabin, it is now a cluttered mess as a variety of </p>
<p>old  maritime  antiques  and  curios  float  through </p>
<p>the room.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Crew Quarters:</b> Each cabin is a reflection of </p>
<p>the former occupant. Some are orderly and clean </p>
<p>while others are in varying degrees of disarray. </p>
<p>Nothing of note is to be found in any of the rooms.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Engineering:</b> The engineering section takes </p>
<p>up two levels, with a balcony overlooking much </p>
<p>of  the  main  deck  portion.  The  ship’s  drive  is </p>
<p>functional,  but  the  artificial  gravity  generator  is </p>
<p>temporarily overloaded. Ten minutes labor and a </p>
<p>Repair roll (–2) can bring it back online.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Galley:</b>  Lightweight  tables  and  chairs  float </p>
<p>throughout  the  room,  along  with  the  body </p>
<p>of  another  of  the <i> Kaine’s</i>  crew. A  Healing  or </p>
<p>Knowledge  (Medicine)  roll  easily  identifies  the </p>
<p>cause of death as multiple stab wounds. If the </p>
<p>team searches the galley, a Notice roll uncovers </p>
<p>a butcher knife (Str+d4).</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Laboratories:</b>  The <i> Kaine</i>  contained  three </p>
<p>state-of-the-art  laboratories.  With  a  successful </p>
<p>Notice  roll,  the  team  members  can  find  one </p>
<p>small improvised weapon in each lab if they are </p>
<p>specifically looking for them.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Ship’s Stores:</b> A variety of standard equipment </p>
<p>is kept in these rooms, including spare space suits </p>
<p>and repair gear, but little is of immediate use. A </p>
<p>Notice  roll  spots  a  pneumatic  bolt  gun  (Range </p>
<p>6/12/24, Damage 2d6, Shots 6) which can be fired </p>
<p>using Shooting or Repair.</p>
<p>Something’s.Amiss</p>
<p>Regardless  of  how  the  salvagers  proceed </p>
<p>in  investigating  the <i> Kaine, </i> they  encounter  a </p>
<p>corpse in the third compartment they enter after </p>
<p>boarding the ship. The body floats, limbs askew, </p>
<p>twirling slowly in the absence of gravity. A mist of </p>
<p>blood globules seems to almost orbit around it. A </p>
<p>successful Healing or Knowledge (Medicine) roll </p>
<p>determines the cause of death to be blood loss </p>
<p>from numerous cuts, tears, and even bites. </p>
<p>Ambush</p>
<p>Immediately after leaving the room where they </p>
<p>discover the body, the team is attacked by a band </p>
<p>of three of the former crew of the <i>Kaine.</i> If possible, </p>
<p>the lunatics attack in a passageway, coming at the </p>
<p>party from both sides as they scuttle along the </p>
<p>walls and ceilings. They have no weapons other </p>
<p>than their teeth, hands, and feet.</p>
<p>Marooned!</p>
<p>Moments after the ambush begins, four other </p>
<p>members  of  the <i> Kaine’s</i>  crew  rush  the  airlock </p>
<p>to  the <i> Clark. </i> Any  characters  at  the  airlock  are </p>
<p>attacked. If there is no one there, the madmen </p>
<p>rush  into  the  airlock  and  manually  release  the </p>
<p>docking tube. The airlock protects the integrity of </p>
<p>both vessels’ atmosphere, but the decompression </p>
<p>of the tube blows the vessels apart.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--174</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>The.Fires.of.Ascalon</p>
<p>The ravaging hordes are coming and a party </p>
<p>of  elven  scouts  must  deny  them  sustenance. </p>
<p>The  town  of Ascalon  lies  in  the  way  and  must </p>
<p>be burned to the ground—if the villagers can be </p>
<p>convinced.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Setting Rules:</b> None.</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Characters:</b>  The  heroes  are  all  elves  or </p>
<p>friends of the elves fighting in a terrible war against </p>
<p>a savage foe.</p>
<p>The premise of this Savage Tale is that there is </p>
<p>a massive war in a typical fantasy world of elves, </p>
<p>dwarves, men, and orcs. The party is assumed </p>
<p>to be made exclusively of elves, who in this world </p>
<p>are viewed as aloof at best or outsiders at worst </p>
<p>by human society.</p>
<p>The  adventure  can  be  altered  to  fit  other </p>
<p>settings—including  those  without  elves  and </p>
<p>humans. The important circumstance is that the </p>
<p>player character’s party is made up primarily of a </p>
<p>race or nationality the villagers of Ascalon won’t </p>
<p>trust easily.</p>
<p>The  orcs  may  be  any  force  of  chaos  and </p>
<p>destruction—the  only  thing  that  matters  is  that </p>
<p>allowing the village’s precious resources to fall into </p>
<p>the horde’s hands would cause devastation for the </p>
<p>locals and hardship for the rest of the kingdom.</p>
<p>The.Mission</p>
<p>The heroes are scouts of the elves tasked with </p>
<p>an important mission. While the main force harries </p>
<p>the  orcish  horde,  the  adventurers  are  sent  to </p>
<p>burn the village of Ascalon. This was a decision </p>
<p>reached by the allied war council, which includes </p>
<p>humans, but the elves were closest and so were </p>
<p>appointed with the destruction of the village.</p>
<p>Read  or  paraphrase  the  following  from  their </p>
<p>commander when you’re ready to begin:</p>
<p><i>The horde approaches more rapidly than </i></p>
<p><i>anyone had believed. But all armies march </i></p>
<p><i>on their stomachs. I will lead our main force </i></p>
<p><i>in a bitter defense against the orcs at Gallows </i></p>
<p><i>Woods. Your mission will be to race to the </i></p>
<p><i>human village of Ascalon and...I’m afraid...</i></p>
<p><i>burn it to the ground. </i></p>
<p><i>Ascalon has rich farmlands and abundant </i></p>
<p><i>crops that will feed the orcs and prolong their </i></p>
<p><i>rampage for months. Even the wood from the </i></p>
<p><i>houses and inns must be destroyed lest it </i></p>
<p><i>be turned into weapons or siege equipment.</i></p>
<p><i>The horde has approached too quickly. The </i></p>
<p><i>villagers have not been told of this decision </i></p>
<p><i>by our allied war council and will likely have </i></p>
<p><i>to  be  forcibly  removed.  Convince  them  to </i></p>
<p><i>leave and do not harm them—but Ascalon </i></p>
<p><i>must burn. You leave immediately.</i></p>
<p>Unless one of the team has remained on the </p>
<p><i>Clark,</i> the only way the salvagers can get back </p>
<p>to their vessel is through an extended EVA. This </p>
<p>requires  a  successful Agility  or  Smarts  roll  to </p>
<p>navigate  the  gap.  On  a  failure,  the  spacefarer </p>
<p>expends two minutes of propulsion and requires </p>
<p>another attempt. On a critical failure, it uses five </p>
<p>minutes. Once a hero is out of fuel, he drifts into </p>
<p>the void unless rescued.</p>
<p>Last.Stand</p>
<p>The <i>Kaine’s</i> captain, Bill Weir, and the remaining </p>
<p>five  of  his  crew  have  laired  in  the  engineering </p>
<p>section. One floats limply through the main deck </p>
<p>pretending to be dead while the others hide in </p>
<p>the shadows of the balcony. If a team member </p>
<p>approaches the “dead” man, he suddenly comes </p>
<p>to life and attacks. The hapless victim must make </p>
<p>a Fear check unless she specifically states she is </p>
<p>expecting a trick. Regardless, the salvagers must </p>
<p>check for surprise.</p>
<p>The  captain  and  crew  attack  the  next  round, </p>
<p>diving from above. Treat this as a Wild Attack (see </p>
<p>page 87). The lunatics fight to the death.</p>
<p>Two of the crewmen on the balcony are armed </p>
<p>with butcher knives from the galley (Str+d4). Use </p>
<p>the <i>Kaine</i>  crewman stats for  Captain  Weir, but </p>
<p>treat him as a Wild Card. He is also armed with a </p>
<p>bolt gun, as above.</p>
<p>Kaine.Crewman</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d8,  Smarts  d4,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d8, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Stealth d8, Throwing d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b> +0</p>
<p><b>Pace:</b> 6; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness: </b>5</p>
<p><b>Edges &amp; Hindrances:</b> Frenzy</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities:</b> </p>
<p>• </p>
<p>Bite/Fist/Kick: Str. (Treat as armed.)</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--175</p>
<p>Adventures</p>
<p>The heroes are given torches covered in pitch </p>
<p>and  two  flasks  of  quick-burning  oil  to  get  the </p>
<p>largest  buildings  burning  as  fast  as  possible. </p>
<p>Ascalon is an hour’s run away and no horses can </p>
<p>be spared, so they must get moving immediately.</p>
<p>The  run  is  long  and  tiring.  Have  each  scout </p>
<p>make a Vigor roll or suffer Fatigue before they </p>
<p>reach Ascalon. Those with the Fleet-Footed Edge </p>
<p>add +2. This Fatigue can be recovered after 30 </p>
<p>minutes  of  rest—precious  time  the  adventures </p>
<p>won’t likely have.</p>
<p>Foraging.Party</p>
<p>The road to Ascalon from the elven camp winds </p>
<p>through green, scrub-covered foothills. Halfway </p>
<p>along the trek, have the group make Notice rolls. </p>
<p>Those  who  make  it  hear  sounds  of  fighting  on </p>
<p>the path ahead and can gain surprise on the first </p>
<p>round if they so choose.</p>
<p>The scene they see before them is an overturned </p>
<p>cart laden with fruits, vegetables, and flour. Two </p>
<p>horses  struggle  to  free  themselves  from  the </p>
<p>twisted  yokes,  and  three  farmers  are  doing </p>
<p>their  best  to  fend  off  three  circling  orcs  riding </p>
<p>mangy boars. The orcs are foraging for the main </p>
<p>horde and chased the cart for several hundred </p>
<p>yards  before  the  driver  took  a  sharp  turn  and </p>
<p>unfortunately overturned the wagon.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Orcs  (3):</b>  The  orcs  ride  boars.  Use  the </p>
<p>statistics  at  the  end  of  this  adventure. The </p>
<p>raiders have Riding at d6.</p>
<p>Assuming the orcs are slain or driven off, the </p>
<p>humans  thank  their  rescuers  and  say  that  the </p>
<p>supplies were a gift to the war council from the </p>
<p>town. The leader of this small group is Nathan </p>
<p>Crenshaw,  a  strong,  soft-spoken  man  of  about </p>
<p>50. If the elves tell Crenshaw their plan, he and </p>
<p>his  boys  begin  to  right  the  wagon  (it  takes  10 </p>
<p>minutes). Then he heads back to Ascalon to warn </p>
<p>the elders and take part in any debate. If the elves </p>
<p>don’t mention their task, he heads on to the allied </p>
<p>war camp none the wiser.</p>
<p>The.Elders</p>
<p>In Ascalon, adults seem alarmed as they spy the </p>
<p>mysterious elves brazenly enter their town, while </p>
<p>the children gather in delight at their strange and </p>
<p>wondrous visitors. If the elves look for someone of </p>
<p>authority, they are pointed to Elder Elias Stosham, </p>
<p>the leader of this village.</p>
<p>Convincing Stosham of the elves’ mission is an </p>
<p>extremely difficult task. To do so, use the Social </p>
<p>Conflict system on page 110. The outsiders roll </p>
<p>at –4 unless Crenshaw accompanied them back </p>
<p>from  the  ambush.  If  so,  his  testimony  that  the </p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--176</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>elves  saved  him  and  his  companions  reduces </p>
<p>the penalty to –2.</p>
<p>If the heroes tie or lose the conflict, the villagers </p>
<p>turn  hostile  and  attack  unless  the  elves  seem </p>
<p>willing to leave.</p>
<p>If the elves win the debate by 1 or 2 successes, </p>
<p>Stosham orders the villagers to comply with the </p>
<p>elves’ “demands.” The villagers slowly gather their </p>
<p>loved ones and belongings and fade off into the </p>
<p>countryside.</p>
<p>If  the  heroes  succeed  by  three  successes </p>
<p>or  more,  the  villagers  gather  their  belongings </p>
<p>and  send  the  women,  children,  and  elderly  to </p>
<p>destinations further behind the lines. The men, </p>
<p>however, join the allied army, hoping to defeat the </p>
<p>orcs before any more villages must be sacrificed.</p>
<p>Village.Fighting.Men.(15)</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts  d4,  Spirit  d6, </p>
<p>Strength d6, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d4, Notice d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma: —; Pace:</b> 6; <b>Parry:</b> 4; <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Pitchforks (Str+d4, add Parry +1) or scythes </p>
<p>(Str+d6).</p>
<p>Fire,.Fire,.Burning.Bright</p>
<p>Whether they are defeated or reluctantly agree </p>
<p>to the plan, the villagers disperse, and no matter </p>
<p>how convincing the elves were, they will not help </p>
<p>burn their town. The moment the heroes begin to </p>
<p>set the fires themselves, a raiding party of orcs </p>
<p>arrives.</p>
<p>There  are  four  points  that  must  be  lit  to </p>
<p>effectively raze the town: the Rampant Lion Inn, </p>
<p>the granary silo, the bridge, and the livery. The </p>
<p>livery still has 2d6 horses and mules in it, so the </p>
<p>heroes will need to decide if they want to take </p>
<p>the time to evacuate them first. A loud yell and </p>
<p>successful Intimidation roll gets 1d4 animals per </p>
<p>round, a raise doubles that. Anyone with Animal </p>
<p>Companion or Beast Bond adds +2 to the roll. </p>
<p>The <i>beast friend</i> power can also be used on the </p>
<p>“lead” horse in the livery. All of the other animals </p>
<p>follow the round thereafter.</p>
<p>Setting  fire  to  these  four  areas  ensures  the </p>
<p>town and its supplies are denied to the rampaging </p>
<p>greenskins. A hero can set one of the objectives </p>
<p>on fire as long as he starts his turn in contact with </p>
<p>it, has a lit torch and oil flask, isn’t Shaken, and </p>
<p>makes a successful Smarts roll. A failed Smarts </p>
<p>roll means a small flame is started but isn’t enough </p>
<p>to set the building truly ablaze.</p>
<p>If any of these conditions aren’t met, the arsonist </p>
<p>must try again next round.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Orc Chieftain:</b> See the statistics on page 162, </p>
<p>and add Riding d8.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Orc Raiders:</b> There are 20 orcs riding giant </p>
<p>boars (see below), though they roam in groups </p>
<p>of five so the Game Master should space them </p>
<p>out accordingly so as not to overwhelm the </p>
<p>heroes. Orc raiders have Riding d6 in addition </p>
<p>to their usual skills.</p>
<p>War.Boar</p>
<p>These  massive  boars  serve  as  the  orcish </p>
<p>horde’s mounts. They’re 700 pounds of muscle, </p>
<p>tusk, stench, and attitude. Only orcs are typically </p>
<p>tough enough to breed and ride them.</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d4, Smarts d4 (A), Spirit d6, </p>
<p>Strength d10, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Fighting d8, Intimidation d8, Notice d8</p>
<p><b>Pace: </b>10; <b>Parry:</b> 6; <b>Toughness:</b> 9</p>
<p><b>Special Abilities</b></p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Tusk Slash:</b> Str+d6</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Gore:</b> If a boar can charge at least 6” before </p>
<p>attacking, it adds +4 to its damage total that </p>
<p>round. It cannot slash and gore in the same </p>
<p>action.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Fleet-Footed:</b> War boars roll d10s instead of </p>
<p>d6s when running.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Size:</b> +2. War boars weigh 700 pounds.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--177</p>
<p>Crime.City:.The.Chase</p>
<p>Crime City was first introduced in the free One </p>
<p>Sheet <i>The Moscow Connection,</i> available on our </p>
<p>website at www.peginc.com. This adventure takes </p>
<p>place immediately afterward, so we recommend </p>
<p>you download and run that adventure first, but it’s </p>
<p>certainly not necessary.</p>
<p>Our action begins moments after a small group </p>
<p>of Russian  mafia members  stop a terrorist cell </p>
<p>from  bringing in  a mysterious cargo. Now they </p>
<p>must escape with it!</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Setting Rules:</b> Blood &amp; Guts, Critical Failures, </p>
<p>Gritty Damage, Joker’s Wild, Skill Specialization</p>
<p> </p>
<p>►</p>
<p><b>Characters:</b> The  player  characters  are  all </p>
<p>criminals belonging to—or in the employ of—the </p>
<p>Russian  Mafia. The  default  characters  can  be </p>
<p>found on the opposite page.</p>
<p>In.Media.Res</p>
<p>At  the  end  of <i> The  Moscow  Connection,</i>  the </p>
<p>group stopped Mahmoud Abbas and a cell of the </p>
<p>Red Hand, and took possession of a mysterious </p>
<p>cargo loaded in the back of a large panel truck. </p>
<p>What’s the cargo? That’s up to you, the Game </p>
<p>Master,  but  it  must  be  big  enough  to  require </p>
<p>moving with the panel truck. The cargo might be </p>
<p>a nuclear bomb, or a dirty bomb, or something </p>
<p>far more bizarre—such as debris from the 1908 </p>
<p>Tunguska  Blast,  or  an  artifact  from  Chernobyl </p>
<p>(since it came in on a ship called the <i>Chernobyl </i></p>
<p><i>Revenge)</i>.  Or  maybe  it’s  a  strange  device  the </p>
<p>gangsters don’t even understand.</p>
<p>Regardless  of  the  nature  of  the  cargo,  the </p>
<p>Russians need to get it out of the area to one of </p>
<p>their own warehouses fast. Reinforcements of the </p>
<p>Red Hand are already on their way and a chase </p>
<p>through the streets of New York City are on.</p>
<p>Choose.Your.Poison</p>
<p>Start the action as one of the Russians (Ivan if </p>
<p>you’re using the pregenerated characters as he </p>
<p>speaks Farsi) hear reinforcements state they’re </p>
<p>“almost there” on one of the dead terrorists’ radios.</p>
<p>Then  give  the  players  exactly  one  minute  to </p>
<p>discuss  which  vehicles  they  want  to  take,  and </p>
<p>who’s driving or riding in each. They have to take </p>
<p>the truck since it holds the cargo, and Mahmoud </p>
<p>Abbas’ motorcycle still idles around the corner. </p>
<p>Alexy also has a black 2005 Ford Tahoe nearby </p>
<p>with armored plates in the doors as well.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Motorcycle (2009 Kawasaki Ninja):</b> Acc/TS </p>
<p>20/40, Toughness 8(2), Crew 1.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>SUV  (2005  Ford  Tahoe):</b> Acc/TS  15/35, </p>
<p>Toughness 17(7) on sides, or 14(3) to front and </p>
<p>back, Crew 1+7, Airbags. Note that the Tahoe </p>
<p>is slightly slower and tougher than normal due </p>
<p>to the armor-plated side panels.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Panel Truck:</b> Acc/TS 5/25, Toughness 14(1), </p>
<p>Crew 1.</p>
<p>The.Chase.Begins</p>
<p>This  entire  adventure  is  a  Chase.  Tell  the </p>
<p>group  that  their  goal  is  to  get  the  cargo  away </p>
<p>from the Red Hand, and there’s no telling how </p>
<p>many  reinforcements  are  swarming  in.  Even  if </p>
<p>they defeat the first wave, more may come. If the </p>
<p>Russians are defeated, the mysterious cargo will </p>
<p>fall right back into their enemies’ hands.</p>
<p>This is an Extended Chase of 10 rounds. See </p>
<p>page  94  for  details  on  running  Chases.  The </p>
<p>heroes’  goal  is  to  escape  with  the  panel  truck </p>
<p>and its cargo intact. If the truck and the heroes </p>
<p>are still moving after 10 rounds, they lose their </p>
<p>pursuers and escape. If the truck is stopped, see </p>
<p>“Last Stand,” below.</p>
<p>The enemy is composed of fanatical members </p>
<p>of  the  Red  Hand,  riding  in  two  cars  and  six </p>
<p>motorcycles.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>6 x Motorcycle (variety of older models):</b> </p>
<p>Acc/TS 15/35, Toughness 8(2), Crew 1 each.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>2 x Mid-Size Cars:</b> Acc/TS 20/40, Toughness </p>
<p>11(3), Crew 1+3 each.</p>
<p>The  motorcycles  have  one  driver  each. The </p>
<p>cars  have  a  driver,  who  does  not  attack,  and </p>
<p>three  passengers,  two  of  which  can  attack  on </p>
<p>any given action.</p>
<p>Remember  that  when  the  terrorists  have </p>
<p>Advantage,  no  more  than  a  third  of  them  can </p>
<p>attack a particular target at once as the various </p>
<p>vehicles weave in and out of traffic.</p>
<p>Complications</p>
<p>The inevitable Complications represent traffic, </p>
<p>construction  work,  or  blind  alleys.  In  addition, </p>
<p>if a red Ace is drawn and used by either of the </p>
<p>groups, it means the police have been drawn to </p>
<p>the pursuit. There’s a single police cruiser after </p>
<p>the first round the Ace is used. After that, roll a </p>
<p>d6 at the beginning of each new round. On a 4+, </p>
<p>another police cruiser shows up.</p>
<p>•	</p>
<p><b>Police  Cruiser:</b> Acc/TS  20/45, Toughness </p>
<p>12(3), Crew 2. Use Soldiers for the policemen </p>
<p>(page  93).  They’re  equipped  with  pump-</p>
<p>action shotguns and 9mm pistols. Only one </p>
<p>policeman per cruiser can attack each round, </p>
<p>but he only shoots at Medium Range or better </p>
<p>for fear of wild shots hitting civilians.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--178</p>
<p>Savage.Worlds</p>
<p>Last.Stand</p>
<p>If  the  Russians  stop  for  any  reason,  the </p>
<p>remaining members of the Red Hand dismount </p>
<p>and fight on through the next two rounds. At the </p>
<p>start of the third, another wave (two more cars </p>
<p>and six more bikes) show up and attack as well. </p>
<p>Deal this new wave in as a separate group. The </p>
<p>cars might try to ram the Tahoe, while those on </p>
<p>motorcycles might circle and strafe in hopes that </p>
<p>their fast movement will keep them from getting </p>
<p>shot. After three more rounds have passed, a truck </p>
<p>with a dozen more terrorists arrive.</p>
<p>Pregenerated.Characters</p>
<p>Below are the five characters assumed to be used for “The Chase,” as well as <i>The Moscow Connection</i> </p>
<p>you can find online at www.peginc.com. If you decide to have the players create their own characters, </p>
<p>these can serve as guides for the types of anti-heroes they might make.</p>
<p>Alexy.“The.Shark”.Petrovich</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts d8, Spirit d6, Strength d6, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Driving  d8,  Fighting  d8,  Healing  d4,  Intimidation  d6,  Knowledge </p>
<p>(English) d6, Notice d8, Persuasion d6, Shooting d8, Stealth d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b> 0, <b>Pace:</b> 6, <b>Parry: </b>6, <b>Toughness:</b> 6</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> Loyal (to family and friends), Outsider (Russian), Wanted (Major, </p>
<p>Alexy is being watched by the FBI—and maybe certain Russian factions as </p>
<p>well, but that’s a tale for another day).</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> Noble (the Petrovich Crime Family)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> 9mm Glock Pistol. In Alexy’s Tahoe is also a pump-action shotgun, a </p>
<p>very good first aid kit (+2 to Healing, 4 uses), a gallon of water, five gallons of </p>
<p>gas, and a couple of DVDs he hasn’t returned to the video store yet (Disney </p>
<p>movies, believe it or not).</p>
<p><b>Background: </b>As crime bosses go, Alexy isn’t so bad. He got his nickname because he supposedly fed an </p>
<p>informant to the sharks down in Queens—a little at a time. It’s not true, but Alexy lets everyone believe it is. </p>
<p>He often says something like “Nah. They call me that because I am such a shark with the ladies.” Alexy is </p>
<p>extremely clever, however, and very thorough. This incident with his cousin Gennedy is a rare exception.</p>
<p>Ivan.“Soldier.Boy”.Petrovich</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts d6, Spirit d8, Strength d6, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Driving  d6,  Fighting  d8,  Intimidation  d8,  Knowledge  (English)  d6, </p>
<p>Notice d6, Shooting d8, Stealth d6, Taunt d6, Tracking d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b> -2, Pace: 4, <b>Parry: </b>6, <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> Lame, Loyal (to family and friends), Outsider (Russian)</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> Rock and Roll, Strong Willed</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> MP5 Submachine gun, 2 extra clips.</p>
<p><b>Background: </b>Ivan Petrovich idolizes his older brother, and strives to show </p>
<p>him how strong and independent he is. He joined the US Army after 9/11 and </p>
<p>later spent two tours in Iraq before getting hit with an IED that left him with a </p>
<p>permanent limp. He’s scrappy, tough, and very skilled, but his stint with real </p>
<p>soldiers occasionally makes him doubt his family’s activities.</p>
<p>If the Russians can’t drive away at this point </p>
<p>(which renews the Extended Chase), they’d best </p>
<p>abandon their cargo and duck down an alley. The </p>
<p>Red Hand won’t pursue—they came in force to </p>
<p>escort  their  package. The  group  might  want  to </p>
<p>figure out how they want to get it back before the </p>
<p>terrorists put the device—whatever it is—to use.</p>
<p>Red.Hand.Terrorist</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility  d6,  Smarts  d8,  Spirit  d8, </p>
<p>Strength d6, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b>  Driving  d6,  Fighting  d8,  Knowledge </p>
<p>(English) d6, Notice d8, Shooting d8, Stealth d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b> –2, <b>Pace: </b>6, <b>Parry: </b>6, <b>Toughness:</b> 7</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> Mean, Loyal (to Red Hand)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> AK47, large knife.</p>
<h1 style="page-break-before:always; "></h1>
<p>--Page--179</p>
<p>Adventures</p>
<p>Irina.“The.Skirt”.Gregorovna</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Attributes:</b> Agility d8, Smarts d6, Spirit d8, Strength d6, Vigor d6</p>
<p><b>Skills:</b> Driving d4, Fighting d6, Knowledge (English) d6, Notice d6, Persuasion </p>
<p>d8, Shooting d8, Stealth d8, Streetwise d6</p>
<p><b>Charisma:</b> +2, <b>Pace:</b> 6, <b>Parry: </b>5, <b>Toughness:</b> 5</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> Loyal (to family and friends), Outsider (Russian), Vengeful</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> Combat Reflexes, Very Attractive</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> 9mm Pistol, 2 extra clips, switchblade.</p>
<p><b>Background: </b> Alexy’s  main  girl  is  Irina.  Irina  reflects  the  new  era  in  the </p>
<p>family—one which is very slowly starting to embrace women as well. She’s </p>
<p>gorgeous and knows it, and frequently uses her charms to distract or spy </p>
<p>on Alexy’s rivals.</p>
<p>Piotr.“The.Bull”.Fydorovich</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Attributes: </b>Agility d6, Smarts d4, Spirit d6, Strength d10, Vigor d10</p>
<p><b>Skills: </b>Driving d6, Fighting d10, Intimidation d6, Knowledge (English) d4, </p>
<p>Notice d4, Shooting d4, Stealth d4, Throwing d4</p>
<p><b>Charisma: </b>-2, Pace:<b> </b>6,<b> Parry: </b>7,<b> Toughness: </b>8</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> Loyal (to family and friends), Outsider (Russian), Clueless</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> Brawny, Frenzy, Sweep, Trademark Weapon (Louisville Slugger)</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Louisville Slugger (Str+d6), chewing gum, hair spray and comb.</p>
<p><b>Background: </b>“The Bull” grew up with Alexy, but spent most of his time in </p>
<p>the gym or playing sports. He’s a massive, mountain of a man, and he likes </p>
<p>to prove it by foregoing firearms and blades—though he’s not unskilled in </p>
<p>their use. His trademark weapon is a Louisville slugger he loves to kiss just </p>
<p>before going to work.</p>
<p>Johnny.“Remora”.Mancebo</p>
<p><b>Rank: </b>Seasoned</p>
<p><b>Attributes: </b>Agility d10, Smarts d4, Spirit d6, Strength d6, Vigor d8</p>
<p><b>Skills: </b>Climbing d6, Fighting d10, Knowledge (Russian) d4, Lockpicking d8, </p>
<p>Notice d6, Shooting d4, Stealth d8</p>
<p><b>Charisma: </b>-2, Pace:<b> </b>6,<b> Parry: </b>7<b>, Toughness: </b>5</p>
<p><b>Hindrances:</b> Loyal (to family and friends), Outsider (non-Russian in Russian </p>
<p>gang), Small</p>
<p><b>Edges:</b> First Strike, Quick, Quick Draw, Thief</p>
<p><b>Gear:</b> Lockpicks, switchblade.</p>
<p><b>Background: </b>Johnny isn’t Russian, but he grew up around them and speaks </p>
<p>the language reasonably well. He’s a sly little man, and frequently people </p>
<p>don’t even realize he’s around until he knifes some poor schmuck in the back. </p>
<p>His nickname comes from the way he follows Alexy around (“the shark”).</p>
<p>Look.for.the.prequel.to.this.adventure,.The.Moscow.</p>

<p>Collected.Charts.&amp;.Tables</p>

<p>Stealth.Modifiers</p>
<p> </p>

<p>Reaction.Table</p>
<p><b>  2d6 </b></p>
<p><b>Initial Reaction</b></p>
<p><b> </b></p>
<p><b>2 </b></p>
<p><b>Hostile:</b> The target is openly hostile and </p>
<p>does his best to stand in the hero’s way. </p>
<p>He won’t help without an overwhelming </p>
<p>reward or payment of some kind.</p>
<p><b> </b></p>
<p><b>3-4 </b></p>
<p><b>Uncooperative:</b> The  target  isn’t  willing </p>
<p>to  help  unless  there’s  a  significant </p>
<p>advantage to himself.</p>
<p><b> </b></p>
<p><b>5-9 </b></p>
<p><b>Neutral:</b>  The  target  has  no  particular </p>
<p>attitude  and  will  help  for  little  reward </p>
<p>if the task at hand is very easy. If the </p>
<p>task is difficult, he’ll require substantial </p>
<p>payment of some kind.</p>
<p><b> 10-11 </b></p>
<p><b>Friendly:</b> The target will go out of his way </p>
<p>for the hero. He’ll likely do easy tasks </p>
<p>for free (or very little), and is willing to </p>
<p>do more dangerous tasks for fair pay or </p>
<p>other favors.</p>
<p><b> </b></p>
<p><b>12 </b></p>
<p><b>Helpful:</b> The target is anxious to help the </p>
<p>hero, and will probably do so for little or </p>
<p>no pay depending on the nature of the </p>
<p>task.</p>
